Mind may comprehend the utmost of Creature-^ion; or if we examine the Creature
in its ^^^^^ive Excellency, especially to Man, we shall find that it cannot
perfect our Nature, neither in the Knowledge, Enjoyment, or Improvement of it;
nor is it capable of completing our Happiness; because it is not
proportionable to us, neither to our Nature, nor to our Wants, nor to our
Desires, nor to our Duration; nor do we truly and fully enjoy the Creature, but
hold it only at the Pleasure of another, to whom it originally belongs, and
in whose Right it remains. I have also,

II. Showed you, That the Perfection of the Creature is finite in its Duration.
For the Creation it self will anon come to an End, and its Excellency flee
away; and we ourselves shall quickly come to the End of our Continuance in this
World. Having thus proved this Doctrine, I told you it was improvable to our
Instruction, Correction, and Exhortation; and under the first of these I have
inferred, what Reason we have to mourn over our Apostasy from GOD, as the grand
Cause of very much of the Imperfection of the Creature: And now I proceed to
improve this Doctrine to our further Instruction.

Wherefore,

2. Hence we may learn, that we ought not to be chiefly concerned about the
Things of this World. If we may see an End of all Perfection, as to the
Creature; if it will neither perfect our Nature, nor make us truly happy, nor
abide with us; then certainly the Things of this World have not a Sufficiency
of Worth, and Value in them, to demand all our Expense, and Labor, nor ought
they to have the chief of our Thought, and Care, employed about them. It is
enough that our Thought, and Labor, are employed about these Things, according
as our daily Task is, that we be diligent in our Business, and not Drones in
the Commonwealth, who live upon the Labor of others; that we have our Minds
so far engaged about our temporal Affairs, as is consistent with our Eye
steadily fixed upon our main Business, and thus serve GOD, and promote our
spiritual Interest, while we are at work about our particular Calling: Thus
Matthew. vi. 34.
sufficient unto the Day is the Evil thereof, and we need not to make the Evil
greater, by suffering our selves to be wholly, or chiefly, concerned for the
Body, and the Things thereof; much less, what shall be on the Morrow. We see,
indeed, a very great Part of Mankind so entirely charmed with the Objects of
Sense, and devoted to their Service, that all their Love, and Joy, all their
Care, and Concern, center in them; and while the Men of a lower Figure are in a
perpetual Hurry and Bustle to raise their Fortune, and scarce afford themselves
Time to eat, or sleep, and will not boggle at any Methods to increase their
Stock, that they may make them a Name, and a Family in the Earth, the Men of
the most elevated Figure, are often, at the same Time, immersing themselves in
a continual Succession of sensual Pleasures, torturing themselves for the
Invention of new and fresher Ones, and racking themselves with the Fears left
another should enjoy more than they do, or should get a Step before them in the
Race of worldly Honor: So that the Cares of this World, and deceitful Riches,
take up the Thought, Labor, and Time, of the Generality of Men, as if they
were made for nothing else. But how mean, and foolish, is this? How much below,
and unbecoming the Dignity of our Nature is it? For certainly, as rational
Creatures, we ought to give the Preference to that which is of most Value in
itself, and of the greatest Consequence to us; and therefore to be constantly
reaching after a State of Perfection, both of Purity and Happiness, to be most
thoughtful and concerned how, and in what Way this may be attained by us.

If, indeed, the Perfection of our Nature, and our State, were to be gained,
purely, by the Enjoyments of this World, there would be something to be said,
for the Reason of Men's present Conduct; but since we see to the End of all
Perfection, in Things here below, we plainly discern that they are limited both
in their Measure and Duration, and we experience that neither the Knowledge,
the Enjoyment, nor the Improvement of them, will lead us unto true Perfection,
but leave us as far from true Rectitude, and real Felicity, as ever; we ought
therefore to have but a more transient Regard to them, and keep Things, that
are of greater Worth and Moment, chiefly in our View, and make the lesser
Concerns of the Objects of Sense subservient unto them. Hence the Apostle gives
us that wholesome Advice, couched in the Representation of his own Practice, 2
Cor. iv. 18.
We look not at the Things which are seen, but at the Things which are not
seen; for the Things that are seen, are Temporal, but the Things that are not
seen are Eternal. Temporal Things hold no Proportion with Eternal ones; and
because the Things of this World, which we are apt mostly to concern our selves
about, are but Temporal, and this Imperfection ever attends them, that the
Grace of the Fashion thereof passes away, therefore it is highly reasonable
that we should not fix our Minds upon them, and make them the Mark and Scope we
aim at in all that we do. For what will signify all our Seize and
Possessions, our acquired Endowments, our increased Riches, and advanced
Honors? If this be all the Portion we have laid up for our selves; if we have
nothing else to trust to, and depend upon, for our Comfort, when we are about
to depart out of this World, into the invisible World, we shall find our selves
miserably provided for at last; and, when our eternal State comes on, there
will not be left to us so much as One of all the Delights of Sense, to
administer to our Necessities, and afford us any Relief.

It Is very great Meanness and Folly, therefore, in Persons, to have no higher
Views than their Bodies, and the Things that relate to the present Life; it is
greatly beneath them, as rational Beings, and reduces them upon a Level with
the Brute Creatures, who are wholly governed by their Senses, and follow the
Motions of their Appetites, without any higher Principle to direct them; and it
is very great Folly, because when they have done all, and raised themselves to
the utmost Height of temporal Enjoyments, they are really never the better for
them, while they possess them; neither will their irregular Appetites be cured,
nor their Desires satisfied, by them; and, for all that they can tell, they
may, within a very little While, be striped of them all: and then what Pleasure
will they afford them? Were we advanced to the highest Pitch of Grandeur, and
become the Darlings of the admiring Crowd; could we heap up Stores, 'till we
were able to purchase the Indies; and were we daily entertained with all the
Delights created Nature could yield us; yet the native and relative
Imperfection of all would still leave the Soul unsatisfied, and in a State of
Want and Uneasiness; the Result of all would be that, Eccl. v. 10.
He that loves Silver, shall not be satisfied with Silver; nor he that loves
Abundance, with Increase. Then certainly we ought to be less sedulous and
careful about such empty and perishing Enjoyments, and have our Minds more
seriously concerned about Things of greater Consequence to us, about our
never-dying Souls, and our eternal Interest; for these are Things of the
greatest and nearest Importance to us, in which all that is dear to us is
enwrapped, on which our eternal Well-Being turns; and therefore we cannot be
too much in earnest to save our Souls, and get to Heaven, by making our Peace
with GOD, through Faith in CHRIST, and a Life of Obedience; but it is vain to
lavish away all, or the chief of our Care and Industry, to so little Purpose,
as the best Accommodations in this World, and, at the same Time, foolishly
neglect eternal Things, which are of everlasting Importance to us. The Apostle
therefore directs us, Col. iii. 1, 2.
to seek those Things which are above, where CHRIST sits at the right Hand
of GOD; to set our Affections on Things above, not on Things on the Earth.

This should put us upon the most earnest Endeavors, and unwearied Prayers, to
the GOD and Father of our LORD JESUS CHRIST, that we may obtain the Graces of
the Divine Spirit in our Hearts, and to make sure of an heavenly Inheritance,
as our Portion forever; because these will heal the Disorders of our Souls, and
afford us abundant Satisfaction here, and render us completely happy hereafter.
Hence we have that Advice of our Savior, Matthew. vi. 19, 20, 33.
Lay not up for yourselves Treasures upon Earth, where Moth and Rust does
corrupt; and where Thieves break through, and steal; but lay up for your selves
Treasure in Heaven, where neither Moth nor Rust does corrupt, and where Thieves
do not break through, nor steal: -- Seek first the Kingdom of GOD, and His
Righteousness, and all these Things shall be added unto you.

3. Hence we may see, what little Reason we have to put our Trust in the
Creature. It was the Injunction laid upon Timothy, by the Apostle Paul, 1 Timothy
vi. 17.
Charge them that are rich in this World, that they trust not in uncertain
Riches, but in the living GOD. GOD only, and not the Creature, is the proper
Object of our Trust and Dependence. And yet we are prone to imagine that there
is an higher Degree of Excellency in the Creature, than, upon Examination, we
shall find, and thence are foolishly led to put our Trust in it, and look for
great Things from it. But, may we see an End of all Perfection? Then certainly
this World, and the Things of it, are unworthy of our Trust and Dependence,
because they will certainly deceive us. Indeed, every Creature of GOD is good,
and ought to be received, by us, with Thanksgiving; nevertheless, we have very
little Reason to trust in what is not truly excellent in it self, and so is
unworthy our Dependence, and what is much more relatively imperfect, and
therefore but a sandy Foundation for us to build our Hopes upon. Put not your
Trust in Princes, nor in the Son of Man, in whom there is no Help: His Breath
goes forth, he returns to his Earth; that very Day his Thoughts perish. Ps.
cxlvi. 3, 4.
Let us descend a little into Particulars.

1. The Creature will not support us under the various Troubles we meet withal
while we are in this World: No not our outward ones. We find, by sad
Experience, that, as our Days an Earth are but few, so, they are full of
Trouble. The World we live in is full of Changes, and many are the Sorrows we
meet with which the most excellent of the Creatures cannot prevent; and how
little a Way do they go toward the keeping of our Hearts from fainting, in the
Day of Adversity? Their Silver, and their Gold shall not be able to deliver
them, in the Day of the Wrath of the LORD; they shall not satisfy their Souls,
neither fill their Bowels, said the Prophet Ezekiel Ezck. vii. 19.
. We often find the Things of the World are the Causes, and Occasions, of our
being in Heaviness, and filled with weeping and mourning: The Hardships, and
Toil we are put to, in our Pursuit after them, the Anguish they give us, when
our Affairs are perplexed and embarrassed, the Anxiety of our Minds how to keep
them, and the exquisite Pain they bring upon us, in our parting with them,
plainly show us, that the greatest Part of the Afflictions that befall us arise
from the Objects of Sense; but how seldom do we find any of them stepping in to
our Relief, when we are ready to sink under our Burdens. So that if our Hope
were only from these Things, our Condition would be truly miserable,
notwithstanding all the Help we could have from them.

But then, alas! what will all these Things avail us under the Convictions of
an awakened Conscience, and that inward, and Soul-Trouble, which arises from a
quick Sense of our Sin and Guilt. And yet something of this we have felt, or
must feel, as ever we hope to obtain the Forgiveness of our Sins, and to be
brought to that true Repentance, which is unto Salvation. The wise Man informs
us, Prove. xviii. 14.
That the Spirit of a Man will sustain his Infirmity; but a wounded Spirit who
can bear? The Vigor and Cheerfulness of the Mind will enable a Man to bear up,
pretty well, under the common Calamities, and Accidents, of the present Life;
but when once the Strength, and Vigor of the Mind is broke in upon, and the
quick Sense of Guilt has deprived it of its inward Peace, and Comfort, it is
not in the Power of all the gaudy Honors, the deceitful Riches, nor the
enticing Pleasures of this World, to sooth and calm the Soul, and restore solid
Joy and Quietness unto it. No; nothing can quiet such a Soul, but either a
sinking into a perfect Stupidity, which will raise a greater Storm in the End,
or else some probable Hopes of the pardoning Mercy of GOD, through the Merits
of JESUS CHRIST our Lord.

2. Again; How little will all these Things avail us in the Day of Death? When
the Harbingers of Death appear before us, we are very ready to betake our
selves to the Creature for Help; (and we do well to make Use of the best Means
we can, that, if possibly, we may ward off the coming Blow) but if the Sentence
is passed, and we find our Life draws nigh to the Edges of the Grave, our
Strength is failing us, our Breath is departing from us, and our Feet are
stumbling upon the dark Mountains; will the Creature then be able to save us
from falling, or pluck us back from the Gates of the Grave? No certainly; they
will all then be miserable Comforters, Physicians of no Value to us, and vain
will be all our Expectations from them. For, as the Psalmist observes, Ps.
xlix. 6, -- 19.
They that trust in their Wealth, and boast themselves in the Multitude of
their Riches; none of them can, by any Means, redeem his Brother, -- that he
should still live forever, and not see Corruption: for be sees that wise Men
die, likewise the Fool, and the brutish Person, perish, and leave their Wealth
to others: -- like Sheep they are laid in the Grave, Death shall feed upon
them, -- and their Beauty shall consume in the Grave. -- Though whilst be
lived, he blessed his Soul: and Men will praise thee when thou do well to
thyself: he shall go to the Generation of his Fathers, they shall never see
Light. The most fervent Affection, and tender Embraces, of the dearest Friends,
will not be able to screen us, nor their most importunate Entreaties obtain a
Release for us; Death will be hardened against all their Fondness, and deaf to
all their Cries; the ablest Physicians, and the richest Cordials, will have no
Power to retain our flying Spirits; nor will our Bags of Silver, and Gold, and
our sparkling Jewels, be sufficient to bride the grim Officer, nor the whole
Creation to save us from the Arrest of the King of Terrors. Nothing will exempt
us from paying the last Debt to Nature, neither is there any Discharge in this
War Eccl. viii. 8.
. There is not one of us all but what must take our Turn, to fall down slain in
this War, as innumerable have done before us. Man dies, and wastes away; yea,
Man gives up the Ghost, and where is he? As the Waters fail from the Sea, and
the Flood decays, and dries up; so Man lies down, and rises not till the
Heavens be no more. Job xvi. 10, 11, 12.


3. Once more; How insignificant will the Creature be to him in the Day of
Judgment? When the Man comes to stand a Trial, before the awful Tribunal of the
great GOD, the supreme Judge of all, as, ever long, he certainly must, which of
all the Creatures will then rise up, and appear on his Behalf, and effectually
plead his Cause, and secure him from all Harm? Yea, will his boon Companions,
the Partners of his Crimes, then have the Face to plead, in Excuse for him,
such Things as they now think to be very witty and unanswerable; or to turn off
the Judge with an unmannerly Sneer, as they now can their virtuous Reprover?
Alas! those mighty Hectors will be seized with an unusual Trembling, and
Astonishment take hold upon them, for Fear of their own Punishment, which they
can see no Way of escaping. Or will the Man's worldly Possessions interpose,
and screen him from the Resentments of his Judge? Alas! Those Trifles have no
Place in that awful Presence. Or can any Man fetch a Plea, from the Creature,
sufficient to wipe off his Guilt, to acquit him from Condemnation, and render
him acceptable unto his Judge? Alas! they will all fail him, and say it is not
in me. For, Riches profit not in the Day of Wrath, Prove. xi. 4.
. Our most profound Learning, and piercing Wit, will not be sufficient to
palliate and cover our Crimes from the View of our Judge, or to find a Nonsuit
in our Case, or bring us off by challenging the Jurisdiction of the Court. And
though we should be able to say, and prove it, that we have heretofore been
accounted the Great Ones of the Earth, and have sat at the Head of Nations and
Kingdoms, have worn the Badges of Honor, and Ensigns of Power, and have
possessed a very large Share of the Enjoyments of the present Life, and
glittered in gaudy Accoutrements, in Embroideries of Gold, bespangled with
Diamonds; yet all of this will procure no Respect to our Persons, before the
righteous Tribunal of that GOD, with whom the Prince and the Beggar are alike,
as to their Persons, and differ only according to their Works. For the Father,
without Respect of Persons, judges according to every Man's Work. 1 Pet. i. 17.


4. Finally; What Relief can the Creature afford to the Soul, under the
Impressions of the Wrath of an angry GOD, in the Place of Torment? Will any of
the Excellencies of the Creature then step in, and support a miserable Soul,
weltering under the Horrors of an enraged Conscience, and the insupportable
Weight of the Divine Anger, and render his Condition easy to him? Will their
united Force be able to rescue him from the strong Hands of incensed Justice,
or pluck him out of the Midst of devouring Flames? Or can they possibly fill
his Mouth with Songs, and his Heart with Rejoicing, while the never-dying Worm
gnaws, and everlasting Burning preys upon him? To which of all the Creatures
will he turn, and say, This same shall comfort me? Or will it be any thing of
Comfort, to such an one, to call to mind his former State of Grandeur, of
Affluence, and Ease; that he wallowed in Pleasures, while People and Nations
bowed down at his Feet: Nay! will it not be said to him, as a Part of his
Punishment, as Abraham to Dives? Luke xvi. 25.
Son, Remember that, in thy Lifetime, thou badst thy good Things; but now thou
art tormented! A sad Remembrance indeed! The very Reflection upon his former
Enjoyments will increase his Misery upon him, and the more, when he shall
bethink himself, how he came by them, and what Improvement he made of them;
yea, his Torment will be so much the greater, by how much, in his Lifetime, he
trusted in them, and now, to his Cost, he finds they are utterly unable to help
him.

II. The second Use of this Doctrine may be for Conviction and Reproof, to all
such as seek for Happiness in the Creature, or that abuse the Creature to ill
Intents and Purposes.

1. This affords Conviction and Reproof to those who seek for Happiness in the
Creature. And how many are there that fall under Rebuke, who live, in this
World, as if Perfection and Happiness were no where else to be attained, but in
the Enjoyment of the Creature? This present World, they think, has a sufficient
Fullness in it to render them truly happy; and here, therefore, they fix their
Affections, and level their Aims, and look for no higher Degrees of Felicity,
than what the Things about them can yield to them. Hence they turn every Stone,
rise early, and fit up late, and are ever hunting, with an eager Chase, after
the Enjoyments of Sense; and, while they are in the hot Pursuit, often leap
over the Boundaries of Religion, and even Humanity, and stick at nothing, how
mean and base and dishonorable soever it may be, so that they can but seize
the Prey, and get what they account enough of the World. And there are,
especially, two Sorts of Persons, who yet agree in one, the Covetous and the
Unrighteous, that evidently place their Happiness in Things here below, who
fall under Rebuke.

1. The covetous Worldling has set his Heart upon the Creature, and looks for
his Happiness in the Enjoyment of it. Why else has the World his Heart? Why
does he mind nothing but earthly Things? but because he has made the World his
God. He has no Love to the Father, because the Love of the World bears the Sway
in him, and leaves no Room for GOD, and RELIGION, in his Heart and Actions; so
that he can part with his Soul, with Heaven, and with GOD himself, for the Sake
of the World. He finds that he cannot serve two Masters, and he is for cleaving
to the Objects of Sense, which seem to him to bring a present Reward with them,
and slights the invisible GOD, whose Rewards, he thinks, if any, are out of
Sight. Hence we see the covetous Man, from the Fondness of his Affections to
the World, sometimes even begrutching himself the moderate Use of what he
possesses, that though he wastes nothing for his Soul of all that he desires,
yet GOD gives him not Power to eat thereof Eccl. vi. 2.
: So there is one alone, and there is not a Second; yea, he has neither Child,
nor Brother, yet is there no End of all his Labor, neither is his Eye
satisfied with Riches, neither says he, for whom do I labor, and bereave my
Soul of Good Eccl. iv. 8.
? And yet if any Thing be demanded of him, for the Service of GOD, or his
Neighbor, in Works of Piety and Charity, it is like pouring out of his Heart's
Blood for him to part with it. His Thought, and Time, are so taken up about
those Things that are on the Earth, that he can find no Leisure to attend upon
the Duties he owes to GOD, and his own Soul; he cannot find Time to go alone,
and read the Word of GOD, and pray to him; he has no spare Minutes to worship
the Lord in his Family; and it is with Regret that he is forced to lay aside
the World, and wait upon GOD, in his House, upon his holy Day Hence the Calls
and Offers of the Gospel (...) light of by him, because of the Cares of the
Farm, and the Merchandise Matthew. xxii. 5.
. Yea, his Covetousness will put him upon felling of his Master, as (...) did,
for a little Pelf, and a worldly Spirit in (...) is often the Parent of the
most horrid and unnatural Crimes; For the Love of Money is the Root of all
Evil, 1 Timothy vi. 10.
and the overvaluing of it makes People haughty and barbarous, and false both
to GOD and Man: And thus, for the Sake of the World, he loses his Soul and
Heaven for ever. It Is evident that this Man seeks for Happiness in the
Creature, because his Heart is entirely set upon it; for where a Man's
Treasure, his Happiness, is, there his Heart will be also Mat. vi. 21.
. And is this indeed to act the Part of a Man? Do thou glory in thy Reason,
as distinguishing of thee from the Brute, and yet will thou herd among them,
and be led and governed by Sense, as they are, and be concerned for no higher
Degrees of Felicity than what arises from sensible Objects? How just is it in
GOD to say to thee, Be it as thou will, and assign thee thy Portion where thou
have sought it, and put thee off with the mean low Gratifications of the animal
Life, and seclude thee forever from the pure, refined, sublime Joys of the
heavenly State, which thou have no Desires after, nor Relish for? Verily, No
covetous Person shall inherit the Kingdom of Heaven. 1 Cor. vi. 10.


2. The unrighteous Person places his Happiness in the Creature. It is very
evident that he seeks for Perfection and Happiness in worldly Enjoyments,
because he can willingly risk every Thing else for the Sake of them; and
therefore can allow himself to violate the Laws of GOD, which forfeits his real
Happiness, by his dealing unrighteously with his Neighbor, that he may gain
the World. Hence we often see the unrighteous Person can please himself in
being guilty of the most violent Oppression upon his Neighbor; and forcibly
rend from him, what, he cannot but ^^ow notwithstanding all his false Claims,
he has ^o just Right to; and, though he pretends a mighty Regard to Justice,
yet he can pervert (...) Law it self, by taking the Advantage of (...) little
Form and Modality of it, to trick and (...) out of his Interest, to his
manifest Hurt and Image. Hence the unrighteous Person can allow himself in
Extortion, by griping Usury, by imposing upon the Ignorance, Weakness, or
Necessity of his Neighbor, to make a greater Gain of him than he ought to do.
Hence, he sometimes openly, and otherwhiles secretly, robs and steals from his
Neighbor, and deals treacherously and deceitfully, with false Weights and
Measures, and false Accounts, and makes no Bones of breaking his Word and
Promise, falsifying the Trust reposed in him: And sometimes proceeds even to
murder his Neighbor, that he may secure his Money. All of these Ways of
Unrighteousness, are the sad Fruits and Effects of the prevailing Influence
which the World has over Men. It Is because the Man thinks that all his
Happiness lies in his having an Abundance of these Things, that he has so
little Regard to Right, or Wrong, to Justice or Injustice, so he may but enrich
himself with them; though such often find it sadly verified upon them, that
what they thought to be the nearest Way to enrich themselves, has in Reality
proved the furthest from it: So the Curse of GOD is fulfilled upon them, Prove.
xxii. 16.
He that oppresses the Poor, to increase his Riches, shall surely come to
want: And the flying Roll shall enter into the House of the Thief, and it shall
remain in the midst of his House, and shall consume it, with the Timber
thereof, and the Stones thereof Zach. v. 2, 4.
; a secret Blast from GOD, upon their Undertakings and Labors, consumes their
Substance, and they are poor, and low, and despised, after all.

Certainly then, their Sin and Folly is to be reproved. For if we may set an
End of all Perfection, then all those, who so place their Happiness in the
Creature, will, sooner, or later, find themselves to have been greatly imposed
upon, and that they have themselves been accessory to the Cheat, by looking for
that in the Creature, which was not in it. All their Possessions are, at best,
but uncertain Riches, and whoever aims at Perfection and Happiness, in the
Enjoyment of them, will in the Conclusion, experience to his Sorrow, that he
has made use of a deceitful Bow, which has carried his Shafts vastly wide of
the Mark, and disappointed his Expectation; though they look ever so fair and
promising, while we view them at a Distance, yet, to those that trust in them,
and found their Hopes upon them, they will only prove, like the tempting Apple
to our Grandmother Eve, hurtful and destructive: they will, not only as
certainly baulk their Hopes, but, leave them as miserable, in the End, as they
did the rich Fool, in the Gospel, Luke xii. 19, 20.
who said unto himself, Soul, take thine Ease, eat, drink, and be merry, thou
have Goods laid up for many Years, when GOD said to him, Thou Fool, this Night
thy Soul shall be required of thee; and then whose shall all these Things be
which thou have provided? For, as the Partridge sets upon Eggs, and hatcheth
them not, so he that gets Riches, and not by Right, shall leave them in the
Midst of his Days, and at his End shall be a Fool Jer. xvii. 11.
. As his Folly is great, so is his Sin, in seeking for Happiness in the Things
of this World, because this is no other than to set up the Creature in the
Throne of GOD, and so to be guilty of that Covetousness, which is Idolatry Col.
iii. 5.
, which will bring a Damnation that slumbereth not.

2. This affords Conviction and Reproof to all such as make an ill Use of, and
abuse, the Creature. Though the Creature is not, of itself, perfective of our
Nature, nor compleative of our Happiness, yet, by the Blessing of GOD, it may
be improved by us, as a Mean, to further these great Ends, by leading of us,
from the Streams, to the Fountain Head: and this is what, as rational Agents,
we should ever have in our View, and make our principal Design, in our Use of
the Good Things of this Life. But while we abuse the Creature, and make an ill
Use of it, we pervert this grand Intention, and do but so much the more blemish
and degrade our Nature, and fix it under its greatest Imperfections; and so
become guilty of very great Sin and Folly in abusing the Creature, and
ourselves with it. And so do all they, who improve what they have of the World
to no higher End and Purpose than the indulging of their Lusts, and complying
with their sensual Appetites: These dishonor the Name of GOD, which is
manifested in, and by, His Creatures; and greatly hurt and injure themselves,
by pampering their carnal and fleshly Lusts with them, and therefore are to be
reproved as guilty before GOD. The Apostolical Rule is, that 1. Cor. vii. 31.
, They that use the World, should be as not abusing it: for the Fashion of the
World passes away. And yet, we often see Persons act so unreasonable a Part,
as to abuse these short-lived Enjoyments to their own Detriment; so Riches are
kept for the Owners thereof to their Hurt Eccl. v. 13.
. Thus, particularly, there are two Sorts of Persons that abuse the Creature,
namely, such as nourish their Pride, and such as indulge their Intemperance
with them.

1. Such as nourish their Pride with their worldly Enjoyments. Thus many often
abuse the Creature, to inflame their Minds, and blow up their Vanity, and so
fall into the Condemnation of the Devil 1. Tim. iii. 6.
. If they possess a little more of this World than some of their Neighbors,
they grow haughty, and supercilious, upon it; and, as if they were raised to
some lofty Eminence, look down with Contempt upon those they see below them;
and very often their Hearts are lifted up in them against GOD Himself, that
they can neither stoop to own their Dependence on Him, and His Goodness to
them, but think it beneath them to petition for their daily Bread, or render
GOD Thanks for what they enjoy; nor to submit themselves to the Government of
His Laws, or the Conduct of His Providence. Thus it is said Deuteronomy. xxxii. 15.
Jeshurun waxed fat, and kicked, -- then he forsook the GOD that made him, and
lightly esteemed the Rock of his Salvation.

But what have thou, O vain Man, to be proud of? What! but an imperfect fading
World! Art thou proud of thy Beauty, thy comely Stature, thy exact Proportion,
thy bright Complexion, thy sprightly Air? Why, in how little a while will all
thy Luster and Charms, be consumed away, and the Beauty which thou have be
turned into loathsome Putrefaction, in the rotting Grave? if they fade not long
before thou descendest to that dark and cold Abode. Or do thou pride thy
self in thy great Estate, the Number of thy Acres, thy Bags of Gold, and thy
splendid Train? Why, thou art but the more loaded with thick Clay, which, at
present, fit heavy upon thee, and is a Cumber about thee, and hereafter will
inflame thy Reckoning, as it increased thy Debt; and beside will anon wing
itself away from thee, or thou must leave it all behind thee. Or art thou proud
of thy swelling Titles, and high Posts of Honor? Why, do not these all perish
in the using? Is not the Ground thou stand on the more slippery? and may not
the popular Blast be turned against thee to Morrow? Or will any of thy Glory
descend after thee? But what art thou really the better for any, or all, of
these things? It Is true, there is a civil Respect due to Men, upon the Account
of their raised Station, and large Possessions, which it is fitting, for others
to give, and for them to receive, though it be not for them to challenge; but
yet, what little Reason has any Man to be proud of them? when they, all of
them, cannot rectify the Disorders of his vitiated Soul, and stamp the bright
Characters of moral Goodness upon him; but rather place his Weaknesses in a
stronger Light, expose him more to View, and draw upon him a more general
Contempt. So that after all the humble Saint, in his lowest Poverty, when
weighed in a just Balance, will turn the Beam against the wealthiest Craesus,
with all his Possessions thrown in for Advantage: For Pride goth before
Destruction, and an haughty Spirit before a Fall Prove. xvi. 18.
.

2. They abuse the Creature who improve it to indulge their Intemperance. GOD
allows us to take the Comfort of the good Things, which, in His Providence, He
bestows upon us; so that we may not only feed ourselves for our necessary
Support, and cloth ourselves to defend our Bodies from the Injuries of the
Weather, but we may, as our Circumstances will admit, sometimes, please our
Palates, by feeding more deliciously, and drink to the cheering of our Spirits,
and make a gayer Appearance than usual; therefore the Preacher says, Eccl. ix.
7.
Go thy Way, eat thy Bread with Joy, and drink thy Wine with a merry Heart, for
GOD now accepts thy Work. But then GOD does not allow us to make use of the
Creature to Luxury, Gluttony, and Drunkenness; no; this is a vile Abuse of the
good Creatures of GOD, and a vile Abuse of ourselves with them. For a Man to
suffer his Appetite to ride Post with him, and be always upon the Switch and
Spur, after the finest, and the best, the richest, and the strongest, as if his
whole Soul had taken up it is entire Residence in his Palate; and never to be
contented till he has gorged down enough to intoxicate himself; that is, to be
excessive in his Craving, and go beyond the Bounds of Moderation, in the
Quality, and Quantity, of his Meats, and Drinks, and Apparel, in the common
Use of them; this is such an intemperate Use of the Creature as the Soul of the
Lord abhors; and therefore He has pronounced His We upon them that chant to the
Sound of the Viol, that drink Wine in Bowls; that rise up early in the Morning,
that they may follow strong Drink, that continue until Night, till Wine inflame
them Am. vi. 5, 6.
. And our Savior straightly charges, all that would be His Disciples, to guard
against such an intemperate Use of the Creature, saying to them, Luke. xxi. 34.
Take heed to yourselves, lest, at any Time, your Hearts be over charged with
Surfeiting and Drunkenness. Such an ill Use of the Creature GOD complains of,
in His People of old, and therefore threatens to recover all out of their Hand,
Hos. ii. 8, 9.
She knew not that I gave her Corn, and Wine, and Oil, and multiplied her
Silver, and Gold, which they prepared for Baal; therefore I will return, and
take away my Corn in the Time thereof, and my Wine in the Time thereof etc.
Such an intemperate Use of the Creature, is exceeding great Sin, and Folly, as
it impairs, and debauches, the Reason, vitiates the Blood, and wounds and
distempers the Body, and often blasteth a Man's Name, and lays his Reputation
in the Dust, and reduces him to Penury and Want; and it is a vile perverting of
what the Bounty of GOD bestows upon Persons, with Design that they may honor
the Lord with their Substance, and do Good in their Generation, by Acts of
Piety and Charity, and not squander them away upon the nourishing and
increasing their Lusts; and it effectually shuts out of Heaven at last, for, no
Drunkard shall inherit the Kingdom of GOD 1. Cor. iv. 10.
.

III. The third and last Use of this Doctrine may be for Exhortation, to
prevail with us to behave our selves wisely in our Regards to the Creature.
Need have we to act a wise and prudent Part, and weigh Things in an even
Balance, and think seriously and closely, upon the Nature of sublunary
Enjoyments, and the Consequence of our doting upon them, before we give a Loose
to our Appetites, and suffer our selves to be run away with by them. For we are
in exceeding great Danger of being imposed upon, by the external Luster of
Things about us, their easy Access to us, and the forcible Impression they make
upon our Senses, and the powerful Attractive of the general Conduct of Mankind
concerning them; and if we suffer our selves to be led away by the gay Cheat,
our Disappointment will be to our unspeakable Damage, in the Loss of all that
would truly render us happy, as well as of that which we vainly thought would
do so; and this will be no other than to leave us finally, and for ever
miserable. Let us then be persuaded, seasonably, to correct the Mistake, and
since we may see an End of all Perfection, in the Creature, be so wise as to
govern our selves in our Conduct, with Respect to the Things of this World, as
those that are fully convinced, that they are not able, by any Excellency in
them, to perfect our Nature, nor complete our Happiness, and, if they were ever
so perfect in themselves, cannot continue long with us.

And therefore,

1. Let us be careful not to raise our Expectations too high, and look for more
in the Creature than it can yield us. We are very apt to run into this great
Mistake, to augment and magnify the Creature, while we view it at a Distance,
through false Glasses; and hence we are ready to flatter our selves with the
Expectation of great Things from it, and thence enlarge our Desires after it:
but when we bring it near to us, like some coarse Paintings, which are
beautiful at their proper Distance, all its Glory vanishes, and we then see it
in all it is real Imperfections. When once Eve had got a Conceit, that the Tree
was good to make one wise, and she should be as Gods, this greatly enflamed her
Desire after it; and there is but a short Step between enflamed Desire and
actual Transgression: He that looks for that in the Creature which it has not,
may enlarge his Desire as Hell, and not be satisfied, and then no Wonder if
that rise suddenly which shall bite him, and awake that shall vex him. We must
therefore learn to maintain a low Opinion of worldly Enjoyments, and always
remember, that it is an imperfect World we converse with; that we may not fix
our Thoughts too much upon it, nor be hurried into too great an Eagerness in
our Pursuit after it, nor be thrown into Uneasiness at the having of our Views
and Designs frustrated by it. This was the Apostle's Advice, 1 Cor. vii. 30.
Let them that weep be, as though they wept not; and they that rejoice, as
though they rejoiced not; and they that buy, as though they possessed not.

2. Let us be very moderate in our Regards to the Things of this World. Let it
be our Care to bring our Appetites, and Desires, under a good Regulation, that
we may not be carried away by the Vehemence of our own Cravings; and let our
Labors after the World be directed by the Moderation of our Desires. We are to
be diligent and industrious in the Business of our particular Calling, but yet
we must not be so immoderately eager, and laborious, as to neglect the Concerns
of another World, which, of all Things, are of the greatest Consequence unto
us. Therefore, as the Apostle directs, Phil. iv. 5.
Let your Moderation be known unto all Men: That is, let it evidently appear
unto all Men, that you are not the Men of this World, who have their Portion in
this Life, by your being moderate in your Affections, in your Cares, and
Labors, after Creature-Enjoyments. For the immoderate Cares of the World very
much tend to eat out the Heart of Religion, and, like the abounding of ill
Weeds, choke the good Seed that is sown in us.

3. Be not impatient under the Loss of any Thing here below. The GOD from whom
we receive our Being, and all that we have, is our Sovereign LORD, and has a
Right to take from us whatsoever he has lent us. Our Impatience, and Murmuring,
under Losses and Disappointments, or that our Condition is no better, will be
an Affront unto the Divine Supremacy, and Government, and argue that the World
has got too strong Possession of our Hearts, or we should not so call in
Question His Authority, His Wisdom, and Goodness. We should not therefore be as
Bullocks unaccustomed unto the Yoke, but learn to behave as weaned Children to
all Things here below, that we may be able to support our Minds, under our
Bereavements, with a steady Calmness and Composure of Soul, and may take with
Contentedness, if not with Joy, the spoiling of our Goods. Thus says the
Apostle, Heb. xiii. 5.
Be content with such Things as ye have. For, why should our Souls be
disquieted within us, when we are obliged to part with what we know to be an
imperfect Creature? This Thought should teach us to inure ourselves to
Patience, that it may have its perfect Work in us, though we should be crossed
in our greatest worldly Interests, or be spoiled of our dearest Enjoyments;
Thou O LORD have done it.

4. Let us endeavor, as much as we can, to retrieve the Creature from its
Imperfection. This would be the noblest Improvement of it, both respecting the
Creature, and our selves. And therefore, to hint;

1. Let us endeavor to get the Creature sanctified. When the Curse, which is
brought upon the Creature, by our Sin, is removed, then will it be recovered
from much of its Imperfecxction; it will then become a sanctified Creature, and
truly profitable to us. For, nothing is unclean of itself, but every Creature
of GOD is good, -- for it is sanctified by the Word of GOD, and Prayer. 1 Timothy
iv. 4, 5.
Let this then be our constant Care to get the Creature sanctified by the Word
of GOD, that it may become a good Creature to us. Therefore attend the Rules
prescribed in the Word of GOD, in all our Desires, and Labors, after it, and
in our Use, and Improvement of it; that the Word of Blessing may accompany it,
and we may receive it, in the Promise, as Part of our Covenant-Portion, suited
to our outward Support in the House of our Pilgrimage; and receive CHRIST, the
LORD, in and with it; so shall we have a Propriety in it, and CHRIST being
ours, all will be ours also. 1 Cor. iii. 21, 22.


And get the Creature sanctified by Prayer; by an earnest imploring the Divine
Guidance, and Assistance, in all our just and laudable Designs and
Undertakings, and the Blessing of GOD upon all that we enjoy. For, how can any
expect that the Providence of GOD should interpose, to lead them in a right
Way, to succeed their Enterprises, and bless what they have, and make it
comfortable unto them, if they will not so much as pray for it? And then,
thankfully acknowledge the Goodness of GOD to you, in bestowing so much of the
Comforts of this World upon you, when the least is more than you deserve. So in
every Thing, by Prayer and Supplication, with Thanksgiving, let your Request be
made known unto GOD. Phil. iv. 6.


2. Improve the Creature to the best Ends and Purposes. See GOD, in the
Creature, shining in His unsearchable Power, and Wisdom, and Goodness, and
displaying His Glory in all the Works of his Hands; and be led by the View and
Enjoyment of sensible Objects, to just Contemplations on the Divine Being and
Perfections, and suitable Acknowledgments unto the great GOD, the first Cause
of all Things. So you find the Psalmist saying, Ps. viii. 1, 3, 4.
O LORD, our LORD, How excellent is thy Name in all the Earth! who have set thy
Glory above the Heavens! When I consider Thy Heavens, the Work of Thy Fingers,
the Moan, and the Stars, which Thou have ordained; what is Man, that Thou art
mindful of him? and the Son of Man, that Thou visitest him?

And improve the Creature to an universal Fruitfulness in Good Works; in Works
of Piety, serving the LORD with our Substance, (...) supporting the Honor of
His Name, and the ^^^^^nances of his House, and Worship. So we are commanded,
and so GOD has graciously promised, Prove. iii. 9, 10.
Honor the LORD, with thy Substance, and with the first Fruits of thine
Increase; so shall thy Barns be filled with Plenty, and thy Presses shall burst
out with new Wine. And to the same Purpose says the Prophet, Mal. iii. 10.
Bring ye all the Tithes into the Storehouse, that there may be Meat in my
House, and prove Me now herewith, says the Lord of Hosts, if I will not open
the Windows of Heaven, and pour you out a Blessing, that there shall not be
Room enough to receive it.

Improve the Creature also in Works of Charity, readily distributing a Portion,
as we are able, to the Relief of the Poor and Needy, doing Good unto all Men,
especially unto the Household of Faith. Gal. vi. 10.
Give Alms of such Things as ye have, and behold all Things are clean unto you.
Luke xi. 41.
And our Savior has assured us, Matthew. x. 42.
Whosoever shall give to drink, unto one of these little Ones, a Cup of cold
Water only, in the Name of a Disciple, verify, I say unto you, be shall in no
wise lose his Reward.

Thus let us make to our selves Friends with the Mammon of Unrighteousness,
that when the imperfect Creature shall fail us, They may receive us into
everlasting Habitations. This will be the Way for us to retrieve the Creature
from very much of its Imperfection, and make it relatively serviceable to us,
in carrying on the Divine Workmanship in our Souls, in glorifying of GOD upon
Earth, and laying up for our selves a good Foundation against the Time to come;
and then, wh^^ Time shall be no more with us, and we shall ^^ve no further
Occasion for the Objects of Sen^^, we shall go to partake of the ineffable
Delights above, in the Possession of which our Nature will be perfected, and
our Happiness for ever complete.

The Excellency of the Divine Commandment.
SERMON IV.
PSALM CXIX. 96. I have seen an End of all Perfection; but thy Commandment is
exceeding broad.


I Have named two Doctrines, as plainly contained in these Words, viz.

I. That the Perfection of the Creature is limited and finite.

II. That the Commandment of GOD is exceeding broad.

I have already discoursed to you upon the First of these, and showed you, that
the Perfection of the Creature is limited in its Nature and Measure, whether we
consider it abstractedly, for so there is no mere Creature that is possessed of
all Excellencies, nor, any of them, of any One Excellency in the highest
Degree; or whether we consider the Creature in its Relation, especially unto
ourselves, for so it is neither perfective of our Nature, nor our Happiness;
and besides there will be an End of all worldly Perfection, either the Objects
of Sense, we so much delight in; will be taken from us, or we from them: Which
shows the sad Effect of our Apostasy, and the Folly of being chiefly concerned
about, or trusting in, the Creature, of looking for Happiness in it, and making
a wrong Improvement of it; and should prevail with us all to be very careful to
behave our selves wisely in our Conduct respecting the Things of this World,
that we don't look for too much from them, nor be immoderate in our Desires and
Labors after them, nor impatient under the Loss of them, but endeavor to
retrieve the Creature from its Imperfection, by getting it sanctified to us,
and by improving of it to the best Ends and Purposes, in Works of Piety and
Charity.

I proceed now to the Second Doctrine, namely,

Doc. II. That the Commandment of GOD is exceeding broad.

By the Commandment of GOD here, I understand, the whole Will of GOD, made
known to us, relating to His rational Agents, especially respecting Mankind, as
including in it our whole Duty, both as to Knowledge and Practice; or what
ought to be our Apprehensions and Conceptions of the Divine Being; and what the
Homage, and Obedience, are, which we owe unto Him; and what should be our
Government of our selves, and Behavior to our Fellow Creatures; and what GOD
will do for us, in Case of Fidelity in our Allegiance to Him: All of which is
comprehended in the Divine Commandment.

And it is to be remembered, that the Psalmist is here making a Comparison
between the Commandment of GOD, and the Creature, and the exceeding Breadth of
the divine Commandment is opposed to the Finiteness of the Creature, or the
limited Perfection of all the Things of this World; and he plainly declares,
that the Commandment of GOD contains an Excellency and Perfection in it, vastly
superior unto all that is to be found upon the Creature; it transcends all
other Things, which Men are apt to be fond of, and is of much greater
Consequence to them, being able to make them holy and happy, in Time, and
throughout Eternity, and therefore ought more to be regarded by us than all
this World.

What therefore I have to do under this Doctrine, is to set before you
something of the superior Excellency of the Divine Commandment; and this will
sufficiently appear, if we consider the Commandment in its Rise and Original,
the Subject Matter of it, the Extent of it objectively, the great End and
Design of it, and it is Duration. I shall offer something to each of these in
their Order.

I. The Commandment of GOD will appear exceeding broad, and very excellent, if
we consider it in it is Rise and Original. It is the Commandment of GOD: Thy
Commandment, says the Psalmist. And agreeably, all over the sacred Pages, it is
called the Word, Law, Statutes, Precepts and Commandment of GOD. Though Men
have been the Instruments of the Promulgation of it, in Part, and of
transmitting of it, in Writing, to succeeding Generations, yet it takes it is
Original, not from Man, or any meet Creature, but from GOD only, who by his
Spirit taught, influenced and directed the first Publishers, and Penmen, of
the holy Writings: For the Prophecy came not at old Time, by the Will of Man;
but holy Men of GOD spoke as they were moved by the Holy Ghost 2 Pet. i. 21.


There are such evident Testimonials of its being the Word of GOD, from the
profound Mysteries contained in it, far surpassing the utmost Stretch of humane
Understanding; from the Loftiness and Majesty of it is Sentiments; from the
Holiness and Purity of its Documents; besides the most convincing Credentials,
which those who delivered the divine Commandment to the World, brought with
them, in the Miracles which they wrought, plainly declaring that they were sent
from GOD; as leave no Room for any reasonable Hesitancy, or Doubt, about it:
and therefore we may receive it as the Thessalonians did, 1 Thessalonians. ii. 13.
not as the Word of Man, but (as it is in Truth) the Word of GOD.

For if the divine Commandment, or what we call the Word of GOD, contained in
our Bibles, be not a Revelation from GOD, and so truly his Commandment, then
there is no Religion in the World that is a Revelation from GOD; for no other
but the Christian Religion, as contained in the holy Scriptures, can at this
Day, make any Pretensions to be the Religion which GOD requires of Man: and if
there be no Revelation from GOD of his Mind and Will concerning us, and our
Duty and Interest, or in what Way we are to serve GOD acceptably, and enjoy him
as our Portion and Happiness, then all Mankind must unavoidably perish in their
Sin; because they know no possible Way, by which they may pacify the Divine
Anger, and obtain the Divine Favor; which is such a State of Unhappiness as no
Man, in the Exercise of his Reason, can wish for, but must wish, and hope, that
it might be otherwise. And, blessed be GOD, this is not the lamentable and
helpless Condition of the World, nor ever was; but from the very Beginning
there was a certain, though more obscure, or rather partial Revelation,
directing Man what he must do to escape the Punishment of his Sin, and be happy
forever, made more immediately by GOD Himself, at first to Adam, and by him
handed down to his Posterity by oral Tradition; 'till it pleased GOD, in after
Times, gradually to open the Counsels of His Will more clearly, by Moses, and
the Prophets, and finally complete the Revelation of His Will, in the fullest
Light, by His only begotten Son, whom He sent into the World, and by His
inspired Apostles; which Revelation has been committed to Writing, and handed
down unto us, with all imaginable Strength of Evidence of its being a
Revelation from GOD, and with the fullest Assurances of our Bible's containing
that Revelation, without any material Error, or Mistake.

If we consider the Divine Commandment, with Respect unto the several Laws, and
Rules, of Life, and Manners, which it prescribes unto us, we shall plainly see,
That all moral Duties are wrought up to their Height, and most compendiously,
and yet plainly, and distinctly, contained in the Sacred Volumn; and thereby we
are more fully, and effectually, taught the Knowledge of the Holy, and what
that Love, and Reverence, is, which we owe to the supreme Being; and are
instructed in the Government of ourselves, and how to subdue our Appetites, and
Passions, to the Dictates of Right Reason; and after what Manner to treat our
Fellow Creatures, so as never to injure them, in Thought, Word, or Deed, but,
on the contrary, to do all the Good we can to all about us, so as that we may
be truly Blessings in our several Relations; and at the same Time it requires
us to believe nothing that is Contradictory to our Reason, though many Things
that our Reason cannot comprehend; and enforces our Duty with the strongest
Encouragments, from the infinite Mercy of GOD, a glorious Mediator having
appeared for us, and an almighty Spirit ready to help us; and the most powerful
Motives, fetched from the everlasting Rewards or Punishments of the other
World; and all of this much beyond what has ever been taught in the Schools of
the ablest Philosophers; so that we may well esteem the Holy Bible as
containing the best Body of Laws that ever were contrived, for the Honor of
GOD, and the good Government of Mankind; I say, when we closely consider these
Things, we cannot but rationally conclude, that these are plain Signatures, and
evident Characters, of the Deity, upon that holy Book; and that because it is
every Way so conducive to the Happiness of Mankind, and so highly worthy of a
GOD, excelling all that the utmost Will of the greatest of Men have been able
to reach, therefore it is truly a Revelation from GOD, and not the Invention of
Men.

But then, when we add this further Consideration, That the great Author of our
holy Religion has given the most clear positive Testimony to the Truth of His
Divine Mission, by the many Miracles which He wrought, in His healing the Sick,
raising the Dead, casting out Devils, stilling the Violence of the Wind and
Sea, and all by a Word's speaking; and that His Miracles were wrought in such
an open, and public Manner, and before so many Witnesses, (and owned by His
very Enemies,) as renders the Facts certain, and the Miracles unsuspected; and
further, that His Miracles were numerous, and never confronted, much less
controuled, by any superior Power: and moreover, that the Apostles of our Lord
wrought many Miracles, in Confirmation of their being divinely inspired in the
Doctrine which they taught, and that they sealed the Truth of their Testimony
to the Facts which they relate, with their own Blood: upon these
Considerations, there seems to me not so much as the least Room left for any
Man, reasonably, to call in Question the Truth of the Divine Commandment, but
there is all the Evidence, of it is being a Revelation from GOD, that can
possibly be desired, or that the Nature of the Thing will admit of. And as the
Apostles of our Lord were evidently under the Guidance of the Divine Spirit, in
what they committed to Writing, either with their own Hands, or by their
Amanuenses, so, That their Writings have been handed down to us incorrupt, and
without any material Error, or Mistake, is apparent, from the numerous Copies
of their Writings, early translated into the several Languages, where the
Gospel prevailed, whereby an Opportunity was given to many Nations to have
discovered the Mistakes of Transcribers, if there were any; from the great Care
the Primitive Church took in examining what they admitted to be the authentic
Writings of the Apostles; by the many Quotations, of all Sorts of Writers, in
all Ages, of the more material Passages, out of the Apostolic Books; by the
very Adversaries of Christianity, and undesignedly, giving their Testimony to
the Truth of these Records in what they quote from them; and by the general
Collation, and Comparing, of all Sorts of Copies, from the earliest Ages until
this Time: so that the Writings of the Apostles have been handed down to us,
through the several Ages since, by the great Care of the Church, pure, and
incorrupt. And now, upon the whole, I may well affirm, That we have all the
Reason in the World to rest entirely satisfied in it, as an indisputable Truth,
That our holy Bible contains in it the Divine Commandment, as being a sure
and certain Revelation from GOD Himself.

And because it is the Commandment of GOD, therefore it must necessarily be a
most perfect Law, and partake of an Excellency adequate unto its Divine Author,
and greatly transcend all the Excellency that is to be found upon the Creature.
Were it the Commandment of the wisest, and best of Men only, we could
reasonably expect no higher Degrees of Excellency in it, than are to be Found
in them, and therefore it would, doubtless, be, in many Things, defective, and
share in the Imperfections of its Author, and not be exceeding broad, or
transcendently Excellent; because there is no mere Man so wise, and good, but
what, with all his Wisdom, and Probity, is fallible, and liable to many
Mistakes. But because it is the Commandment of GOD, therefore we may justly
conclude that it partakes of the Divine Excellencies, and is perfect, like GOD
Himself.

Though it be true, that all the Creatures, as well as the Commandment, derive
their Original from GOD, the Fountain of Being, who spoke and it was done, who
commanded and they were created, yet they are vastly different in their Rise,
and as different in their Degrees of Excellency. For the Creatures originate
solely from, and are purely dependent upon, the Will of GOD, for whose Pleasure
they are, and were created Rev. iv. 11.;
who, as the Apostle informs us, Ephesians. i. 11.
works all Things according to the Counsel of His own Will; though His
infinite Wisdom, and Goodness, as well as His Power, accompanied his Will in
the Formation of them: But, upon Supposition of a moral Agent, capable of
Obedience, the Divine Commandment necessarily results from the Nature of GOD
itself, considered in all His adorable Perfections, and not from the Will of
GOD only. GOD could have chose whether He would have made a World of Creatures,
or no; there was nothing, out of Himself, to move Him thereunto; it was the
pure Act of His Will; and it was dependent upon his Will, of what Order and
Kind of Beings, to make them, and what Capacities, Powers and Virtues, to
furnish them withal: But, when he had made a Number of rational Agents, it was
not solely dependent upon His Will, and Pleasure, whether This, or That should
be His Commandment, or no; (I mean now, more especially, the Moral Precepts;)
because, it naturally, and necessarily, flows from the essential Holiness,
Justice, Truth, Goodness, etc. of the Divine Nature, that if there be a
Creature capable of yielding a rational Homage and Service to the Supreme
Being, the Divine Commandment must necessarily be what it is. So that the
Commandment necessarily partakes of all the Divine moral Excellencies and
Perfections, and in the highest Degree, and is no other than the Divine Mind
manifested to us in His Word, or GOD Himself subsisting in His Law.

As the Commands of a Man, were he always true to himself, (which GOD ever is)
would be the fairest Image of the intellectual Part of the Man, and let us see
his Excellencies and Defects, much more truly, and clearly, than any of the
Operations of his Hands; so the Commandment of GOD is the highest, unbegotten
Image of the Divine Nature, because the essential Veracity of GOD necessitates,
that the Commandment give us a true Representation of the Divine Mind, and be
like GOD Himself, excellent as He is; so that the Characters of the Deity are
more deeply engraven upon His Law, than upon all the Creatures. Hence it is
that the Commandment is said to be Holy, Just and Good, Romans vii. 12.
as partaking of the Divine Holiness, Justice, Goodness; (as well as requiring
them of us) that is, as partaking of the Divine Nature. Though the invisible
Things of GOD are clearly seen from the Creation of the World, being understood
by the Things that are made, even His eternal Power, and Godhead; Romans i. 20.
that is, the Works of Creation plainly manifest that there is some First
Cause, who gave Being unto all Things, and therefore existed before all Things,
and so is eternal, and who is uncontrollable in Power, though this Eternity,
and Omnipotence of the Divine Being, clearly appears from the Things that are
made, yet in the Commandment of GOD, we have a clear and full Discovery, not
only of the Existence of GOD, but of the Nature, Excellencies and Perfections,
of this GOD, so far as our finite Minds can make any Discoveries of that which
is Infinite: and by this it is that we plainly see that He is an ALLPERFECT ONE.
Thus the Commandment, being the bright Image of the supreme Intellect, is it
self perfect like Him; so that here it is that, as in a Glass, we all with open
Face, or in the fullest Light, behold the Glory of the Lord, as the Apostle
expresses it. 2. Cor. iii. 18.


I am sensible that there is what we call moral Good and Evil, resulting, as we
say, from the Nature of Things, or rather from the Relation, and Dependence, of
rational Creatures; and that there is no Possibility of altering, and changing,
the moral Nature of them, but they are so stubborn and inflexible, as that,
That which is morally Good, always was, and always will be, Good, and that
which is morally Evil, ever was, and will be, Evil: But then I can by no Means
suppose, that moral Good, and Evil, are any distinct Things independent on GOD,
His Nature, and Will, and, as such, have an Influence upon the Divine Will, in
determining this shall, or shall not, be a Law unto rational Creatures; because
this would be to suppose something antecedent to, separate from, and having the
Supremacy over, the Divine Being. I conceive, rather, that moral Good, and
Evil, are founded in the Purity of divine Nature, and, when considered in the
Creature, are no other than the Parity, or Disparity of the Actions of rational
Agents, (so and so related) to the divine Nature, or their Agreement or
Disagreement, to the Holiness and Purity of GOD; which Agreement is what the
holy GOD ever wills concerning them. And therefore when we consider moral
Good and Evil, for the Direction of our Actions, that we may shun the one, and
choose the other, it will not be so proper for us to say, that This is morally
Good, and therefore GOD cannot but will it, as that GOD has willed This,
therefore it is morally Good; because it is much easier for us to look into the
plain divine Commandment, and see what agrees with it, than to look into the
unsearchable divine Nature, and compare all Things, that fall under our
Consideration, therewith, and see how far they agree, or disagree, with it: so
that, to us, GOD's willing of a thing rendereth it morally Good, and His
prohibiting of it, morally Evil. The intrinsic moral Goodness, or Evil, of
Actions, is from the eternal Law of Nature; as they express it, who seem to aim
at setting up something, distinct from GOD Himself, to give Law to the First
Cause. But I would ask, what is this eternal Law of Nature? What, after all our
Search, but the Will of GOD, resulting from His Nature? or, the Law of the GOD
of Nature? A Law flowing directly, and upon Supposition of moral Agents,
necessarily, from the Nature, and Perfections, of the Deity; and therefore is
the fairest Transcript, the clearest Character, and brightest Manifestation of
the Divine moral Perfections.

Thus because the Commandment has GOD for it is Author, and originates from Him,
in another, and more excellent Manner, than the Creatures do, necessarily
flowing from the Perfections of the Divine Nature, and not purely from the Will
of GOD, therefore it partakes of His glorious Excellencies; and whilst the
Perfection of the Creature is limited and finite, the divine Commandment is
exceeding broad.

II. The Commandment of GOD will appear exceeding broad, and very excellent, if
we consider the Nature of it, the Subject Matter of it, or what this
Commandment is. And there are several Things, respecting the Nature, and
Subject Matter of the divine Commandment, which greatly discover to us the
transcendent Excellency of it; as, the Aspect it has upon the Honor of the
Lawgiver, and the Welfare of the obedient Subject, the Suitableness of it to
the Capacity of Man, and its comprehending the whole of our Duty in it.

1. It shows the exceeding Breadth of the divine Commandment, that it is most
perfectly adjusted both to the Lawgiver, and the obedient Subject, to advance
the Honor of the One, and promote the Welfare of the other. Thus it is most
perfectly calculated to advance the Honor of GOD, the supreme Lawgiver, to
raise in our Minds the most august and honorable Thoughts of Him, and lead us
to the most reverend, and profound Submission, and Obedience, to Him; that GOD,
in all Things, may be glorified by us. In what sublime Majesty does He appear,
when GOD said, Let there be Light; and there was Light? Genesis i. 3.
With what Awe and Reverence does it strike us, when He prefaces His Law,
saying, Exodus xx. 2.
I am the LORD thy GOD? Can we hear Him saying, Isa. xlv. 18.
Thus says the LORD that created the Heavens, GOD Himself that formed the
Earth, and made it, -- I am the LORD, and there is none else? or read His Name,
The great, the mighty, and the terrible GOD Neh. ix. 32.,
and not be filled with admiring, and adoring Thoughts of Him? This indeed is
the great and ultimate End of all the divine Revelations to us, to impress our
Minds with the Awe of GOD, and excite us to praise and honor, to obey and
serve Him: And, subordinate hereunto, it consults the true Interest of the
humane Nature, and aims at our Welfare, considered in public Societies, and in
our private Capacity, both in this World, and for ever in the next: As we shall
see afterward more fully under some of the following Heads.

Here humane Laws often fail, and a Licurgus, or a Solon, have not been able to
give such a well digested Body of Laws, as fully to answer all the Ends of
Government; but, after all their Care, there has been left some wide Chasms,
through which, the Sovereign's Honor, on the one Hand, or the Subjects Good,
on the other, have been struck at, and deeply wounded. Whereas the Commandment,
considered as the Law of GOD, is every Way perfect and complete, so that it
wants not the least Iota to render it an absolutely perfect Body of Laws, most
wisely adjusted to those great Ends of Government I have named, and the least
Derivation from it, or Addition to it, would mart the Perfection of the whole.
Hence it is, that, in the Conclusion of the sacred Volumn, we are told, Rev.
xxii. 18, 19.
If any Man shall add unto these things, GOD shall add unto him the Plagues
that are written in this Book; and if any Man shall take away from the Words of
the Book of this Prophecy, (which may well be understood of the whole sacred
Revelation, as truly as of that by John,) GOD shall take away his Part out of
the Book of Life. Because this would be a Man's presumptuous calling in
Question the Perfections of GOD, and an arrogating unto himself the Honor of
being able to give a more perfect Body of Laws.

2. The Excellency of the divine Commandment appears, in it is being exactly
suited to the Nature, and Capacity, of those who owe Obedience to it. Thus it
treats the intelligent Creature in a Way suitable to his rational Nature, and
requires nothing of him but what his own Reason and Understanding, under a due
Improvement, readily consents to, and approves of, as just, and equitable; and
what the Relation, which, as such a Creature, he stands in unto, and the
Dependence he has upon, GOD, the great Creator, necessarily demands of him.
Hence we find the Almighty making His Appeal to the Reason of Mankind, in all
that He requires of them, Isa. i. 18.
Come now, and let us reason together, says the Lord; cease to do Evil, and
learn to do well. And what can be more rational than that we should do no Evil,
but learn to do well? And this is the Sum of what all the divine Commandment
requires of us. Thus also GOD addressed His People of old, to call them off
from the Service of Idols, that they might cleave to Him alone, Isa. xlvi. 8.
Remember this, and show your selves Men: as if He had said, do but act the
Part which becomes you, as rational Agents; I require no more of you; bring it
again to Mind, think closely, O ye Transgressors: Is it reasonable you should
rebel against your Maker, and your Sovereign? And so you find the Apostle,
Paul, styles the whole of our Duty to GOD but a reasonable Service, Romans xii. 1.
I beseech you, Brethren, by the Mercies of GOD, that ye present your Bodies, a
living Sacrifice, holy, and acceptable, which is your reasonable Service. That
is, a Service fitting and becoming you as reasonable Creatures, and what, in
the Exercise of your Reason, you cannot refuse; you must act contrary unto your
very Nature, as rational Beings, to deny unto GOD that which is His Due: So
admirably is His Commandment adjusted to your very Nature. So excellent is the
divine Commandment, in this Regard, that if the whole Body of intelligent
Creatures were to sit in Council, upon the framing such Laws as should be best
adapted to their Nature and Capacity, they would be able, under the utmost
Improvement of the most rectified Understanding, to give us but some faint
Sketches, (for it would be no more) of this well contrived, and thoroughly
digested Commandment, which GOD has given us in its Perfection.

Besides, the divine Commandment requires no more than what the reasonable
Creature has a Sufficiency of Power to perform. While Man was in his State of
Innocence, his Powers were every Way adequate and proportionable to the Service
required of him, nor did his sovereign Lord expect more from him than he was
able to do; and he might have maintained his Integrity, under all the
Allurements of Sense, and Suggestions of the Devil, if he had not chosen rather
to hearken to, and comply with, the Voice of the Tempter. And though it be
granted, That, since the original Apostasy, and Lapse of the humane Nature,
there is no Man but what has his Powers so very much weakened, as that, of
himself, he is not able to perform his Duty to GOD; (though his reasonable Mind
may still, in some Measure, consent to the Law of GOD, that it is good, yet he
finds not in the Might of his Hands to perform that which is good;) and there
is no Reason that the Law should be changed, in Compliance with the Weakness of
a Creature, who, by his own Default, has brought upon himself an Incapacity to
keep it, in its present Form; nevertheless, the Grace of GOD, according to the
grand Intention of rescuing the Creature from his Sin, and Misery, by a
glorious Mediator, has provided sufficient Strength for him, to enable him, in
some Measure, to will, and to do, the Things that are holy, just, and good.
Therefore we are told, Phil. ii. 13.
It is GOD which works in you, both to will, and to do. And since there is
Provision of supernatural Strength for him, that, by the Grace of GOD, he may
be enabled to keep the divine Commandment, and walk in the Path of Life, if,
after all, he will not improve the Advantage he has, it will be entirely his
own Fault; and he can have no just Cause to complain, that there is any
Iniquity in GOD, that his Ways are not equal, or that He is an hard Master, who
gathers where he has not strawed, and reaps where He has not sowed; nor will he
have Room to matter, that he would have done his Duty, but was not able; when
GOD Himself offers to assist him by His Holy Spirit. So that still the divine
Commandment is adapted to the Capacity of the obedient Subject, whether that
Capacity be natural, or adventitious to him; whether what GOD furnished him
with at his first Make, or what He offers to bestow upon him afterward. And
this is a necessary Part of the Excellency of the divine Commandment, to be
thus suited to the Nature, and Capacity, of the Subject, so as to be but a
reasonable Service, and what he is some Way or other able to perform.

But then,

3. Here lies very much of the exceeding Breadth of the divine Commandment,
that it requires the whole of our Duty, and that both to GOD and Man. Were it
defective in any Part of our Duty, either to our Creator, or our
Fellow Creatures, as all humane Laws are, in many Instances, it would not be
exceeding broad; but since He has showed thee, O Man, what does the Lord thy
GOD require of thee, and there is no Part of thy Duty, but what is fully
contained in the Commandment, therefore it is a most excellent, and perfect
Law. Particularly,

1. What can be more excellent, and perfect, than the divine Commandment is, as
it includes the whole of our Duty respecting GOD Himself? This shows us what we
are to believe concerning GOD, what is the Duty we owe to Him, and how this
Duty is to be performed by us.

First; This show us what we are to believe concerning GOD. The divine Being
was very much hid and obscured from the natural Reason of Mankind, under the
Power of the Apostasy; and therefore the Heathen World, what ever were their
Sentiments of the Existence of a GOD, had little or no Knowledge of the One,
True, supreme Deity; their Ignorance of whom laid the Foundations of that
Disposition, which we ever find in them, to Idolatry; and yet much less
Acquaintance had they with the Nature, and Perfections, of the true and living
GOD. But the divine Commandment has revealed to the World, to the Jewish
Nation first, and then unto the Gentiles, so much of the Nature and Perfections
of the One-True-GOD as was necessary for them to know. Not that this Revelation
has made such full Discoveries of the divine Nature to us, as are commensurate
to what GOD is in Himself, this Knowledge is too high and wonderful for us,
neither have we any Powers capable of receiving it; for thus GOD dwells in
Light which no Man can approach unto, whom no Man has seen, or can see 1 Timothy
vi. 16.
They are only the Back Parts of Himself, which GOD has manifested to us,
which yet afford us such a true Representation, and Resemblance, of his Nature
and Glory, as is more equal to our Capacity, and sufficient to influence us to
pay our Homage and Adoration to Him. And thus, by this most excellent
Commandment, GOD has showed us something of the Glories, and the Wonders, of
His Nature, the Perfections He is everlastingly possessed of, and the
mysterious Subsistence of the Godhead in Three Divine Persons, or that this One
GOD is, FATHER, SON, and HOLY GHOST; the Second of which is GOD manifest in
FLESH, having assumed the Nature of Man into a personal Union with Himself.
Hence it is that we are told, 1. Job. v. 7.
There are Three that bear Record in Heaven, the Father, and the Son, and the
Holy Ghost.

Some tell us, that this Verse is not to be found in a very ancient Copy. Be it
so. Certainly it is more reasonable to suppose that it was an Omission in the
Transcriber, than to imagine that it was interpolated by Transcribers in all
other Copies; as it is more reasonable to correct a single Copy or two, by the
general Run of Copies, than to correct all the Rest by a single One; especially
in an Instance where the Generality of Copies agree in the same Sentiments,
fully expressed in other Parts of the Writings; which is the Case here. For if
this Text were not to be found in any of our Bibles, yet there are so many
others that assert, that there is but One GOD, and that this GOD is, FATHER,
SON, and HOLY GHOST, equally the Object of our religious Worship, equally
possessed of the divine incommunicable Perfections, and yet distinct in their
Operations, that we may with a very good Warrant assert a TRINITY in UNITY: nor
know I of any Disadvantage, that can justly be supposed to arise; from our
calling the Father, the Son, and the Holy Ghost, three distinct Persons, when,
at the same Time, we so plainly declare against a Plurality of Effences, and
assert the Unity of the Godhead: especially seeing we have no Word in our
Language that will convey to our Minds the Distinction, that the sacred
Scriptures give us, between the Father, Son, and Holy Ghost, so well as the
Word Person does; though yet we do not conceive of it, when applied to a divine
Person, in that Latitude in which we understand it when it is used about an
humane Person.

But to go on; as the Word of GOD sets before us the one GOD, as Father, Son,
and Holy Ghost, so it acquaints us with GOD the SON His condescending to take
upon Him our Nature, that He might accomplish the great Work of a Mediator,
which He had undertaken for us. Therefore we read, Job. i. 14.
The Word was made Flesh, and dwelt among us, and we beheld his Glory, the
Glory as of the only begotten of the Father. Both the Excellencies of the
divine Nature, and the Mysteries relating thereto, had forever lain beyond our
View, if divine Revelation had not made them known unto us: so that we may say
of them, (as CHRIST said to Peter, when he made that glorious Confession of
him, Thou art CHRIST, the SON of the living GOD,) Matthew. xvi. 17.
Flesh and Blood has not revealed it unto thee, but my Father which is in
Heaven. Thus by the divine Commandment, or Word, we are taught, that GOD is,
and that He is a Rewarder of them that diligently seek Him, that He is Father,
Son, and Holy Ghost, infinite, eternal, unchangeable, in His Being, Wisdom,
Power, Holiness, Justice, Goodness, and Truth. With Respect hereto GOD said to
His People of old, Isa. xliii. 10, 11, 12.
Ye are my Witnesses, says the Lord, -- that ye may know, and believe me, and
understand that I am He: Before me there was no GOD formed, neither shall there
be after me; I, even I am the Lord, and beside me there is no Savior; I have
declared, -- and have showed, -- therefore ye are my Witnesses, says the Lord,
that I am GOD. And thus said John the Divine, John xx. 31.
These Things are written that ye might believe that JESUS is the CHRIST, the
SON of GOD. And I may add, that This leads us into the Faith, that GOD framed
the Worlds by His Word, so that Things which are seen were not made of Things
which do appear; and that this GOD upholds, and governs, the World of
Creatures, which He has made, and directs, and influences them, in all their
Actions; and that, to Him, we, and all rational Creatures, must be accountable,
as to our Judge, and receive our final Rewards from Him.

Secondly; This shows us what is the Duty we owe to this GOD. The Commandment
not only shows us what ought to be our Conceptions of the divine Majesty, but
what is the Homage, Service, and Allegiance, which naturally results from the
Perfections of the Deity, and His Threefold Relations, as well as from the
divine Will. I say Relations, not as respecting us only, but as they are
founded in the divine Nature, as the Father relates to the Son, and the Son
unto the Father, etc. which necessarily implies a Distinction in those that
stand so related, so that the one is not the other, in the State in the which
they are related, and yet the Relation hinders not the Unity of the divine
Essence. Here we learn that this GOD is to be loved by us supreamly, and to be
feared before all that are called Gods; that He is to be acknowledged by us, as
our GOD, by our daily fervent Supplications, and our hearty and thankful
Praises; that His Law is to be observed by us as the Rule of our Life, and His
governing Providence to be entirely and humbly submitted unto; that we are to
reverence His Name, and Word, and Ordinances, sanctify His Day, and observe His
Institutions; and that He, and He only, is to be religiously worshipped and
adored by us.

This teaches us, that the First Person in the adorable Trinity, is to be
