acknowledged by us as the Father of all Things, the Author and Contriver of the
whole Method of our Salvation; and as such our Offerings are to be brought unto
His Altar, our Bodies and our Spirits are to be devoted to His Service, and His
holy Name is forever to be praised by us: that the Second glorious Subsistence
in the Deity, united to our Nature, and, in it, working out everlasting
Righteousness for us, is firmly to be believed in, as the promised Messiah, the
Son of GOD, sincerely chosen by us as our Surety, and Days-Man, unfeignedly
accepted of as our Savior, heartily beloved by us as our great Reconciler, and
humbly adored as the Purchaser of all our Happiness: that the Third Person in
GOD, even the Holy Ghost, is to be glorified by us, by our earnest seeking to
Him for His Gifts, and Graces, His Comforts and Joys, by submitting to His
Teaching, and Conduct, and by our cherishing all His holy Motions in our Souls,
and to be worshipped as making Application of eternal Redemption, and all the
blessed Benefits thereof, unto us.

Thirdly; The exceeding Breadth of the divine Commandment is seen, in the
Manner of our Performance of our Duty and Homage unto GOD; in that it requires,
that all our Worship, and Obedience, be performed in the highest, sublimest,
and most spiritual Manner, that possibly can be: that we not only offer unto
GOD the Calves of our Lips, and serve him with bodily Exercise, which alone
profits but little, but that we offer to him our very Hearts, and Souls,
which must be seriously engaged in every religious Duty we attend upon. For
CHRIST himself has told us, Job. iv. 23, 24.
The true Worshipers shall worship the Father, in Spirit, and in Truth; for the
Father seeks such to worship Him: GOD is a Spirit, and they that worship Him:
GOD is a Spirit, and they that worship Him must worship Him in Spirit, and in
Truth.

Besides; the Duty required of us forever exceeds the utmost Exactness of our
Performance. Though, through the perfect Obedience of One Man many are made
righteous, and our sincere, but imperfect, Services, are acceptable unto GOD,
through JESUS CHRIST, yet we are not able to see to the whole of our Duty, much
less to perform it; for we know but in Part, and therefore can do but in Part.
We may, in Part, know what is our present Duty, but the more exact we are in
our Obedience to the divine Commandment, we shall but the more plainly see,
that there is still wanting a more perfect Conformity to it, ever we can fully
answer it: So that it is ever an Height, which, when we have gradually
ascended as high as we can reach, in our present State of Imperfection, we
shall still be vastly below the Top of. Hence it is, that Christians are
commanded to grow in Grace 2 Pet. iii. 18.
for there is perpetually Room, and Occasion, for their Growth; and no Man is
so Good, but he may, and ought to be Better. Thus after our greatest Progress
toward Perfection, in the Duties of the Christian Life, we must never come to
a Stand, and think that we have already attained all that is required of us,
but forgetting those things which are behind, we must still reach forward, unto
those things which are before pressing toward the Mark, for the Prize of the
high Calling, which is of GOD, in Jesus Christ, our Lord Phil. iii. 13, 14.
.

2. How exceeding broad is the divine Commandment, as it includes the whole of
our Duty respecting Man? For it requires all possible Duty from us, both
respecting ourselves, and our Fellow Creatures, in the private, and social
Life; without omitting the least Instance, wherein we could conduct ourselves
with greater Prudence, and Advantage to our own Comfort, or with greater
Decency, and Usefulness, unto humane Society. The sacred Volume is full of
Rules, Laws, and Orders, for the Regimen and Government of ourselves, our
Appetites, and Passions, and for our regular Behavior toward one another; and
requires of us, that we deny Ungodliness and worldly Lusts, and live soberly,
and righteously, as well as godly, in this present World Tit. ii. 12.
that we mortify our Members which are upon the Earth, Fornication,
Uncleanness, inordinate Affection, evil Concupiscence, and Covetousness Col.
iii. 5.
: that no Man go beyond and defraud his Brother, in any Matter 1 Thessalonians. iii. 6.
: that we put away Lying, and speak the Truth every Man with his Neighbor;
that we be angry and sin not, nor let the Sun go down upon our Wrath; that be
that stole steal no more; that no corrupt Communication proceed out of our
Mouth; that all Bitterness, and Wrath, and Anger, and Clamor, and Evil
Speaking, be put away from us, with all Malice Ephesians. iv. 25 -- 31.
: that we put on, as the Elect of GOD, Bowels of Mercies, Kindness, Humbleness
of Mind, Meekness, Longsuffering; forbraring one another, and forgiving one
another; -- that above all, we put on Charity, which is the Bond of Perfectness
Col. iii. 12, 13. 14.
: that we recompense no Man Evil for Evil; but, if it be possible, as much as
in us lies, to live peaceably with all Men Romans xii. 17, 18.
.

But it would be to transcribe a very great Part of our Bible to enumerate all
the Rules of Sobriety, and Meekness, of Justice, and Temperance, Benevolence
and Charity, and the Duties of our several Relations, in the Church, in the
State, and in the Family, which the divine Commandment lays before us; I shall
therefore omit any further mentioning of them; and only observe, that,

The Commandment of GOD challenges the Superiority, and Precedence to all other
Laws, upon this Account, in that it requires all that is necessary to our own
personal Benefit, and the Welfare of the Community. Hence it is styled good and
perfect Romans xii. 2.
. The Laws of Men have no Tendency to this End, any further than they are
founded upon the divine Law: And all the Laws which the ablest Politicians have
enacted, cannot answer this End a Thousandth Part so well as the Laws of GOD; as
is plainly seen, in that the better Christian any Man is, (caeteris paribus)
the more worthy Member is he of the Commonwealth.

Thus the Commandment, which shows us the whole of our Duty, that we do justly,
love Mercy, and walk humbly with our GOD, appears, in its Nature, and
Subject Matter of it, to be exceeding broad.

III. The Commandment of GOD will appear to be exceeding broad, if we consider
the Extent of its Object. We see that it is a most excellent Law subjectively
considered, or what is the Subject Matter of it, namely, the whole of our Duty,
both to GOD, and Man, and no less excellent will it appear if we view it
objectively, as it reaches to every Individual among the Children of Men, and
to all of Man. There is no Man but what owes Obedience to it, and no Part of
Man but what is under the Obligation thereof.

1. The divine Commandment extends to every individual Person, among the
Children of Men. However humane Laws may make a Difference between Man and Man,
and be too much like the Spider's Web, which catches the lesser Flies, while
the greater easily break through, it is certain the divine Commandment has no
Respect unto Persons, but is equally calculated for, and enjoined upon, all
Mankind, under like Circumstances, and includes every individual Person under
the Bonds of it. Hear the Conclusion of the whole Matter, the Sum of all that
has been heard from the sacred Code. Fear GOD, and keep His Commandments; for
this is the whole of Man Eccl. xii. 13.
. It Is the whole of every Man, or what every Man, even the whole Race, or Body
of Mankind, stand bound unto; the whole of their Duty, and their whole
Happiness, is laid up in it. The Monarch, who sits upon his Throne, swaying his
Scepter, and gives forth his Orders, and governs his Subjects by his Nod, is
equally obliged to bow down his Head, and submit himself to the Authority of
the great GOD, the supreme ruler of the Universe, as the meanest Vassal that
attends his Footstool. Be wise now therefore, O ye Kings, be instructed, ye
Judges of the Earth; serve ye the LORD with Fear, rejoice with Trembling Ps.
ii. 10, 11.
. There is no Man so great, but GOD is infinitely greater; and He that is
higher than the highest demands Obedience from them, and will call them to an
Account. Men of the politest Learning, and strongest Reasoning, are required,
to give this as the greatest Proof of their Wisdom and Knowledge, to reverence,
and obey their Maker. Nor are the Ignorant and Unlearned, excused from their
Obedience to their high Sovereign; for even they know enough of the divine
Commandment to stop their Mouth, in the Day of Retribution, if they do it not.
Some, indeed, have clearer, and fuller, Discoveries made to them, of the divine
Will concerning them, than others; and whilst some grope in the dark, feeling
out their Way, by the Use of their natural Powers, others have superadded
thereunto the Light of Revelation, which, like the Sun shining in its Strength,
renders it clear Day with them; so that these have the Advantage, doubtless, of
knowing more of the divine Will, than those can reach unto by the highest
Improvement of their natural Reason: nevertheless, all Men are alike under
Obligations to obey the Commandment of GOD, so far as they know it to be his
Commandment; nor will any Man ever be faulted for not yielding Obedience to a
Command which he was wholly, and unavoidably, ignorant of; because it can be no
Law to him, not, that will not, but, that cannot, know it, for Romans iv. 15.
where there is no Law there is no Transgression. Those, that have only their
natural Reason to direct them, owe Obedience to the divine Commandment, so far
as they are able to find out what is the divine Will concerning them; and
those, that enjoy Revelation, are under Obligations to a further Obedience to
all that That Revelation requires of them. Hence it is, that where the
Revelation of the divine Mind is enjoyed, GOD has now commanded all Men every
where to repent Act. xvii. 30.
: and that while they have the Light, they should believe in the Light Joh.
xii. 36.
; and that all Men should honor the Son as they honor the Father Joh. v. 23.
. So that this is the Homage, and grateful Sacrifice, which Kings of the Earth,
and all People, Princes, and all Judges of the Earth, Young Men, and Maidens,
Old Men, and Children Ps. cxlviii. 11, 12.
, owe to their great Creator, and his Law alike extends to them all.

2. The divine Commandment extends to all of Man, to our whole Nature, and to
all our Powers, and Capacities. It reaches the Body of Man, and aims at the
Government of every Member, and every Power belonging to it; that we do not
yield our Members Instruments of Unrighteousness unto Sin, but yield ourselves
unto GOD, and our Members as Instruments of Righteousness unto GOD Romans vi. 13.
. It extends to all our secular Interests, Possessions, Employments, and
Recreations, and directs us in our Pursuit, Enjoyment, and Improvement, of
them. And it reaches to the very Soul, and requires the Obedience of the inner
Man of the Heart, and means to direct, and influence, us, in all our spiritual,
and eternal Interests. Thus it calls upon us, 1 Cor. vi. 20.
glorify GOD, in your Body, and in your Spirit, which are GOD's.

And here lies very much of the Excellency of the Commandment of GOD, that it
is obligatory upon the Conscience, which no humane Laws can be, only as they
evidently accord with the divine; and then, not because they are established by
the Authority of Man, but, because they derive their Authority from the supreme
Lord of all. So that whatever Laws may be enacted by the civil Power, which, to
our Reason and Understanding, improved and regulated, by an humble, modest,
diligent Search into the Word of GOD, appear to have such a Disagreement with
the divine Law, as renders it sinful, in our Apprehension, for us to comply
with them, we may, by no Means, so yield up our Consciences to the Wills of
Men, as to submit our selves to them, but must choose, rather, to obey GOD, than
Man, let the Event be what it will. Therefore when the holy Apostles were
enjoined, by humane Authority, to do what clashed with the divine Command, they
boldly make a Stand, in the very Face of the Civil, as well as Ecclesiastical
Rulers, and made an Appeal to their own Consciences too, saying, Act. iv. 19.
whether it be right in the Sight of GOD, to hearken unto you, more than unto
GOD, Judge ye. And one would think, that there were no great Difficulty in
determining, whether we ought to obey GOD, or Man.

And, because all acceptable religious Worship is appointed by GOD alone, who
only knows what is grateful and pleasing to himself, therefore, any Modes, and
Forms, of Worship, not directly appointed by him, or not deducible, by plain
and natural Consequence, from the general Rules he has prescribed, I say, all
such Rites, and Modes, not founded upon the divine Commandment, ought to be
rejected by us, whatever be the humane Authority that enjoins them, or the
Pretensions to Order, and Decency, in the observing of them. Hence we may
observe, that the inspired Apostle blames the Colossians, for their Fondness
for either Jewish, or Pagan Traditions, after their Conversion to the Christian
Faith: Col. ii. 20, 22.
If ye be dead with CHRIST, says he, -- Why are ye subject to Ordinaries, --
after the Commandment, and Doctrines of Men?

For Man has not, nor can he have, any Power over the Consciences, what ever he
may have over the Bodies, of Men: but God's Commandments direct and govern the
Consciences of all his rational Creatures. And though from the Dullness of our
Understandings, we may not be able, always, to see the Reason of what is
commanded us, yet, it is sufficient for us, that we know it to be the Will of
GOD concerning us; here our Reason ought to be superceeded by our Faith; and
the Commandment, from a Consciousness of the divine Supremacy, ought forever to
be obeyed by us.

I might add; that the Command of GOD extends to the perfected Spirits above,
and the glorious Angels bow down before it, even that Part of it which relates
to us, so far as it is suited to their Nature; they are his Angels, that do his
Commandment, hearkening to the Voice of his Word Ps. ciii. 20.
. The Excellency of the Commandment shines forth in it is Luster in it is being
so admirably adapted to the Natures of Men, and Angels, that while a poor
infirm Worm of the Dust is capable, in some Measure, by divine Assistance, of
yielding Obedience unto it, yet, it is so sublime, and lofty, as to exercise
the Obedience of the highest Angels in Heaven.

SERMON V.
PSALM CXIX. 96. I have seen an End of all Perfection; but thy Commandment is
exceeding broad.


THERE have been two Doctrines proposed to be spoken to from these Words,
namely,

Doc. I. The Perfection of the Creature is limited, and finite.

Doc. II. The Commandment of GOD is exceeding broad.

The last Opportunity I made some Entrance upon the Second of these Doctrines;
and having observed, that, by the Commandment, I understand, the whole revealed
Will of GOD, I proposed to show the Excellency thereof, beyond any Thing that
is to be found upon the Creature, by considering,

I. The Original of it. II. The Subject Matter of it. III. The Extent of it
objectively. IV. The great End and Design of it. And V. Its Duration.
Under the first of these, viz.

I. The Original of the Commandment, I have considered our Bible, as containing
a sure Revelation of the Mind of GOD; and this Mind of GOD, so made known to
us, does not result, purely, from the divine Will and Pleasure, as the
Existence of all Creatures does, but from the Perfections of the divine Nature,
and therefore in this Regard, partakes of those divine Excellencies far above
what is to be found upon any mere Creature. Under the Second Head, viz.

II. The Subject Matter of the Commandment; I have considered the Excellency of
it, as perfectly adjusted to the Divine Lawgiver, and to the obedient Subject;
as being exactly suited to the Nature and Capacity of those that owe Obedience
to it; and as it requires the whole of our Duty, both to GOD, and Man. Under
the Third,

III. The Extent of the Commandment objectively, I have showed its Excellency
in that it reaches to every individual Person without Exception, and to our
whole Nature, Body, and Spirit. And I proceed to the Consideration of the
Fourth Head proposed, viz.

IV. The Commandment of GOD will appear exceeding broad, if we consider the
great and glorious End and Design of it; what GOD intends it for, and what it
is improvable unto. The great Excellency and Perfection of all Laws, and
Commandments, are to be seen, chiefly, in the End which they aim at, and the
direct Tendency, Influence, and Power, which they have for the Attainment of
this End. Now, the divine Commandment aims at the highest, and noblest End,
that possibly can be, namely, the Glory of GOD, and our best Good, both in this
World, and in that which is to come, in Time, and throughout Eternity: this is
what GOD designs it for, what it is improvable unto, and what it has a direct
Tendency to promote.

I shall not, here, enter into a distinct Consideration of this great and noble
End, the Glory of GOD, because I have already spoken something to it, under a
former Head, and because this is ever answered, in the Accomplishment of the
great Design respecting Man; the Purity, and Happiness of Mankind, being so
closely connected to the Glory of GOD, that in what Way soever the First is
brought about, by the same Means, and in the same Method, the divine Glory is
also displayed, and made to shine forth in it is greatest Luster. I shall
therefore confine myself unto such Thoughts, as show us the original Intention,
and peculiar Adaptedness, of the divine Commandment, to perfect our Nature, and
render us completely happy; wherein it infinitely transcends all the Excellency
that is to be found upon the Creatures, which every Way fall short of this End;
as I have already proved. And I shall take a View of the excellent Design of
the divine Commandment, under these Three Heads, 1. To make us truly Wise. 2.
To make us really Good. 3. To make us completely Happy.


1. One great End and Design of the divine Commandment is, to make us truly
wise. The Commandment has a very great Influence upon the making of us wise for
the Things of this World, and therefore may well be looked upon as excellent by
us; because, as we value ourselves upon our Reason, which raises us above the
Level of the Brute, so our Wisdom is the highest natural Exercise of our
Reason, and is that which gives any Man the Preference to his Neighbors. That
the divine Commandment is of this Advantage to us, is apparent, in that it
tends to brighten our Understandings, and recover them from those Prejudices,
with which our Lusts and Passions very much cloud, and darken the Mind; by
which Means, it renders our Apprehensions, and Conceptions, of Things more
clear, and distinct, that we may be enabled to see them in a better Light, and
discern them more thoroughly: Thus it enobles our rational Powers, and assists
them to choose out a right Way for us. For while the Word of GOD is, a Lamp unto
our Feet, and a Light unto our Path, we shall not only take the more Heed to
our Ways, and walk with Caution and Circumspection, and so be among the
well-advised, with whom is Wisdom, but we shall have a more full and plain
Discernment of the Path of Understanding, and clear Discovery of the Way, in
the which we should go; and thus be assisted to act like rational, and prudent
Creatures, who are not led blindfold, by Passions, and Prejudices, but, govern
themselves by the Dictates of right Reason. Hence, when Moses had set the Law
of GOD before the Children of Israel, said he, Deuteronomy. iv. 6.
Keep, therefore, and do them; for this is your Wisdom, and Understanding, in
the Sight of the Nations, which shall hear all these Statutes, and say, surely
this great Nation is a wise, and understanding People. This also made the
Psalmist say, Ps. cxix. 98, 99, 100.
Thou, through thy Commandment, have made me wiser than mine Enemies; for they
are ever with me: I have more Understanding than all my Teachers; for thy
Testimonies are my Meditation: I understand more than the Ancients; because I
keep thy Precepts. Thus a due Regard to the Commandment will influence us to
walk wisely, and surely, and help us to shun many Inconveniences, which we
should be apt, otherwise, to run ourselves into, through the Prevalency of our
too eager Passions, and unbridled sensual Appetites.

But however; The great End of the divine Commandment is, to make us
spiritually wise, which is the truest, and highest, Wisdom, and which, when all
is done, will be found to be most serviceable unto us. We are therefore told,
Ps. cxi. 10.
The Fear of the Lord is the Beginning of Wisdom; a good Understanding have all
they that do his Commandment. For no Man begins to be truly wise, until, by the
Fear of GOD prevailing in his Heart, he is influenced unto a conscientious
Regard to the divine Commandment, the Pathway whereof is pleasant, and the End
Peace. If thou be wise, thou shall be wise for thy self, said Solomon Prove.
ix. 12.
. This is true Wisdom, for a Man to be wise for himself, for his best Interest,
and his latter End; and all Pretensions to Wisdom, short of this, is but acting
for a wrong End, and to no good Purpose, the Folly of which will appear, in the
Disappointment, and Confusion, which will be the certain Issue of it. For let a
Man be ever so wise, in his Projections, and the Methods which he takes, to
promote some little Interest, that has no Relation to him, he will be found, to
be but a Fool, in the Conclusion, for his Neglect of himself, and suffering his
main Interest to run to Ruin, for want of his seasonable, and prudent, Care
about it: or, let him provide, for his present Comfort, with the finest
Schemes, and most diligent Application, yet, if he has been wholly negligent of
Futurity, and must remain, the latter Part of his Existence, utterly destitute
of every thing that would be comfortable to him, he will find, at his End, that
he has been a Fool. Now, the Design of the divine Commandment is, to correct
this Folly; and it has a very powerful Influence to cure us hereof, by
acquainting us, where our true Interest lies, and what are the best Methods to
promote it; by making us considerate, and thoughtful, about our own State and
Condition, and how it will fare with us in the End of Days; and by exciting of
us dilligently to improve the Means, that are necessary to secure what is of
the greatest Consequence to us, that it may not only be well with us for the
present, but that our latter End may be Peace. The Commandment is therefore
said, to be pure, enlightening the Eyes, Ps. xix. 7.
That is, the Eyes of the Mind, which are naturally o^^^^red, and clouded, by
the thick Mists, which our Fondness for Lust, and the World, cast before them,
so that they have no clear, and distinct, Perception of our ultimate End, and
the Way to it. The Commandment is a Lamp, and the Law is Light, and Reproofs of
Instruction are the Way of Life; said the wise Man Prove. vi. 23.
because by these we are taught our Duty, and Interest, and are led in the Path
of Life.

The divine Commandment affords us the Knowledge of spiritual and divine
Things, which are the most excellent in their Nature, and most beneficial unto
us. What is there so full, so lofty, so glorious, as the LORD our GOD is? Whose
Nature infinitely transcends all the Objects of Sense, in true Excellency, and
contains a Beauty, Reality, and Truth, in it, beyond all other Things that are
knowable by us; and therefore so much the more enlarges our Minds, and elevates
our Conceptions, in the Knowledge of Him: and inasmuch as this GOD is the
Fountain of all Good, therefore also the Mind in Closing with him, by our
practical Knowledge of Him, enjoys unspeakable Delight and Satisfaction in Him,
and becomes secured of His Favor; and thus reaps the highest Benefit, from
this most excellent Object, that our Nature is capable of. For by this Means,
we have taken all the Care of ourselves that we can do, have established our
main Interest upon a sure Foundation, and are provided with all that is
necessary for our future Well-being, yea, throughout an endless Eternity: and
this is true Wisdom, and Understanding, such Wisdom as is not to be attained
unto, by the Force of our own Powers, but by the divine Commandment. For the
natural Man receives not the things of the Spirit of GOD, for they are
Foolishness unto him; neither can be know them, because they are spiritually
discerned; how be it, we speak Wisdom, yet not the Wisdom of this World; but we
speak the Wisdom of GOD in a Mystery: -- but GOD has revealed them unto us by
his Spirit 1 Cor. ii. 6, 7, 10, 14.
. They are the Things of GOD, his glorious Perfections, his deep Counsels, his
merciful Designs, with all the Wonders of redeeming Love, and Grace, which lie
very much out of the Reach of our natural Powers, but the Spirit of GOD has
revealed them unto us; and it is the Design of the divine Commandment, to
acquaint us with those glorious Truths, and give us a just View of the things
of our Peace, and so fill us with the Knowledge of his Will, in all spiritual
Wisdom, and Understanding; and it has an happy Tendency, and Aptitude, so to
impress our Minds with them, as that we may ourselves receive the Benefit of
them.

Hence, it presents us with the melancholy Prospect of our own miserable State,
and Condition, by Nature; how enslaved we are unto diverse Lusts, and Passions,
captivated by Devils, included under Guilt, and liable unto Punishment, in this
World, and the next, great, and endless; and shows us, what absolute Need there
is of a Savior, to deliver us from all of this Infelicity, and directs us unto
JESUS CHRIST, the only Hope of Israel, and the Savior thereof.

Hence, it opens unto us the whole Method of Salvation by CHRIST, unfolds the
Mysteries of our holy Religion to us, tells us what we must do to be saved, and
offers divine Assistance to us, to enable us to walk in that Way which leads
unto true Life and Happiness.

Hence, it sets before us, the strong and alluring Arguments, and most powerful
Motives, fetched from the future, unseen, and eternal World; it presents us
with the View of the Crown of unfading Glory, which awaits the humble and
obedient Soul; and gives us a distant Sight of the Place of Torment, the
inexpressible Pain, Horror, and Anguish, which is reserved as the endless
Portion of the impenitent, and disobedient; and all to move us to act wisely,
and walk safely.

Thus Life, and Immortality, is brought to Light, through the Gospel 2 Timothy i.
10.
; and by this Means we come to know the only true GOD, and JESUS CHRIST, whom
he has sent; and so are made wise unto Salvation 2 Timothy iii. 15.
. This is the great End and Design of the divine Commandment, what GOD intends
it for, and what, if it be not our own Fault, we may improve it to. This is the
great Design of preaching the Word of GOD unto the World; as the Apostle tells
us it was the End of his Ministry, and equally is of ours, Act. xxvi. 18.
to open Men's Eyes, and turn them from Darkness to Light: and hence, when it
was prophesied of CHRIST, Isa. xlii. 6, 7.
I the Lord have called Thee in Righteousness, and will give Thee for a
Covenant of the People, for a Light of the Gentiles, it is particularly taken
Notice of, that one of the great Ends, and blessed Benefits, of that
Designation, is to open the blind Eyes. And give me me Leave to add upon it,
agreably to what our Savior remarked, when he read the Lesson, out of Isaiah
unto his Hearers, Oh! that, by our wise Improvement of it, it may be said of
us, Luke iv. 21.
This Day is this Scripture fulfilled among us. Thus, the Commandment of God
appears to be exceeding broad, in this noble and glorious Design of it, to make
us truly wise; to furnish us with the Knowledge of the best Things, and direct
our Feet in the Path of Understanding, to the securing of our Selves, and our
great and lasting Interest; which is such a Wisdom as highly becomes us, as
rational Creatures, and compared with which, all the Wisdom of this World is
but mere Foolishness.

I now proceed, to the Second Thing proposed, namely,

2. The glorious End and Design of the divine Commandment is, to make us really
Good. The infinitely wise GOD has given us his Commandment, not only to inform
our Judgment, and make us wise to know, but, to regulate our Practice, that our
Wisdom may evidence itself, by the proper genuine Fruits of it, in our Hearts,
and Lives. For all our Knowledge will be but to our Disadvantage, and render us
so much the more unhappy, if we are not careful to govern ourselves, in our
Practice, according to it: and therefore the Commandment aims, at the
rectifying of our Nature, and curing the Irregularities of our Behavior, and
so, to make us really good Men. When Mankind had universally sunk into
Infidelity, and Immorality, and were utterly destitute of the divine Life, then
it pleased GOD to make a Revelation of himself, and his Mind and Will unto the
World, gradually opening the Mysteries of the Kingdom of GOD, from the calling
of Abraham out of Ur of the Chaldees, until, in the Fullness of Time, the Light
shone with the greatest Clearness, by the Appearing of the SON of GOD in Flesh,
to instruct the World, personally, and by his Apostles that Mankind might be
recovered, in the Exercise of their Faith and Virtue, to a God-like Temper and
Disposition: which abundantly shows the superior Excellency of the divine
Commandment. Thus, particularly, it aims, at the begetting in us Faith in GOD,
and in his Son JESUS CHRIST, the converting of us from the Error of our Ways,
and to sanctify, and make us holy.

(1) The Design of the divine Commandment is, to work true Faith in us; that we
may live a Life of Faith in GOD, and in his Son JESUS CHRIST. Faith in GOD, as
the Maker, Ruler, and Judge, of the World, and in his Son, JESUS CHRIST, as the
only Redeemer of lost Mankind, and ours in particular, is the very Root and
Principle, of all Evangelical Goodness; without which, we can neither serve
GOD, nor find Acceptance with him. The Author of the Epistle to the Hebrews
therefore assures us, Heb. xi. 6.
without Faith it is impossible to please GOD; for he that comes unto GOD, (so
as to find Acceptance with him,) must believe that he is, and that he is a
Rewarder of them that diligently seek him. And CHRIST said to his Disciples,
and so to all that mean to receive any Benefit by him, Joh. xiv. 1.
Ye believe in GOD, believe also in ME. For he that does not believe that there
is a GOD, and that JESUS CHRIST is the Son of GOD, and Savior of the World,
cannot possibly live religiously; because all Religion turns upon the Belief of
a GOD, and That Religion only, which is acceptable and pleasing to GOD, is
founded in the Belief of JESUS CHRIST his being the promised Messiah, the Son
of GOD, and Savior of the World; this being the only Way in which GOD has
revealed Himself unto the World, and in which he will be worshipped, namely, by
his Son, JESUS CHRIST; which occasioned the Apostle's saying Joh. xx. 31.
These Things are written, that ye might believe that JESUS is the CHRIST, the
Son of GOD.

Whatever Difficulties any may imagine they find in believing JESUS CHRIST to
be the Son of GOD, in such a proper Sense of the Phrase as imports his
partaking of the same Nature with the eternal Father, because they cannot
comprehend the Manner of the divine Filiation, it is justly to be feared that
the great Bar which lies in their Way is, the Haughtiness, and Pride, of the
Hearts of Men, who cannot stoop to resign up their Understandings to the divine
Mind, as they must do, to credit a Report which contains Mysteries in it which
they are not able to unriddle; and that therefore it is they refuse to believe
what they cannot see through. For, after all, there is no such Absurdity in
believing Mysteries, or, believing such Doctrines as contain Mysteries in them,
as some Men would persuade us; because we are even forced to do so, in Nature,
and in Arts, whether we will or no. And, truly, I know of no more Difficulty,
in believing the Truth of a Proposition, clearly, and distinctly, expressed,
(that is, in such plain Terms as I fully understand,) when it is handed to me
by divine Revelation, (which Proposition, nevertheless, contains a Doctrine
that couches Mysteries in it, which I do not understand) than there is in
believing a clear Proposition, concerning any Thing in Nature, handed to me by
my Fellow Creature, when yet the Subject of that Proposition, or the Thing
spoken of, contains such Mysteries in it, as neither I, nor any Man living, are
able to explain. As, for Instance, all Bodies are endowed with a Power of
Gravitation: or, if you desire a more familiar one, The Sun gives Light.

Now, this is what the divine Commandment aims at, to produce this Faith in us,
in GOD, and CHRIST, as the vital Principle of all spiritual Life, and the
Spring of all our acceptable Obedience. Hence it declares to us the Being,
Perfections, Works, Dominion, and Will of GOD: Hence it sets JESUS CHRIST
before us, in all his amiable Excellencies, and altogether lovely, in the high
Concern he has expressed for our Welfare, and the wonderful Methods he has
taken to manifest his prevailing Love to us; it shows him to us, in all the
Charms, and Endearments, of a GOD incarnate, wounded for our Transgressions,
bruised for our Iniquities, and as having freely laid down his Life for us
miserable Sinners. Hence the Commandment so often urges this upon us, as our
indispensible Duty, that we believe in JESUS CHRIST, 1 John iii. 23.
This is his Commandment, that ye believe on the Name of his Son JESUS CHRIST.
Hence it uses the most powerful Motives, the weightiest Considerations, to
accomplish a Work of Faith in us. It gives us the fullest Evidence, the most
incontestible Testimony, of the Truth of the whole Gospel of CHRIST, and his
own Mission from the Father, as confirmed unto us by them that heard Him,
(assert his Mission, and deliver his Doctrines) GOD also bearing them Witness,
both with Signs, and Wonders, with diverse Miracles, and Gifts of the Holy
Ghost Heb. ii. 3, 4.
. So that there is no Room for us reasonably to doubt the Certainty of his
Mission from GOD, or, consequently, to suspect the Truth of the Doctrines, and
Precepts, which he has taught. It gives us full Proof of JESUS CHRIST his being
the ancient promised Messiah, the Son of GOD, the Prince of Peace, in the exact
Agreement of all the Characteristicks, spoken of in the old Testament, unto
him, and him only; as, the Time of his appearing in the World, the
Circumstances of his Appearance, the Description of his Person, by the
particular Events befalling him, the Contempt that should be poured upon him,
the Death he should submit to, his Triumphs over the Grave, the Extent, and
Glory, of his Kingdom; these, with many other Predictions concerning him,
having their exact Accomplishment in JESUS CHRIST, and in him only, are an
unquestionable Evidence of his being the true Messiah. And if CHRIST be the
true Messiah, and sent from GOD, we may be sure he has told us the Truth,
however sublime, and exceeding our Comprehension, the Doctrines he has taught
us may be. Because GOD, who perfectly knows all things, would send none upon
his Errand, and under the Character of HIS SON, especially, in so important an
Affair, wherein his own Glory, and the Happiness of Mankind, are so nearly
concerned, but such an One as would keep exactly to his Instructions, and
publish the Truth, the whole Truth, and nothing but the Truth. And all of this
full, and clear Evidence, which the Word of GOD affords us, of the Messiaship,
and Mission, of CHRIST is, to prevail upon us to credit the Report of the
Gospel, and submit ourselves unto the Government of it.

In short; without the Commandment, or revealed Will, of GOD, there can be
nothing of this Faith, which is so necessary to the religious and Christian
Life; and consequently, the Life of Man, here, would be little better than that
of the Brutes, and his Condition, hereafter, that of Devils: for, as the
Apostle well argues, Romans x. 14, 17.
how shall they believe in him of whom they have not heard? and how shall they
hear without a Preacher? -- So then Faith comes by hearing, and hearing by the
Word of GOD: which clearly evidences it to be the Design of the Commandment, to
beget Faith in us, that we may not remain in Infidelity, and Unbelief of GOD,
and his Son JESUS CHRIST, and so be destitute of the first moving Principle of
all real Goodness. Hence also, the same Apostle elsewhere observes, 2 Cor. iv.
3.
if our Gospel be bid, it is hid unto them that are lost: because they are
destitute of the ordinary, and proper Means, appointed by GOD, by which a true
and saving Faith is wrought in them. How far the Faith of the one supreme GOD,
resulting from the Works of his Hands, with a correspondent Care to please him,
according to a Man's natural Light, may avail to Acceptance with him, through
the Meditation of his Son, we are not able positively to determine; but we are
led by Revelation to suspend all Hope concerning such, as well as from the
general View of the World; the wise Man assuring us, where there is no Vision
the People perish Prove. xxix. 18.
.

(2.) The Design of the Divine Commandment is to convert the Soul. The
omnipotent, and wise Creator made all his Creatures Good, and therefore Man, a
moral Agent, morally Good; for it was impossible that his Creator should make
him vicious, without being himself either weak, or depraved, both of which are
Blasphemies of too high a Degree to be imputed to the infinitely Great, and
Holy GOD. But though GOD, at first, made Man morally good, and free from all
irregular Appetites, and Passions, yet he made him capable of being invaded by
them, and brought into Subjection to them: And accordingly, we see that humane
Nature, which once had the beautiful Image of GOD shining full upon it in
Knowledge, Righteousness, and Holiness, now greatly stained and polluted; so
that it may be said of all Men, whether Jew, or Gentile, as the Apostle speaks,
Romans iii. 23.
All have sinned, and come short of the Glory of GOD. The first Sin, of the
first Man, was what we call the Fall, the Fall of the humane Nature from its
GOD, and Happiness. I know there are some who admit of the Fall of the first
Man, according to the Account we have thereof, in the Beginning of our Bibles,
but imagine, and I think vainly, that all the Hurt done to the humane Nature
thereby is, that the Body has received some Damage, is weakened, and become
liable to Mortality. But I should look upon it as much more agreeable to
Reason, as well as Revelation, that the Soul, or Mind, the chief Agent in
Sinning, should be the chief Sufferer, in the Effects of it; and, as one Act of
Sin has turned Angels into Devils, so the Sin of the first Man has brought an
universal Disorder upon the whole humane Nature. By this Fall from GOD, the Man
has fallen from his Perfection, and greatly enfeebled, and debased his Nature,
and brought a Stain and Blemish upon it, by his Soul's being sunk under the
Power of corrupt, and vain Affections, and Lusts; by which Means, he has lost
the Image of his Maker, which was at first put upon him, and has contracted the
Likeness of the impute, the false, the malicious, and revengeful Spirit; and so
is become unfit, both, for the Service of the pure and holy GOD, and the
Enjoyment of him, until there is a blessed Change wrought in him, translating
of him, out of the Kingdom of Satan, into the Kingdom of GOD's dear Son.

For, that Heart which is naturally full of Sin, and Enmity against GOD, and
wholly bent to transgress his holy Law, must be first altered, changed,
renewed, by the Workmanship of the divine Spirit upon it, before it can
possibly be in a State of Friendship with GOD, or take Delight in doing his
Will; the Tree must be made Good, that the Fruit may be Good: And therefore it
is we are told, They that are in the Flesh, cannot please GOD Romans viii. 8.
; and, Except ye be converted, ye cannot enter into the Kingdom of Heaven.
Matthew. xviii. 3.


Now the great End and Design of the divine Commandment is, to accomplish this
beautiful, and glorious Change in the Soul of a Sinner, to recover him from the
Empire of Sin, and Satan, over him, to free him from the Dominion of his sordid
Lusts, and Passions, and vindicate him into the Liberties of the Sons of GOD,
that is, to make a new Creature of him, and restore him to that Perfection, and
Integrity, which he lost. The Psalmist therefore takes Notice of this, as the
End of the Commandment, and what stamps a peculiar Excellency upon it; Psalm.
xix. 7.
The Law of the LORD is perfect, converting the Soul.

This convinces the Sinner that he is so, and shows him the vile, and odious,
Nature of Sin, and what a mean and despicable Creature it renders him,
preposterous in his Views, irrational in his Actions, a Slave to more than
brutish Appetites, ever acting below himself, ever hurting and wounding
himself, and bringing Reproach, and Shame, upon himself; of all which, until he
has a through Sight and Sense, and feels something of the Smart and Pain, in the
Uneasiness of his Mind, at his Condition, he is never like to be a true
Convert. The first Thing in Conversion is, to bring the Sinner to a suitable
Conviction of his present wretched, miserable, Condition, by Reason of Sin. For
the Whole need not a Physician, but they that are sick Matthew. ix. 12.
. While a Man thinks himself to be whole, be he ever so sick, he is not
apprehensive of his Danger, and therefore is at no Pains to seek out for Help;
but when once he comes so much to himself, as, to feel himself sick, then a
Physician will be welcome to him, and he will be in earnest in seeking Help
from him, and in following his Directions, in Hope of a Cure. So the Soul must
first feel, perceive, and be thoroughly sensible, of its own sick, and dangerous,
Condition; that is, it must be thoroughly convinced of its own Sinfulness, and
the infinite Evil of Sin, that the Wrath of GOD comes upon the Children of
Disobedience; that is, it must see it self dead, and damned, in the Eye of the
Law, by Reason of Sin, before it will look to CHRIST for Help, or take any
Pains to alter its present Temper and Course. And this Conviction it is the
Design of the divine Commandment to bring the Sinner to.

Therefore you find the holy Apostle Paul, from his own Experience, assuring of
us, Romans vii. 9.
That he was alive without the Law once; that is, in his own Apprehension, all
was well with him, so stupidly ignorant was he of the Disorders of his own
Heart, and insensible of the Irregularity of his Actions, and what all would
end in, as that he knew nothing amiss in himself, and feared no Danger: But
(says he) when the Commandment came, Sin revived, and I died: That is, when the
exceeding broad Commandment was brought home to him, and appeared in its true
Light, and full Extent, then he saw the Life and Power of Sin in him, and what
a base and unreasonable Part he had been acting all his Life long, in
transgressing that holy and good Commandment; and he saw what was the Fruit,
and Wages, of Sin, that it exposed him to the Wrath and Curse of Almighty GOD;
and this was a full Conviction to him, that he needed a Change both, in the
Temper of his Mind, and in his State, otherwise he was a dead Man, dead in
Trespasses and Sins, and under a Sentence of Condemnation, as the just
Punishment of all his Folly.

Besides; the Commandment means not only, to give us a Sight of our Weakness,
and Disorder, but, effectually to recover us from under the Power of them; to
convince us of our Sin, and subdue it in us, to break us off from our Love to,
and Delight in, Vanity, and convert us from the Error of our Ways. Therefore it
publishes to us what is the positive Will and Pleasure of our high Sovereign,
that we may know what our Lord and Master requires of us; that GOD has
commanded all Men every where now to repent Acts xvii. 30.
; cast away from you all your Transgressions, whereby ye have transgressed, and
make you a new Heart, and a new Spirit Ezekiel. xviii. 31.
: And again, Wash ye, make you clean, put away the Evil of your Doings, from
before mine Eyes; cease to do evil, learn to do well. Isa. i. 16, 17.
Thus does the divine Commandment positively enjoin Repentance, and Renovation
of Heart, and Life, upon us: And, that it might carry the greater Force with
it, and work us into a Compliance with what it demands of us, it presses our
Duty upon us with the most moving Considerations, with the Hopes of Pardon, and
Mercy, from a gracious GOD, if we sincerely repent, and turn, from our evil
Ways; Isa. lv. 7.
Let the Wicked forsake his Way, and the unrighteous Man his Thoughts, and let
him return unto the Lord, and he will have Mercy on him, and to our GOD, for he
will abundantly pardon: And it threatens the most terrible Punishment, the most
amazing Misery, in Case we refuse to hearken to the Demand, and choose to go on
in our Sins; Romans ii. 6, 9.
That GOD will render Indignation, and Wrath, Tribulation, and Anguish, to
every Soul of Man that does Evil, of the Jew first, and also of the Gentile.
And that the Threatening might not lose its Force, by our vainly imagining, that
a good GOD will not be so severe upon us, but will be better to us than his
Word, he has let us know what he has already done unto sinning Angels, though a
more noble Order of Beings than our selves: That He has reserved them, in
everlasting Chains, under Darkness, unto the Judgment of the great Day. Jude
ver. 6.


Yea further; Through the Assistance of the divine Spirit, the Commandment
becomes effectual for the Conversion of the Sinner. Accordingly, the Apostle
says, 2 Cor. x. 4.
The Weapons of our Warfare are not carnal, but mighty, through GOD, to the
pulling down of strong Holds, casting down Imaginations, and every high Thing
that exalts it self against the Knowledge of GOD, and bringing into
Captivity, every Thought, to the Obedience of Christ. And when GOD gives Men up
to reprobate Minds, that the Word shall have no Power upon them to convert
them, it is by making their Hearts fat, and their Ears heavy, and by shutting
their Eyes, lest they see with their Eyes, and hear with their Ears, and should
understand with their Hearts, and should be converted. Isa. vi. 10.


And GOD has been pleased to honor his own Commandment, by making use of the
preaching of the Word, as the ordinary Means by which Sinners have been
converted; which made the Apostle say, Romans i. 16.
I am not ashamed of the Gospel of CHRIST; for it is the Power of GOD unto
Salvation, unto every one that believes. Thus by the Preaching of Peter, and
the other Apostles, at Pentecost, Act. ii. 37, 41.
about three Thousand were pricked at the Heart, and said, Men, and Brethren,
what shall we do? and they gladly received the Word, and were baptized. Thus
also, by the preaching of Paul, Act. xvi. 14.
the Lord opened the Heart of Lydia: that is, she became a real Convert, whose
Heart received the Word, and submitted to it. And this is ever the gracious
Design of the Word, wherever it comes, to turn Men from Darkness, to Light, and
from the Power of Satan, unto GOD, that they may be made really good Men.
Wherefore,

(3.) The Design of the divine Commandment is, to sanctify us, and make us
holy; to make us Partakers of the divine Nature, and influence us to live the
divine Life. Whereby is given unto us exceeding great and precious Promises,
that by these you might be Partakers of the divine Nature 2 Pet. i. 4.
. Holiness is the Glory of the divine Nature; Exodus xv. 11.
GOD is glorious in Holiness. Holiness, in us, is our Conformity unto the Image
of GOD, in Righteousness, Mercy, and Truth etc, and in our Love to all that is
good, and Hatred of all that is evil, and this is to be perfect, as our Father,
which is in Heaven, is perfect. This is that which the divine Commandment aims
at, and what it has a direct Tendency to produce in us, It does not mean to
convert us from Sin, and leave us in a State of Indifferency, or to make us
only negatively holy, but it is Design is, to make us positively holy, in the
Stamp, and Characters of the divine Likeness, renewed upon our Souls, and in
our living in the Exercise of those Virtues, and Graces, which are required of
us; that is, That we improve the Grace conferred upon us in our first
Conversion, and make Progress in mortifying of our corrupt Part, and living
more in Conformity unto the Will of GOD: and it is our own Fault, if we do not
improve the Commandment so as to answer the good End which GOD aims at, in
giving it unto us.

Hence it enjoins Holiness upon us, in the general; 1 Pet. i. 15, 16.
As he who has called you is holy, so be ye holy, in all Manner of
Conversation; because it is written, be ye holy, for I am holy. And it directs
us to the particular Virtues of which Holiness consists: That Phil. iv. 8.
whatsoever Things are true, whatsoever Things are honest, whatsoever Things
are just, whatsoever Things are pure, whatsoever Things are lovely, whatsoever
Things are of good Report; if there be any Virtue, if there be any Praise,
think on these Things. 2 Pet. i. 5, 6, 7.
Add to your Faith, Virtue; and to Virtue, Knowledge; and to Knowledge,
Temperance; and to Temperance, Patience; and to Patience, Godliness; and to
Godliness, Brotherly-Kindness; and to Brotherly-Kindness, Charity.

Hence also, it sets before us, the excellent Example of the most holy Life of
the blessed JESUS, his Piety, Devotion, and Reverence, to GOD; his Temperance,
Patience, and Humility, in the Government of himself; and his Righteousness,
Meekness, Benevolence, and Charity, in his Behavior toward Man; and all to
raise our Ambition, that we may go and do likewise: And it entertains us with
the Lives of the Prophets, and Apostles, and other Men of GOD, who were subject
unto like Passions with our selves, that we may learn to shun their Errors, and
imitate their Excellencies, and so be Followers of them, who through Faith and
Patience, inherit the Promises.

This is the natural Effect, and genuine Produce, of that Law which is itself
holy, and requires Holiness of us; which has an holy GOD, for its Author, and
leads to a holy JESUS. The Commandment shines full, and clear, with this
beautiful Aspect upon it, Even our Sanctification, for this is the Will of GOD
concerning us. 1 Thessalonians. iv. 3.
It tends to beget in us all the Graces of the Holy Spirit, Love, Joy, Peace,
Long-suffering, Gentleness, Goodness, Faith, Meekness, Temperance. It Is the
good Seed, which, sown in good Ground, springs up, in the Fruits of Holiness,
unto eternal Life. It Is the incorruptible and immortal Seed 1 Pet. i. 23.
, by which we are begotten again, unto GOD, and have the Disposition of our
heavenly Father ruling in us, and his Image shining upon us. The Apostle James
therefore says, Jam. i. 18.
Of his own Will begat he us, by his Word of Truth: And the Apostle Paul
glories in his being instrumental, through GOD, by the preaching of the Gospel,
for the Sanctification of the Corinthians, 1 Cor. iv. 15.
Though you have ten Thousand Instructors in Christ, yet have ye not many
Fathers; for, in Christ Jesus, I have begotten you through the Gospel. And to
add no more, hence our blessed Savior, in his devout Prayer for his Disciples,
informs us, what is the End and Design of the Commandment, in that Petition,
Joh. xviii. 17.
Sanctify them through thy Truth, thy Word is Truth.

This sufficiently shows us, that the noble Design of the divine Commandment
is, the making of us good Men; and that the Goodness which it aims at, and
accomplisheth in all the People of GOD, far surpasses all the Excellency and
Goodness which the greatest mere Moralist could boast of. Though the
Commandment of GOD strictly requires Morality, without which there can be no
Likeness to GOD, nor Acceptance with him; yet this is not all that is expected
from us; but there is something more in being a Christian. An Heathen may glory
in his Morality; and, indeed, considering the mighty Disadvantages he labors
under, a moral Heathen is a very great Attainment; but it is justly required of
the Christian, who enjoys a clearer Light, stronger Motives, and a more
powerful Assistance, that he be, and do, more than others Matthew. v. 47.
, who are not favored with the like excellent Means; that he has more noble
Principles to act and govern him, that he walks by a more exact Rule, and that
he be possessed of more excellent Virtues, than ever lodged in the Breast of a
mere Moralist: In short, that he has the Grace of GOD, a vital Principle of
spiritual and divine Life produced in him, by the quickening and enlivening
Influences of the divine Word, and Commandment, accompanied with the prevailing
Operations of the Holy Spirit of GOD; and that is a more exalted and refined
Virtue, and Goodness, than a Seneca, or a Plate, were ever Masters of.

Thus, under these two Heads, of making us wise, and good, I have endeavored
to show you, that the divine Commandment is exceeding broad, and has such an
Excellency and Perfection in it, as is not to be found in all the Creatures;
for thus it becomes perfective of our Nature, renewing of us in Knowledge, and
Righteousness, by regulating of our Powers, and curing the Disorders of our
Souls, by recovering of us to a God-like Temper, and Behavior, and rendering
of us universally Beneficent; which blessed Privilege, under the first
Doctrine, I showed you, the Creature was not able to convey to us.

SERMON VI.
PSALM CXIX. 96. I have seen an End of all Perfection; but thy Commandment is
exceeding broad.


I AM upon the Second Doctrine contained in these Words, viz.

Doc. II. The Commandment of GOD is exceeding broad.

I proposed to evidence the Excellency of the Divine Commandment, by
discoursing on,

I. The Original of it. II. The Subject Matter of it. III. The Extent of it
objectively. IV. The great End and Design of it. And V. The Duration of it. All
of which will help to show us the Excellency of the divine Commandment, beyond
what is to be seen upon the Creatures.
Under the Fourth of these Heads, namely,

IV. The great End and Design of these Commandment of GOD, I proposed to take a
View of its Excellency, as the manifest Design thereof, is to make us,

1. Truly Wise: 2. Really Good: And 3. Completely Happy.
I have discoursed on the first of these, viz.

1. The Design of the divine Commandment is to make us truly wise; as it
affords us the best Means to be wise for the Things of this World, but much
more as it tends to make us wise to Salvation.

I have also showed,

2. The great Design of the divine Commandment is to make us really Good. And
this is apparent, in that it is admirably calculated, to beget Faith in us, in
GOD, his Being, and adorable Perfections, and in JESUS CHRIST as our only
Savior; as also to convert the Soul, by convincing the Sinner of his
Sinfulness, and Misery, and turning him from the Error of his Ways; and to
sanctify and make us holy, and God-like, giving us the most holy Laws, and
setting before us the most holy Example; and by this Means to make us really
Good.

I proceed to say,

3. The great End and Design of the divine Commandment is, to make us
completely Happy. You see I keep in my View the two Rules, I formerly laid
down, by which to make Trial of the Perfection of any Thing, as it relates to
us; and, when we examine the divine Commandment by them, we find there is an
exact Agreement between them, which is a full Proof of the exceeding Breadth,
the transcendent Excellency of it. We have seen, under the foregoing Heads,
that it is perfective of our Nature, and now if we take a View of the Aspect it
has upon our Happiness, we shall see, that the glorious Design of the
Commandment, what GOD intends by privileging of us with it, and what it has a
direct Tendency to, is, to bring us unto true, complete, and endless Happiness:
It means to afford us all the Happiness, Joy, and Comfort, we are capable of
here, and bring us to complete and endless Happiness hereafter.

1. The exceeding Breadth of the divine Commandment is seen, in that Comfort,
and Joy, of Soul, which it aims at, in us, while we are here in the present
World. We are very prone to be mistaken in our Notions of Comfort, Joy, and
Pleasure, and think that they all are to be found, in the Possession of, what
we call, a Fullness, and Sufficiency of earthly Delights, as Silver, and Gold,
Houses, and Lands, and Children, and Friends, and the like; or in the Abundance
of the Pleasures of Sense, and that there is no Joy like the noisy Mirth of
Fools, reveling over their Cups, and sporting themselves with Vanity, or in the
gratifying of some fleshly Appetites: Whereas, if we do but consider Things a
little closely, we may easily discern the Truth of what our Savior tells us,
Luke xii. 15.
A Man's Life, (much more the Comfort of it) does not consist in the Abundance
of the Things which be possesses. The fullest Possessions are often the
Companions of an uneasy, disturbed Mind, and the greatest noisy Mirth and
Jollity is very consistent with inward Perplexity; for even in Laughter the
Heart is sorrowful, and the End of that Mirth is Heaviness; as the wise Man
observes Prove. xiv. 13.
. But there is a spiritual Solace, and Joy of Soul, which is peculiarly the
Entertainment, and Satisfaction, of the Saint: An heavenly Delight it is! Which
even the holy Soul himself experiences, not always, but only when he is under
the Influence of the more vigorous and lively Exercise of his Graces, and as it
pleases his heavenly Father sovereignly to dispense his special Favors to his
Children: And this is a Joy too bright, and pure, for the carnal Heart, in its
dark, and polluted State, to have the least Sight, or Taste of. This is a Joy
which a Stranger intermeddleth not with. Doubtless, the holy and good Man will
have his uneasy Sensations, as well as other Men, produced, by the Wounds that
may be given to his Body, Name, Family, or Interest, which he is liable unto,
in common with others, while he is in a World of Sin, and Sorrow: But yet, if,
at the same Time, he has that to comfort him, which is an Over-balance unto all
his Pains, and is sufficient to afford him inward Peace and Joy, he may well be
said to be an happy Man, notwithstanding all the adverse Circumstances that
attend him. And this is the Case of every truly good Man, he not only has
enough to keep him from sinking under his present Difficulties, but to cause
him to rejoice in Tribulation. 2 Cor. vii. 4.


Now, this spiritual Delight and Joy is all of it administered unto the Soul, by
the divine Commandment, as the great Instrument the holy Spirit makes Use of,
to irradiate, and comfort, the renewed Mind. It Is this makes us the capable
Subjects of this Joy; this hands the Comfort out into the Soul; this leads the
Soul to the Fountain, to drink of the pure River of Pleasures, and take in of
the Fullness of Joys. Hence our blessed Lord, in that heavenly Discourse he made
to his Disciples, a little before his Death, says to them, Joh. xv. 11.
These Things have I spoken unto you, that my Joy might remain in you, and that
your Joy might be full. And so the beloved Disciple of our Lord tells us, in
his first Epistle, 1 John i. 1, 4.
That which was from the Beginning, which we have heard -- of the Word of Life;
-- these Things write we unto you, that your Joy might be full. Here I shall
take Notice of two Things in particular,

1. The Commandment administers Support and Comfort to the holy Soul under all
his present Afflictions. We know, that through much Tribulation we must enter
into the Kingdom of GOD, Acts xiv. 22.
and that many are the Afflictions of the Righteous; Psalm. xxxiv. 19.
yet, nevertheless, our heavenly Father, in his tender Compassion to us, has
laid in a sufficient Stock of Comfort for us, in his holy Word, in the many
Encouragements, and precious Promises therein set before us, suited to our
present Condition, be it what it will.

Not only are we directed thereby, so to govern, and behave ourselves, as that
we do not, by our Sloth and Negligence, our Impatience and Peevishness, our
Rashness and Inconsiderateness, our Intemperance and Wantonness, our Falseness
and Injuriousness, and many other foolish Ways, bring upon ourselves those many
Distresses and Perplexities, which the ungodly World involve themselves in; but
when our heavenly Father sees it meet, in His holy Sovereignty, to lay any kind
of Affliction and Sorrow upon us, He also, for our Encouragement and Support,
gives us herein His gracious Promise to be with us Ps. xci. 15.
, and never to leave us nor forsake us Heb. xiii. 5.
, to uphold us from falling Isa. xii. 10.
, and prevent our Burdens from being too heavy for us, and upon our earnest and
fiducial Calling upon Him, to deliver us out of them, Job. v. 19.
if he sees it best; and, in the mean while, that we may be enabled, patiently,
and cheerfully, to bear what He appoints for us, He assures us, in His Word,
of His Fatherly Love, and Compassion, to us, under all, and that He means all
for our real Benefit and Advantage; that we may be more weaned from a vain and
thorny World, by our too fond Regards to which we often hurt and wound
ourselves, and may be more at Liberty to mind, and secure, our spiritual and
eternal Interest; to work upon our Corruptions, and purge away the Remainder of
our Filth, that we may be more pure and Godlike; to search and try us, and
discover the Reality, and Strength, of our Faith and Virtue, to ourselves, that
we may rejoice in the Prospect, and to others, that they may be allured unto
real Godliness; and, finally, to be the Means to promote and increase, our
future Crown of Glory. And who can think seriously of these mighty Advantages
from the divine Commandment, or have any Perception of them, without seeing,
that here is enough, not only to keep him from sinking into Dispondency, in the
Day of Affliction, but, to enable him to count it all Joy when he falls into
diverse Temptations?

Thus, under all our outward, and worldly Sorrows, we may repair to the divine
Commandment, and find a Word peculiarly adapted to our Circumstances, from
which, by a due Improvement of it, we may fetch in so much of Light and Joy, as
shall raise us above the Impressions, which our Afflictions would, otherwise,
make upon us. Thus, when we meet with any heavy Losses, and Bereavements, and
we find the perishing Creature wings itself away from us, we have this to
support, and comfort us, under all, Psalm. xxxiv. 9, 10.
There is no Want to them that fear the Lord; the young Lions do lack, and
suffer hunger, but they that fear the Lord shall want no good thing: And that,
Luke x. 42.
there is a good Part, which shall not be taken away. Thus, under bodily
Sickness, Pains, and infirmities, we are told, for our Comfort, Heb. xii. 6, 7,
10.
Whom the Lord loves, he chasteneth; and scourges every Son, whom he
receives: if ye endure chastening, GOD deals with you, as with Sons: be
chasteneth us for our Profit, to make us Partakers of his Holiness. And that, 2
Cor. iv. 17.
Our light Affliction, which is but for a Moment, works for us a for more
exceeding and Eternal Weight of Glory. Should Poverty invade us, and bring us
low in the World? we have this for our Viaticum, and Refreshment, Matthew. v. 3.
Blessed are the poor in Spirit, for theirs it the Kingdom of Heaven: And that,
Jam. ii. 5.
GOD has chosen the poor of this World, rich in Faith, and Heirs of the
Kingdom. Or, are we reproached, and reviled, and have Contempt, and Ignominy,
poured upon us, by the slanderous Tongues of those, whose Mouths are as an open
Sepulcher? What a Word of Comfort have we, in that of our Savior? Matthew. v.
11, 12.
Blessed are ye, when Men shall revile you, and say all Manner of Evil of you,
falsely, for my Sake; rejoice, and be exceeding glad; for great is your Reward
in Heaven. So that if we are careful not to suffer as EvilDeers, but endure
Grief, and suffer wrongfully, for. Conscience toward GOD, this-is' Thankworthy.

And thus, when we are exercised with any inward, and spiritual Trouble,
arising, either, from a deep Sense of our own Guilt, and daily Imperfections,
there is enough in the Commandment to revive, and comfort us; as that, Mic.
vii. 18.
Who is a GOD, like unto our GOD? that pardons Iniquity, and passes by the
Transgression of the Remnant of his Heritage; he retains not his Anger for
ever, because he delights in Mercy. And that, Ps. ciii. 13.
Like as a Father pitieth his Children, so the Lord pitieth them that fear him:
And that, Romans v. 20.
Where Sin abounded, Grace did much more abound: Or, for Fear of the Malice,
and Temptations of the wicked One, whom we find continually buffetting of us,
and casting his fiery Darts at us; this is our Encouragement, 1 Cor. x. 13.
GOD is faithful, who will not suffer you to be tempted above that ye are able,
but will with the Temptation also make a Way to escape, that ye may be able to
bear it; and that, Heb. ii. 18.
for in that he himself has suffered, being tempted, he is able to succor
them that are tempted; and that, 2 Cor. xii. 9.
My Grace shall be sufficient for you: Or, from the Withdraw of the divine
Favor, and the Hidings of the Light of the divine Countenance from us; yet
even in this sore Distress we are not left comfortless, but may still repair to
the Name of the Lord, the strong Tower whereto the Righteous run and are safe;
for he has said, Isa. xxvi. 20.
Come, my People, enter into thy Chambers, and shut thy Doors about thee; hide
thyself, as it were, for a little Moment, until the Indignation be everpast:
And, Isa. live. 7, 8.
for a small Moment have I forsaken thee, but with great Mercies will I gather
thee; in a little Wrath, I hid my Face from thee, for a Moment, but with
everlasting Kindness will I have Mercy on thee, says the Lord, thy Redeemer.

Thus the exceeding broad Commandment affords Relief; and Comfort to us, under
all the Difficulties, and Sorrows, whether outward, or inward, which any of the
People of GOD, are liable to, in the present World; and that such Support, so
great, so solid, so joyous, as is not to be met withal in any, nor all, of the
Creatures: A Sense of which made the Psalmist say, Ps. cxix. 92.
Unless thy Law had been my Delight, I should then have perished in mine
Affliction. And it is with a peculiar Reference unto the Advantages which he
reaped from the Commandment, when the whole Creation would not support him,
under the fierce Trials which he met withal, that he says, in the Words of my
Text, I have seen an End of all Perfection, but thy Commandment is exceeding
broad.

2. Another thing I would observe is, That the natural Produce, and Effect, of
our keeping the Commandment is, a true, inward, spiritual Joy, and Satisfaction
of Mind. Surely, there is nothing more delightful, and pleasant, to a rational
Creature, than the inward Peace, and Satisfaction, of his own Mind; that this
be calm, and quiet, and have nothing to disturb it. This has been the utmost
Aim of Philosophy, and the great Search of wise Men has been how to attain it:
but after all their Enquiry, it will be found, that there are no Methods, any
can fix upon, which will so naturally, and certainly, afford this inward
Satisfaction, as a steady, and constant, Observation of the divine Commandment,
as a firm Belief of all the Doctrines, and a conscientious Regard to all the
Precepts, contained in that sacred Revelation, will. Hence are those Texts, Ps.
xix. 8.
The Statutes of the Lord are right rejoicing the Heart. Ps. cxix. 165:
Great Peace have they that love thy Law, and nothing shall offend them. Prove.
iii. 17.
Her Ways are Ways of Pleasantness, and all her Paths are Peace. Isa. xxxii. 17.
The Work of Righteousness shall be Peace, and the Effect of Righteousness,
Quietness, and Assurance forever.

For, let but any Man seriously weigh the natural, and mighty Influence it will
have upon his Mind, to preserve it calm and steady, composed and easy, cheerful
and pleased with himself, for him to uphold a constant Reverence to the divine
Majesty, and worship him in Spirit and Truth, freely to approach to him with
his humble Supplications for all that he stands in Need of, and return him the
Praise of all that he receives from him; and to live in the universal Practice
of Righteousness, Truth, and Charity, injuring no Man, but being ready to put
up Injuries, and pass by Offenses, and extend his Beneficence to all about him;
and to restrain his Appetites, and Passions, by the Rules of Sobriety,
Patience, Temperance, and Contentment in his Station, and Condition; and to
have his humble Dependence on the boundless Mercy of GOD, and his firm Reliance
upon the infinite Merits and prevailing Intercession of JESUS CHRIST, our only
Mediator, for Acceptance, when he has done all; all of which the Divine
Commandment teaches, and requires of us; I say, let any Man thoroughly consider,
and weigh, these Things, in his own Mind, and he will plainly see, and be
forced to own, That no Man can possibly take a wiser Course, to preserve his
Mind in perfect Peace, and enjoy that inward Satisfaction, and Self-pleasing
Delight, which all the Rules of the wisest Philosophers could never attain to,
than to pay a strict, and constant Regard to the Divine Commandment.

This, then, is the Solamen of the gracious Soul! and it is such a
Satisfaction, and Joy, to him, as the greatest Fullness of the Profits, the
Pleasures, and the Honors, of this World, cannot yield him, nor can the
various worldly Sorrows, he may meet with, deprive him of it: and this is but
the genuine Effect of GOD's Commandment: for, 2 Cor. i. 2.
let but every Man prove his own Work, (bring it to the Touchstone of the
divine Oracles, and see that it agrees with that sacred Rule,) and then he
shall have Rejoicing in himself alone. For what can ruffle the Soul, and make
it uneasy, while the Man is conscious to himself, that he walks in the Ways of
Wisdom, and acts as becomes a rational, and religious, Creature? This takes
off the Offense he would, otherwise, conceive against himself, for doing a
Wrong, or base Thing, and makes him pleased with himself, and his own Actions,
and gains him the Plaudite of his own Conscience, which is more to a wise Man,
and lays a surer Foundation for his inward, secret, but yet very powerful, Joy,
and Pleasure, than the Approbation of all the Men in the World, without it.
This made the inspired Apostle break forth, in that Transport of Joy, 2 Cor. 1,
12.
This is our Rejoicing, the Testimony of our Conscience, that in Simplicity,
and godly Sincerity, not by fleshly Wisdom, but by the Grace of GOD, we have
had our Conversation in the World. Certainly, the Goings of such a Man must
need be pleasant; and let the World frown, and things about him be thrown into
great Confusion, let Friends treat him unkindly, Enemies insult him, and Nature
fail him, yet his Pathway, when he retires within himself, and takes a Survey
of himself, and his Actions, affords him true Peace, and Serenity of Mind.
Hence we read, Romans xv. 13.
of all Joy in believing: and, 1 Pet. i. 8.
of rejoicing with Joy unspeakable, and full of Glory. For now the holy Soul
can say, I have an advocate with the Father, JESUS CHRIST the righteous, who is
a Propitiation for my Sins: and if any thing can yield true Joy, and Peace, to
the Soul, certainly a Sense of GOD's being, in CHRIST, reconciled to us, and,
for His Sake, overlooking our Infirmities, and fully pardoning all our
Iniquities, and delivering of us from the Curse, and entituling of us to the
promised Blessing, will.

Hence also we read, of the Comforts of the Holy Ghost Act. ix. 31.
. For when that Holy Spirit brings home the Soul unto GOD, and enableth it to
yield a hearty, sincere, and universal, Obedience to the Divine Commandment, He
takes up his Residence in that Soul, and sheds abroad his holy and heavenly,
Influences in it, by which it is that the Soul is made willing, and obedient;
and wherever He dwells, we may reasonably expect that, there will be true solid
Joy and Comfort; because it is His proper Office, as the Divine Paraclete, to
administer Joy, as well as to sanctify; and therefore is He styled John xiv. 26.
the Comforter; who witnesses with our Spirits, that we are the Children of
GOD, and Heirs of Salvation.

Thus, the natural Produce of the divine Commandment is, the bright Rays of
divine Light, and Joy. This is the Joy of the Lord, Phil. iv. 4.
and the Peace of GOD which passes all Understanding Ver. 7.
! This Comfort, and Joy, is the Saints peculiar Privilege, and is the highest
Degree of Happiness he is capable of in this World; and is to him the Earnest,
and Foretaste of the Heavenly State. This the Wicked, who live in Disobedience
to the Commandment of GOD, and have no Delight in his Word, know nothing of:
but the Wicked are like the troubled Sea, when it cannot rest, whose Waters
cast up Mire, and Dirt; there is no Peace, says my GOD, unto the Wicked Isal.
lvil. 20, 21.
: Wasting, and Destruction, are in their Paths, the Way of Peace they know not;
they have made them crooked Paths, whosoever goes therein shall not know Peace
Isai. lix. 7, 8.
.

The exceeding Breadth of the divine Commandment is seen, in that full,
complete, and endless Happiness, which it lead to, in the World that is to
come. That no Man is truly happy, until he arrives at his End, has been an old
Observation. For, however it may fare with any Man at present, we know not what
may befall him hereafter; He that is now in the most afflicted Condition, may,
possibly, anon, have such an happy Turn given to his Circumstances, as that he
shall never more know any thing that would be burdensome to him, but ever dwell
at Rest, in the quiet Possession of all that is delightful and pleasant to him:
or, however agreeable and satisfactory a Man's present Circumstances may be to
him, we cannot tell, but, that within a little while, he may undergo such a
Change, in his Condition, as to be striped of all that was joyous to him, and,
instead thereof, to have a continued Succession of Pain, and Anguish,
tormenting of him. And no Man, that thinks calmly, will suppose, that a present
State of Affluence, and Delight, will render that Person Happy, who must by and
by change the Scene, and pass into a final State, and of longer in Duration, of
the extremest Want, and the most exquisite Pain. No; He is the truly happy
Man, who ends happily; who, whatever be his present Circumstances, shall anon
possess all that is agreeable to him, without any Mixture of Uneasiness, or
Fear of his ever altering his Condition for the worse.

Now, it is the blessed Design of the divine Commandment, to lead us unto this
happy End, to render our final, and last, State in which we shall exist
longest, and from which we shall know no Alteration, a State of true Pleasure,
and endless Satisfactions, to us. It Is this that informs us of a State of
supreme, and endless, Glory, and Happiness, to be enjoyed in the future World;
after a Period is put to the present Life; without which Information we should
have had no just Conceptions about it. 2. Tim. i. 10.
Our Savior JESUS CHRIST, who has abolished Death, has brought Life, and
Immortality, to Light, through the Gospel. Col. i. 5.
The Hope which is laid up for you in Heaven, whereof ye heard before in the
Word of the Truth of the Gospel.

This show us how, and by what means, this happy State is procured for us,
namely, by JESUS CHRIST, who, Heb. ii. 14.
forasmuch as the Children are Partakers of Flesh and Blood, Himself also
likewise took part of the same, that, through Death, he might destroy him that
had the Power of Death, that is the Devil: by whose Blood we have Boldness to
enter into the Holiest Heb. x. 19, 20.
, by a new, and living Way He has consecrated for us, through the Vail, that is
to say, His Flesh: who, Heb. vi. 20.
as our Forerunner, is for us entered within the Vail, and Joh. xiv. 3.
will come again, and receive us unto himself, that where He is, there we may
be also.

This shows us the Path Way leading unto Life, and acquaints us with those
Terms, which GOD has prescribed, to be complied with by us, in Order to our
safe Arrival at this happy State; that Mar. xvi. 16.
He that believes, and is baptized, shall be saved; and he that believes not
shall be damned: that, Joh. x. 27, 28.
they that hear His Voice, and follow Him, He will give unto them eternal Life,
and they shall never perish; that, Romans ii. 7.
it is by patient Continuance in the Way of Well-doing that we are to seek for
Glory, Honor, and Immortality, and shall obtain Eternal Life.

It Is this also that qualifies us for the Enjoyment of the promised Felicity,
by pourtraying the Lineaments, and Characters, of the Divine Image upon our
Souls, and making of us like to GOD, and meet for the Inheritance of the Saints
in Light; thus it is the Word of Truth, the Gospel of our Salvation Ephesians. i. 13.
; it is a Cor. iv. 4, 6.
the Light of the Glorious Gospel of Christ, that shines into our Hearts, to
give us the Light of the Knowledge of the Glory of GOD in the Face of Jesus
Christ; and Ephesians. iii. 6.
we are made Partakers of His Promise in Christ, by the Gospel.

And finally, it is this that assures, and confirms, this Happiness to us, and
according to which we shall receive our future Reward; Joh. ii. 25.
This is the Promise He has promised us, even eternal Life; Joh. xiii. 17.
If ye know these things, happy are ye if ye do them: and, Romans ii. 16.
GOD shall judge the Secrets of Men, by Jesus Christ, according to my Gospel.
The whole Gospel is a clear Demonstration that this is the great End and Design
of the Commandment, to bring us to the full Enjoyment of true and complete
Happiness; and therefore is it said, Jam. i. 21.
to be a Word able to save your Souls.

Thus, the Commandment appears to be exceeding broad, in that it leads to
complete Happiness, in the World to come; and its Perfection will be more fully
seen, by considering the Suitableness, the Fullness, and the Durableness, of
this Happiness to us.

1. The Suitableness of this Happiness, 'T a Felicity every way adapted to our
Nature, and to our Condition.

It Is suitable to our Natures, spiritual as we are; and this renders it an
happy State, indeed, because therein is possessed what is most agreeable unto
us; so that there is no Jar between our Nature, and the Objects from whence our
Happiness resulteth. It consists in spiritual Enjoyments, GOD, and CHRIST,
and holy Angels, and the Spirits of just Men made perfect: for we shall then,
come to the City of the living GOD, to the heavenly Jerusalem, to the Spirits
of Just Men made perfect, to the innumerable Company of Angels, to the general
Assembly, and Church of the Firstborn, and to GOD the Judge of all, and to
JESUS the Mediator Heb. xii. 22. 24.
The Pleasure, Satisfaction, and Joy, are all the most spiritual, as are, in
some Measure, the lesser Degrees of it, which the Saint experience here: our
Bodies themselves will then be spiritualised, and be no more capable of the
carnal Joys which now affect them. The Services, and Employments, of Heaven are
spiritual also; Hallelujahs, and Praise, and the highest Devotion, being the
Work of Saints, and Angels, throughout an endless Eternity.

It Is an Happiness suited to our Condition and Circumstances, and contains in
it a perfect Deliverance from all Evil, both of Sin, and of Punishment. For,
there enters into the holy City above, nothing that desileth, or works
Abomination, or makes a Lie Rev. xxi. 17.
