The holy Soul will carry no Remainders of Corruption with him there, to
discompose, or pollute, his Mind, and mar the Pleasancy of his Society, and
Converse; nor shall any tempting Devil there invade him, but there is perfect
Harmony, and perfect Purity.

There no Sorrow shall disturb us, but Rev. xxi.
GOD shall wipe away all Tears from our Eyes; and there shall be no more Death,
neither Sorrow, nor Crying, neither shall there be any more Pain. We shall then
be subject to none of those afflictive Evils, which our Lives here are often
imbittered with; nor shall the Second Death have any Power over us Rev. xx. 6.


This happy State consists in the Possession of a suitable Good, what a
rational, and immortal, Soul craves after, and is delighted in. Then GOD shall
be all in all unto the Soul; and the Possession of him, who is the Perfection
of Beauty, will be such an agreeable Happiness, that the Soul can wish for
nothing in Heaven besides him. Then the dear Object of our Affection, who has
so loved us as to give himself for us, to wash away our Sins in his own Blood,
will forever appear before us, not, as on Earth, with a Crown of Thorns, and
his Visage marred more than any Man's, but, in all the radiant Luster of an
enthroned Redeemer, surrounded with the glorious Retinue of the heavenly Host,
shouting their loud Hosannahs to the incarnate Son of GOD; and the Sight, and
Enjoyment of him, whom here we have not seen, but loved, will be the continual
Satisfaction, and Delight, of the holy Soul; whose devout Breathings now are,
like that of the Psalmist, Ps. lxxiii. 25.
Whom have I is Heaven but thee, and there is nothing on Earth that I desire
besides thee.

2. This Happiness is most full and sufficient, answerable to our Wants, and
our most enlarged Desires. It Is not only suitable unto our Nature, but there is
enough of it, and to spare. There is such a Fullness, in the Happiness of
Heaven, that the Soul cannot possibly need any thing more, to render it
possessed of true and unspeakable Felicity, and that far beyond what are it is
present most raised Expectations, and earnest Cravings. For, 1 Cor. ii. 9.
Eye has not seen, nor Ear heard, neither has it entered into the Heart of Man
to conceive, how great things GOD has laid up for them that love him.

Fullness, and Sufficiency, are very necessary Inpredients in true Happiness.
For, let a Man's Possessions be what they will, yet, if they are not, equal to
his Desires, he is miserable, in the Midst of his greatest Abundance; because
his Desires, of what he has not, and cannot have, will be a continual Torment
to him. But here, in the Happiness of the future World, there is an immense
Fullness; not Streams only, but Rivers of Pleasure, not Abundance only, but
Fullness of Joys, which are at GOD's Right Hand Ps. xvi. 11.
It Is a satisfying Fullness, which completely fills every Appetite of the Soul;
and more; the holy Soul enters into the Joy of his Lord Matthew. xxv. 21.
He is swallowed up with ineffable Delights and Satisfactions.

In short; There is enough in GOD, and CHRIST, and Heaven, to satisfy all the
Appetites of the innumerable Hosts of Heaven; and, whilst each particular
Believer shall have as much as he can contain, there remains an infinite Ocean
of Delights behind, from whence all the glorified Angels derive their
unutterable Joys, and yet, there is no more of an Abatement, and lowering, of
the Fountain, than if there were none of those Miriads of Streams continually
issuing from it, which everlasting delight those happy Spirits.

3. Lastly; to render this Happiness truly complete, it shall never have an
End. The Happiness, which the divine Commandment leads us to, not only succeeds
to that mixed Condition which attends us while we are in this World, and is our
last Stage, after which we shall know no other State, but it will abide, and
continue, with us, throughout an endless Duration; and this renders it a State
of Happiness indeed. A short Fit of Ease, following upon a much longer one of
Pain, is exceeding pleasant; and how greatly would the Pleasure be enhansed,
could we besure the Pain would return no more upon us? What then will the long,
the uninterrupted, the endless Delights, and Pleasures, of Eternity be? How
Ravishing! how Transporting! must it be, for the Soul to feel itself in the
full Possession of perfect Transquility, encircled with all that is
entertaining, and delightful to it, and to be able to look Forward, and be
assured, that this State will continue forever and ever? This is the Condition
of the happy Spirits in the heavenly World. The Rivers of Pleasures at GOD's
Right Hand continue to flow, and will do so forever and ever. Nothing shall be
able to dam up the flowing Stream; no Duration will be sufficient to run it
dry; but, throughout an endless Eternity, the Happiness will remain, and
increase, upon the obedient Soul; and the more he receives, the more capable
will the enlarged Mind be of advanced Degrees of it, and be perpetually as
filled, as it is extended, without ever being cloyed, or the least Diminution
of the Felicity.

The great Author, and Object, of this Happiness is, from everlasting to
everlasting Ps. xc. 2.
; and this Felicity can no more cease to flow from him, upon Supposition of a
Subject capable of receiving it, than He can cease to have a Being.

The joyful Partakers of this Happiness are purified, immortal Spirits Matthew.
x. 28.
, and immortal Bodies 1 Cor. xv. 53.
also, and consequently the Happiness it self must needs be everlasting.

Hence the Seat of this Blessedness is styled, an everlasting Habitation Luke
xvi. 9.
an House, not made with Hands, eternal in the Heavens 2 Cor. v. 1.
; and the blessed State is termed, eternal Life Rem. vi. 22.


Thus we see that the Happiness of the future World is perfect and complete,
being suitable, full, and endless; and that it is the great, and noble End, and
Design, of the Divine Commandment, to bring us to all of this Happiness, and
fix us in it: hence said our Savior, Joh. xii. 49, 50.
I have not spoken of myself, but the Father which sent me, He gave Me a
Commandment, what I should say, and what I should speak; and I know that his
Commandment is Life everlasting.

These Things show us, that the Divine Commandment is exceeding broad,
considered as to its gracious End and Design, which, we see, is to perfect our
Nature, and complete our Happiness; which none, nor all, of the Creatures are
able to Effect. There remains one Head more to be spoken to, which I shall
more briefly go over, and conclude the doctrinal handling of these Words. viz.

V. The Commandment of GOD will appear exceeding broad, if we consider its
Duration, that it forever abides. Duration adds greatly to the Worth and
Excellency of Things which are otherwise valuable. It Is This that renders Gold
the most precious of Metals, in the Estimation of Mankind, that it is less
Subject to Corruption, and Loss, by Rust, or to Destruction, by the severest
Trial the Fire can make upon it, and so is of a more durable Nature, than any
other, And this stamps a peculiar Excellency, and Dignity, upon the
Commandment, Law, or Word of GOD, that, when all the Objects of Sense are
fading, and perishing, in their Nature, yet That remains fixed, permanent,
and abiding, and continues stedsast forever: for, who shall change what the
infinitely great and wise GOD has determined; or, alter the Things that has
gone out of His Mouth? Isa. xl. 6, 8.
All Flesh is Grass, and the Goodliness thereof as the Flower of Grass; -- the
Grass withers, the Flower fades, but the Word of our GOD shall stand
forever. Particularly,

1. It may not be improper to observe, the permanent Duration of that excellent
Book, which contains the Commandment of GOD, and handeth to us the Revelation
of the Divine Mind and Will unto the World. However the first Ages of the
World, under the Advantage of the Longevity of the Patriarchs, might have the
Knowledge of what GOD had revealed, handed down from Father to Son, in a
traditionary Way, sufficiently certain, to guide them in their Conduct; Yet as
those Revelations multiplied, and the Life of Man was shortened, the divine
Wisdom saw it necessary, to direct to a Collection of these Revelations, (as
far as there was Occasion,) and committing them to Writing, by Men under the
Inspiration and Guidance of the divine Spirit; that there might be a more
certain Conveyance of the various Truths, and Duties, necessary to be believed,
and practiced, to succeeding Generations, than the Brevity of Life, Defects of
Memory, and sinister Designs of multiplied Nations of Men, would admit of; and
accordingly, all that GOD has seen meet to reveal, and thought proper to
preserve, through the Series of the Old Testament, and the New, until the
sacred Canon, the Rule of our Faith, and Manners, was completed, and there was
no Occasion for any New Revelation, has been, at different Times, collected,
and put into Writing, and is contained in that Book we call THE BIBLE, the Book
of Books.

Now, it is a Matter well worthy of our Observation, for us to consider, after
what a wonderful Manner, this holy Book, containing the Commandment, Law, and
Word, of our GOD, has been preserved, and handed down to us, through so many
Generations; notwithstanding all the Malice and Spite, the Rage and Fury, of
the World against it. When Moses beheld a Bush burning with Fire, and yet not
consumed, it filled him with Wonder; and he said upon it, Exodus iii. 3.
I will now turn aside, and see this great Sight, why the Bush is not burnt.
That the Word of GOD has continued to this Day, after having endured so many
Ages fiery Trial; and all the Flames, which the Lusts of Men, and Rage of
Devils, have kindled against it, have not been able to consume it, is little
less wonderful and surprising. For it is very certain, that there is no Book in
the World so directly contrary to the Kingdom, and Interest, of the Devil, as
our Bible is; no Book so diametrically opposite to the carnal Views, and
sensual Pleasures, of Mankind, that gives such a Check to their most violent
Inclinations, that so pungently touches them in the most tender Point, by
thwarting and disturbing, of them, in their most pleasing Gratifications, as
this Book does, by the strict Holiness, and Purity of its Doctrines, and Laws;
and therefore it would be no strange Thing, but what might be expected, that
Earth and Hell should combine together, in their utmost Endeavors, to destroy
this holy Book from off the Face of the Earth, that there may be no more a
Remembrance of it among Men. And accordingly, the Enemy have made their fierce
Assaults upon the Bible; there have been public Orders, and vigorous Attempts,
from the ruling Powers of the Earth, to call in, and burn, and destroy, all the
Copies of this Book of GOD; and yet it has outlived all the Spite, and Fury, of
its persecuting Adversaries; and has been translated into most Languages, and
spread over many and mighty Nations. While innumerable Writings, of merely
humane Composition, though greatly valued by the World, have been eaten out,
and totally devoured by the Iron Teeth of Time, these sacred Writings, though
the first born of Writings, have remained firm, and secure, through all Ages,
to this Day; and no Attempts of Heretics to corrupt them, have been able to
prevail against them, but the Imposture has soon been discovered, and the
canonical Books preserved pure, and incorrupt, in every material Article, to
our Times: though probably there may be some literal, and less material Errors,
through the Mistakes of Transcribers, and Typographers, easily discerned and
corrected. So the Word of GOD abides forever, and shall do so as long as the
World lasts. And it is no weak Argument of the divine Original of our Holy
Bible, that such a peculiar Care of divine Providence has been so evidently
manifested in the Preservation of it, as has baffled all Endeavors to
suppress, and destroy it.

If we take a View of the several Matters contained in our holy Bible, we shall
see that they are permanent and durable, I do not mean now the historical Part
of the Bible, (though even that, being once true, remains forever so,) but I
intend those Parts of the Bible which refer to our Duty, and our Happiness:
and, leaving the moral Part to be considered by itself, I shall here only touch
upon some other Heads.

Thus, if we consider the several Revelations contained in the sacred Oracles,
we shall find, that, however they may, many of them, comprise such deep and
mysterious Doctrines in them, as the greatest Search of the humane
Understanding is not able to comprehend, yet, they are such sure and certain
Truths, as will remain forever immutably the same; so that we may say upon them
all, Psalm. cxix. 162.
Thy Word is true from the Beginning, and every one of thy righteous Judgments
endures forever.

Or, if we consider the Predictions of the holy Writings, they will all of them
appear to be infallibly certain, and, as many of them have been already exactly
fulfilled, so, they all shall, in their due Time, without failing in the least
Point, receive their full Accomplishment; and, when they are finally
accomplished, it will remain an eternal Truth, that they were Predictions of
such, and such, future Events, and that the Event exactly corresponded with the
Production. Therefore the Prophet Isaiah introduces GOD Himself saying Isai.
xlvi. 9, 10.
I am GOD, and there is none else; I am GOD, and there is none like Me,
declaring the End from the Beginning, and, from ancient Times, the Things that
are not yet done; saying my Counsel shall stand, and I will do all my Pleasure.

Or, if we consider the Promises contained in the Word of GOD, we shall find,
that they are not Yea, and Nay, uncertain, and indeterminate, loose, and
changable, but they are all of them Yea, and Amen, sure, and infallible, firmer
than Mountains of Brass, and shall all of them, without Exception, in due Time,
and in the proper Manner, be fulfilled unto them who are entitled unto them;
being founded upon the immutable Nature of GOD, which admits of no
Variation, or Shadow of turning; and when they are once fulfilled are made good
forever. Hence the Psalmist said, Psalm. cxix. 89.
Forever, O Lord, Thy Word is settled in Heaven; Thy Word of Promise is
ratifyed and confirmed in Heaven; Thy Faithfulness is unto all Generations.

So the Religion, taught us in the Word of GOD, abides forever. Whatever have
been the Alterations in the external Modes, Rites, and Ceremonies, of the true
Religion, which came down from Heaven, yet, as to the Substance thereof, it has
been, and ever will be, invariably the same; therefore it is called, Psalm.
cxxxix. 14.
the Way everlasting, and 1. Chron. xvi. 17.
an everlasting Covenant. For there never was, nor ever will be, any, from
amongst the sinful Children of Men, received into the Favor of GOD, but
through a Mediator, making himself an Offering, and Sacrifice for Sin; and by a
sincere turning from all Wickedness, and patient Continuance in the Way of
Well-doing. The Terms of Blessedness are forever the same.

I may add, the Blessed Effect of the Word of GOD, upon the hearts of Men, is
permanent and abiding. That divine Work wrought upon the Soul of a Sinner,
whereby he is begotten with the Word of Truth, and has the divine Image, and
Likeness, renewed upon him, in a real through conversion to GOD, shall never
perish and come to nothing, but be perfected unto the Day of CHRIST; He that
has begun the good Work, will take care of the Completing of it; and the
divine Life, introduced into the Soul, here, by the Vehiculum Spiritus, the
Chariot of Salvation, shall pass over into eternal Glory. However frail the
Believer may be in himself, and subject to many Weaknesses, and Falls, yet, the
divine Power which has taken Possession of him, will not be forced to let go
it is Hold, but, will uphold, and preserve him; and none shall be able to pluck
him out of the Redeemer's Hands. The Seeds of divine Grace, planted in the
renewed Soul, are incorruptible, immortal, and shall never die, but flourish
forever and ever. Hence we read 1 Pet. 1, 23.
of, being born again, not of corruptible Seed, but of incorruptible, by the
Word of GOD, which lives and abides forever.

3. The praceptive Part of the divine Commandment is of Everlasting Duration. I
mean the moral Part of GOD's Law. For, though positive Precepts, depending upon
the Will of the Lawgiver, and the variable Circumstances of the Subject, are
alterable, at Pleasure, and as those Circumstances are changed, yet, the moral
Precepts, which flow from the immutable Nature of GOD, and the constant Nature,
and Relation, of Man, remain forever invariable. So the Divine Commandment was
a Commandment unto Adam, a Law unto Israel, and is so to us Gentiles, since,
through the tender Mercy of the most High, the Light of Israel is risen upon
us. So that the divine Commandment endures throughout all Ages, as well as
extends to all Persons. Hence the Psalmist said, Ps. cxix. 152.
concerning thy Testimonies, I have known of old, that thou have founded them
forever: they are designed to endure forever, and are infinitely more
unchangable than the Laws of the Medes and Persians.

Yea, the Divine Commandment is eternal Verity, founded upon the infinite
Perfections of the Divine Nature, to which nothing can be added, from which
nothing can be wanting, and therefore, like the divine Nature itself, shall
endure throughout all Generations, and to an endless Eternity. Hence said our
Savior, Matthew. v. 18.
Till Heaven and Earth pass away, one Jet, or one Tittle, shall in no wise pass
from the Law, The moral Law is unchangable, immutable; sooner shall Heaven and
Earth be abolished, than the Authority, and Obligation, of the moral Law be
dissolved Mr. Burkit.
. For though the Believer, when he shall arrive at his happy Seat, may no
longer be a Subject capable of yielding Obedience to this, or that, Part of the
Commandment; (which was adapted unto him, while he was on Earth,) yet, this
argues no Alteration in the Commandment itself, much less a nullifying of it;
the Commandment abides still, and forever, the same; because the natural, and
necessary, Result of those Perfections which eternally center in GOD; so that
if these were, through an whole Eternity, a capable Subject, every Part of the
Commandment, including Moral Duty, would forever remain in Force's but it only
argues a Change in the Subject, and that, because of his, then, advanced
State, and Condition, this, or that, Part of the Commandment would have no
Relation to him.

To give an instance, in that Repentance, and Sorrow of Soul for Sin, which,
here, is the great Duty of every Christian: These are the natural Result of the
Perfections of GOD, considered in Relation to a sinful Creature, as yet a
capable Subject of Mercy; and therefore they forever remain good, in
themselves, though, in Heaven, there is no Sinner to yield Obedience to them,
nor, in Hell, any that are the capable Subjects of Mercy. Though there may be
an Alteration in the Capacity, and Relation, of the Subject, by which Means he
is no longer held under Obligation to perform such, or such a Duty; that it, is
not under Obligation to obey a Law which was not made for him; yet there can be
no Alteration, strictly speaking, in the Nature of the Divine Commandment;
which is unchangeable, as GOD himself is. So that there is an eternal
Excellency in the Divine Commandment.

Thus, I have showed you, the Commandment of GOD is exceeding broad, considered
in the Excellency of its Original; it is Nature; and the Extent of it, to every
Man, and to our whole Duty; in it is great End and Design, to perfect our
Nature, and make us completely happy; and in it is eternal Duration; And, upon
the Whole, we see, with what good Reason the Psalmist said, I have seen an End
of all Perfection, but thy Commandment is exceeding broad.

I must now leave the Improvement of these things to a farther Opportunity, GOD
willing; Consider what you have now beard, (or read,) and the LORD give you
Understanding in all Things.

SERMON VII.
PSALM CXIX. 96. I have seen an End of all Perfection; but thy Commandment is
exceeding broad.


THE last Opportunity I had of discoursing to you from these Words, I finished
what I had to say upon the Second Doctrine; viz. That the Commandment of GOD is
exceeding broad: under which I have showed the exceeding Breadth, or very great
Excellency, of the Divine Commandment, in its Original, the Subject Matter of
it, it is Extent, the noble End and Design of it, and in its Duration: and I
shall now proceed to make some suitable Improvement of what has been said.

Use. I. And the first Use of this Doctrine may by Way of Information, to
instruct and teach us, and that in several things. As,

1. This Doctrine may serve to teach us, the wonderful Goodness, Mercy, and
Compassion, of GOD to a miserable World. The exceeding Breadth of the Divine
Commandment, we have seen, lies very much in the gracious Ends and Designs of
it, which are to correct the Disorders of our Nature, and to make happy
Creatures of us; and since these are the excellent Designs of the Divine
Commandment, what GOD aims at by it; and what it is admirably adapted unto, we
have from hence a clear Conviction of the abundant Mercy, Goodness, and
Compassion, of GOD, to fallen miserable Sinners, in so highly favoring of us,
as to make such a Revelation of his Mind and Will to us, as may happily recover
us from our lapsed Condition, the Sinfulness, and the Misery of it. GOD might,
if He had so pleased, have left us in the Condition of fallen Angels, to whom
He has made no such new Discoveries of his Mind and Will, as affords any
Direction, and Encouragement, unto them, to return to their Duty to Him, with
the Assurance, of their being forgiven their past Offenses, and received into
his special Favor, in Case they do so: whereas he has been pleased to deal
quite otherwise with us, and has given us His Word, his Commandment, the
Revelation of his Will concerning us, that hereby we might be directed in the
whole of our Duty, both as to Faith, and Manners, and that we might have all
imaginable Encouragement, to return to him, and carefully attend our Duty, from
the fullest Assurances, that, through the Mediation of his dear Son, He is most
ready to admit us into his Friendship, and bestow upon us all the Happiness we
are capable of receiving. What Obligations could the divine Majesty be under to
Creatures that had lost their Rectitude, and forfeited his Favor, by the Act
of their own Will, to entertian one kind Thought of recovering them from that
Death, and Hell, which was their just Due, and to give Light and Instruction to
them, to guide their Feet into the Way of Peace? And what is there to move the
infinitely great GOD, who needs us not, neither can be benefited by us, thus to
distinguish us with his kind Regards to us? What, but the pure Goodness of his
Nature, his free and rich Mercy, and Compassion? It Is because be delights in
Mercy Mic. vii. 18.
, that he has given us his Commandment, without which our Condition had been
unavoidably miserable, nor could we have known any possible Way of helping
ourselves.

It is true, if we had been left wholly to the Light of Nature, without a
divine Revelation, we might have spelled out so much of our Duty to GOD, and
our Neighbors, as would have rendered us altogether inexcusable in the Neglect
of it: for the Work of the Law is written in the Hearts of them, who have not
the written Law, so that they are a Law unto themselves, as the Apostle
discourses Romans ii. 14, 15.
; and so much of the invisible things of GOD is clearly seen, being understood
by the Things that are made, chapter i. 20.
as would have forever condemned us, if we should not have glorified him as
GOD: yet this natural Light, alone, would never have been able to have answered
the great Designs, of perfecting our Nature, and completing our Happiness;
yea, I doubt not to say, it would have left us far short of moral Rectitude,
and altogether in the dark about the Way of Salvation. For, this inbred Law is
so dimmed, and obscured, by the Corruption, and Depravity, which, we certainly
find by sad Experience, attends our Nature, (howsoever we first came by it,)
that we should not have been able, by the Light of it, to have read the whole
of our Duty, nor to have seen where our true Interest lay; as is very evident
if we consider the Condition of that Part of the World, in any Age of it, which
has been left wholly without a divine Revelation. We very much mistake the
Force of natural Light, when we imagine, that all we find agreeable to the
Sentiments of our own Minds, now that we have the Advantage of Revelation,
might have been sufficiently discovered to us by the ordinary Improvement of
our rational Powers; whereas this only teaches us, how highly reasonable the
divine Revelation is; that the Duty GOD therein requires of us cannot be set
before us, in it is proper Light, but our Reason immediately sees the Equity of
it, and acknowledges it to be good; and not what we should have been able to
have seen, by the Strength of our own Reason, without Revelation. It no more
infers the Capacity of our natural Reason, to discover the Duties revealed to
us, because, by the Help of such a Revelation, we can trace the Reasonableness,
and Equity, of the Duty, than our plain beholding Jupiter's Satelletes, or
Saturn's Ring, by the Help of a Telescope, or the Animalcula in a Drop of
Water, by the Help of a Microscope, infers the Capacity of our Eyes, by their
natural Strength, and without those Assistances, to behold them. The best
Evidence of the Power of Nature is to be fetched from those Nations, and People
who never had any Thing but natural Light to guide them; and there we see, not
only among the more barbarous Nations, but even the most civilized, and greatly
improved in humane Learning, that the Generality of the People were destitute
of the Knowledge of many moral Virtues, and their most learned Men were
Ignorant of some, and that they were all absolute Strangers to true Happiness;
they knew not the only true GOD, the Way of serving of Him acceptably, nor how
to enjoy his Favor: And hence we find the greatest, and best, of their
Philosophers, as Socrates, and Plato, expressing their Sense of the Want, and
their Hope, of a future, divine Revelation. There are, indeed, some moral
Duties which do, as it were, lie uppermost in the humane Mind; Reason easily,
and without much Search, discerns them; and there are some others which,
probably, our natural Light might find out, by close Attention, and diligent
Application. But the Bulk of Mankind are not very capable of so industrious an
Enquiry, nor have they Leisure for it, if they were capable of it: and after
all, the great and wonderful Discoveries which Athens, and Rome, have made of
moral Virtue, left us in the Writings of their most learned Men, I am apt to
think, that, upon a due Enquiry, it will be found, they owed it, not to the
Force of their natural Powers, which some of them greatly improved, but to the
Light they received from the Jewish Writings, with which they were undoubtedly
conversant, which contained a Revelation from GOD, of what Nature would never
have taught them. Since such was the Condition of Mankind, that, of themselves,
they could not have come at the Knowledge of those things which were necessary
for them to know, therefore GOD, in his great Goodness, and Compassion, has
condescended to our Weakness, and Infirmity, in giving to us his written Law,
firstly made known by Revelation from himself, wherein the whole of our Duty is
fully, and clearly, set before us, and the only Way to true and endless
Happiness is plainly discovered to us.

As the Case stands with us, at present, we can neither be recovered from the
Imperfection of our Nature, nor our State, without a Mediator, a Redeemer,
appearing on our behalf, becoming a Surety for us, obeying the Law, and
undergoing the Penalty of it; that is to say, bearing the Curse for us, that we
might not fall under the Malediction of the Law, which we have broken. This
natural Reason would never have discovered to us, but we should forever have
wandered, as even the most polite Parts of Athens, and Rome, did, in Search
after some certain Method, by which to appease the Anger of the Deity, whom,
natural Conscience, from a Sense of our own manifold Miscarriages, would have
told us, we had offended: and so we should have endlesly remained in the dark
about the Way of Salvation, if GOD had not, in his great Compassion to us,
given us a full, and clear Revelation thereof, in his holy Word.

Thus, we may see the Goodness of GOD to us, both in adjusting his Commandment
to our rational Nature, requiring of us only a reasonable Service, a Service
which, when we view it in the true Beauty of it, we cannot but acknowledge to
be just, and equitable; a Service which enobles our Minds, rectifies our
Manners, sweetens our Relations, endears our Society, and is every Way
advantageous to us, and, at the same Time, making known to us thereby the Way,
the Truth, and the Life, or the true Way unto Life, and Happiness. For he has
told us, in his Word, that he has provided a Redeemer for us, even the Lord
JESUS CHRIST, his only begotten Son, the dearly Beloved of the Father, whom he
has set forth for a Propitiation for our Sin, through Faith in his Blood Romans
iii. 25.
; He has assured us of the Fullness, and Sufficiency, of the Merits of his
Obedience, and Suffering, by his Resurrection from the Dead, of which he has
given Assurance to all Men, where the Gospel is preached; and he graciously
invites the greatest Sinner of us all to come to the Blessed JESUS, and yield
the Obedience of Faith to him, and live. Thus is GOD, in CHRIST, reconciling a
guilty World unto himself, not imputing their Trespasses unto them 2 Cor. v. 19.
. And if it had not pleased GOD thus to reveal his Designs of Grace and Favor
to us, in his holy Word, we should, doubtless, have perished among those that
are lost. Hence it is that his Commandment is called Act. xx.
the Word of his Grace: not only because, by it, he works Grace in our Souls,
but in that it is an Act of free Grace, and rich Goodness, in GOD, to
privilege us with a Divine Revelation.

The divine Commandment aims at the Recovery of us from all the sad Effects of
our Apostasy, and to bring us unto GOD, and Happiness: and however natural
Light was sufficient unto innocent Man, while as yet there was nothing to blind
his Mind, and bias his Will, and Affections, so that he might have seen his
Duty clearly, and, possibly, have performed it fully, and so have secured the
Favor of GOD, and his own uninterrupted and endless Happiness; yet Sin has so
obscured the Understandings of Men, and prejudiced the Powers of their Souls,
in Favor of what is agreeable to the Senses, and the lower Appetites, and
against what would any Ways abridge them of the Gratifications of Sense, that
under the Influence of natural Light, alone, we should never be able to
discover every Mystery of Iniquity, nor be sufficiently moved to part with our
beloved Lusts; and, of Consequence, we should never be recovered from the sad
Effects of our. Fall, to the Grace and Favor of our GOD. Hence the Apostle
says, 1 Cor. ii. 14.
The natural Man receives not the things of the Spirit of GOD; for they are
Foolishness unto him; neither can be know them, because they are spiritually
discerned. And our Savior observes, Math. vi. 23.
if the Light that is in thee be Darkness, how great is that Darkness? So that
I cannot sufficiently wonder at it, that Men of Learning, and Thought, and such
as set themselves up for a polite Way of thinking, and reasoning, should be so
fond of their natural Light, as, for the Sake thereof, to discard divine
Revelation; when it is apparent, not only, that they are beholden to Revelation
for their Master Thoughts, but, without it, they would be destitute of the
clearest Light, and the strongest Arguments, that can have any moral Influence
upon a reasonable Creature, to a constant and diligent attendance upon even
moral Duties: that is they would be destitute of the best Means, to live like
GOD, and to enjoy his Favor forever.

But, blessed be GOD; we are advantaged with a divine Revelation: and as this
was the peculiar Profit of the Jewish Nation, above all People, that unto them
were committed the Oracles of GOD Romans iii. 1, 2.
; so now is it our special Advantage, since, through the tender Mercy of the
most High, the Day Star has risen, and shined, upon us Gentiles, and CHRIST has
been given for a Light, to lighten the Gentiles, as well as to be the Glory of
his People Israel. And as they did of old, so ought we to see, and own, the
Goodness of GOD to us herein, and sing his Praise: Ps. cxlviii. 19, 20.
He has showed his Word unto Jacob, his Statutes and Judgments unto Israel;
He has not dealt so with any Nation, as for his Judgments they have not known
them: Praise ye the LORD. And indeed our Obligations to Gratitude, and
Thankfulness, are so much the greater, by how much the Light of the Gospel has
shined more full, and clear, upon us, in the more abundant Discoveries of the
Person, Nature, Offices, and Benefits, of the Messiah, and in the more evident
Testimony, and Assurances, of Life and Immortality, than it did upon them; and
GOD has been graciously pleased to speak plainly unto us, whereas he spoke very
much in Parables, Types, and Shadows unto them.

O how great is his Goodness! That thus the Blessing of Abraham should come
upon us Gentiles, and unto us, now, pertains the Adoption, and the Glory, and
the Covenant, and the giving the Law, and the Service of GOD, and the Promises;
that now unto us is this Grace given, that, among us Gentiles, the unsearchable
Riches of CHRIST are preached; to the intent, that now unto Principalities, and
Powers, in heavenly Places, might be known, by the Church, the manifold Wisdom,
and Goodness, of GOD: to use the Language of the inspired Apostle Gal. iii. 14.
Romans ix. 4. Ephesians. iii. 8, 10.
.

2. Is the Commandment of GOD exceeding broad? then we may, from hence, learn
the indispensable Obligation we are under to keep it; that we ought always to
keep, and do, all that the Lord our GOD has commanded us: that we ought to be
obedient, universally, and forever obedient.

Particularly,

(1.) From hence we learn our Obligation to keep the Commandments of GOD. The
divine Original, the excellent Nature, and the blessed Design of the
Commandment plainly, and strongly, infers this.

1. Our Obligation to a due Respect to the divine Commandment is plainly
inserrable from the divine Original of it. For, if the GOD that made us, and
all the World, and to whom we must finally be accountable, has made known his
Mind and Will to us, and showed us what He requires of us, it is very certain,
that then we are under all possible Ties, and Engagements, to remember and do
as he has commanded us. Since it is the Commandment of GOD, and derives from
the eternal Deity, we ought to give a suitable Entertainment to it, and believe
all that he has made known to us, as Articles of our Faith, and obey all that
is required of us, as Matter of our Practice.

Thus, we learn, from the divine Original of the Commandment, that we ought
firmly to believe it: because every Word, which GOD has spoken, is a faithful
Saying, and worthy of all Acceptance by us. For GOD is not a Man, that He
should lie Number. xxiii. 19.
; yea, it is impossible for GOD to lie Heb. vi. 18.
; for the Lord is a GOD of Truth, Just, and Right, is He Deuteronomy. xxxii. 4.
When therefore it can be said to us, thus says He that is holy, He that is
true, there is no Room for us to hesitate whether we ought to believe what is
spoken, or no. Our own Reason tells us, that infallible Truth ought to be
believed; and we cannot possibly withhold our Assent from what we know to be
infallibly true, without putting a Force upon ourselves, and doing Violence to
our own Understanding. It is not to be wondered at, that they, who are
possessed with the firm Persuasion of an infallible Chair, upon Earth, should
swallow the grossest Absurdities, when they are dictated from that Chair, by an
implicit Faith; but the greatest Wonder is, that any Men should have so little
Reason, as to imagine, that Infallibility is to be found in a fallible
Creature. But that GOD is infallible, is most evident to our Reason, because he
is infinite in Understanding, and therefore cannot possibly be imposed upon;
and infinitely pure, and Good, and therefore cannot deceive any, by giving them
a false Account of Persons, or Things; There are no natural, or moral,
Imperfections in GOD, to render His Word suspicious, precarious, and fallible;
and hence it plainly follows, that whatever he makes known to us, is infallibly
true, and therefore to be credited, by us, purely upon His Word, whether we are
able to understand all that is contained in what He has spoken, or no. For the
Supreme Being, who has furnished us with Understanding, never meant to give us
the Power to arraign his Veracity before the Bar of our Reason, nor may we
assume it to ourselves to fit in Judgment upon the Truth of what he has said;
he has given us Reason, indeed, to judge of the Clearness, and Strength, of the
Evidences that are brought in Proof of a divine Revelation, or whether what is
pretended to have been spoken by GOD be really so, or no: and thus we are not,
presently, to believe every Spirit, and bold Pretender that may come to us, as
he says, in the Name of GOD, but are commanded to try the Spirits whether they
are of GOD; 1. Joh. iv. 1.
to search and prove their Credentials, whether they bring with them plain and
full Evidences of their being sent from GOD; and, if, upon Examination, it be
found that their Credentials are authentic and valid, and sufficient to
determine our reasonable Minds, that GOD thereby speaks to us, it is not for us
then to proceed to try and judge, whether what GOD has thereby spoken be true,
or no, before we will give credit to it; no; GOD demands it of us to believe
what he has said, upon the Truth of his Word, and not upon our Capacity of
discerning the Truth of it, or upon it is Agreement with such Maxims, and
Principles, as we have taken up with, or such Ideas, and Conceptions of Things
as we have formed in our Minds.

All the Difficulty here will lie in the Evidence, and Assurance, that what we
are to believe is truly a divine Revelation; and if the Evidences of a Thing's
being a Revelation from GOD are full, and strong, there ought then to be no
Difficulty with us in our crediting of it; because Truth itself can never
deceive. It is readily acknowledged, that there are Mysteries in Religion,
though some, I know, would persuade us there are none. I do not mean that the
Proposition, in which the divine Revelation is expressed, is mysterious, for
then, I suppose, we could not know the Terms of the Proposition, and so, I
think, could not possibly believe it; because it would contain just Nothing at
all in it, nothing to us, whatever it might do to those that understand the
Terms of it; but it would be, to us, as a sealed Book, which we could neither
read, know, or believe, any thing contained in it. But I mean, that, though the
Proposition be ever so plain, and clear, and the Terms of it perfectly well
understood by us, and so it hands to us, a certain Truth, sufciently knowable,
yet, it contains in it such Doctrines as are, in the Nature of them, mysterious
to us, and beyond our Understanding how such Things can be. When a Proposition
can be demonstrated to be true, (as what is proved to be from GOD certainly
is,) it ought to be of no Weight with us, nor give us any Uneasiness, that it
is impossible for us to comprehend, or frame any adequate or complete Ideas, of
the Manner how the Things so demonstrated can be; or that there are such
perplexing Difficulties on the other side, which merely for want of adequate
Ideas of the Manner of the Existence of the Things demonstrated, are not easy
to be cleared. Vid. Dr. Sam. Clark, of the Being and Attributes etc. p. 10.
. And it is very wrong to reject, and disown, That for a divine Revelation,
(and it is a false Way of arguing to conclude, that there can be no Evidences of
it is being a divine Revelation,) because it contains such Doctrines in it as we
are not able to comprehend: for this would be for us to make our own Reason,
and Knowledge, and not the Truth of GOD, the Foundation of our Belief. And the
Absurdity, and Falseness, of this Way of Reasoning, however polite, and
conclusive, some Men may think it, will evidently appear, by applying it to the
most familiar Instances in Nature. It is a very plain Proposition, the Terms of
which are sufficiently understood by every Child of Ten Years old, That Five
burns. But can any Thing be more ridiculous, and absurd, than for any Man,
(and much more any Man pretending to a superior Genius, greater Learning, and
Philosophy, and a more masterly Way of thinking,) to deny the Truth of this
Proposition; merely because he knows not what Fire is, in the real Nature of
it, nor how it burns? A Philosopher may show some Smartness, indeed, and try
his Brother Philosopher's Powers, by disputing against this Proposition, there
is local Motion, which however plain, yet has it is Difficulties; but should any
one that sets up for a Philosopher, in sober Earnest, deny local Motion, and
for this Reason, because he could not reconcile it to some Difficulties that
occurred to him, he would only render himself justly ridiculous, and every
unlettered Person could show him his Folly, only by walking a few Steps. And is
it not an equal Degree of Weakness, and Folly, for any Man to deny a divine
Revelation, sufficiently confirmed, purely because he cannot understand the
Nature of the Thing revealed, though the Terms of the Proposition are plain,
and easy. Certainly, whatever GOD makes known is true, whether we understand
the Nature of it, or no; and because GOD has spoken it, therefore we are
obliged to believe it. So that the Divine Original of the Commandment obliges
us most firmly to believe all the Revelations, Doctrines, Promises, and
Threatenings, contained in it.

And so does it equally oblige us to obey the Precepts of it. For GOD is not
only true in what he says, but he is our Sovereign, and has an original,
underived Right, by Virtue of his being GOD, to enjoin us what Law he pleases,
and demand our Obedience to it. Therefore this is prefixed to the Epitome of
the divine Commandment, I am the Lord thy GOD Enod. xx. 2.
; which shows us the unquestionable Right GOD has, as he is GOD, and our GOD,
to command us, and the strong Obligation we are under to obey him; even such an
Obligation as it is not in the Power of GOD himself to dispense with, and free
us from the Bonds of. The Lord is our Maker; we are the Workmanship of his
Hands, and because he has made us, and not we ourselves, therefore he is our
rightful Sovereign, and cannot but be so, unless we can cease to be his
Creatures: He is Lawgiver, our King, and our Judge, whose Prerogative alone it
is to be obeyed, in whatsoever he commands us; for the Excellencies of his
Nature will not admit of any Injunction, but what is worthy of a GOD, and what
is best for his Creatures; and his Commands cannot possibly interfere with any
prior, and superior, Obligation we are under, because there is none prior,
none superior to him. Besides he is our constant Preserver, and bountiful
Benefactor, from whom we receive our All, and in whom all our Hopes are laid
up; So that Disobedience to any of his known Commands challenges his Right, and
Authority, over us, denies him his peculiar Honor, and slurs the Luster of all
his Perfections, renounces our Dependence on him, and disowns his Kindness to
us, and so is at once the highest Rebellion, and the blackest Ingratitude. But,
since he is GOD alone, he is jealous for the Honor of his Name, and will not
suffer any of his Glory to be taken from him, especially this natural Homage,
Obedience to his Commands. And think thou this, O Man! thou that live at
Defiance with GOD, thy Maker, in thy known Disobedience, and Contempt of his
Authority, by doing what he has forbidden to thee, or by neglecting to do what
he has required of these, think thou, that thou shall escape the righteous
Judgments of GOD? Verily, whatever the Sinner may imagine, the Time will come,
when GOD will cause his Jealousy to burn like Fire, and manifest his
Indignation in flaming Rebukes, upon every wilfully Disobedient Soul, without a
Possibility of their escaping.

2. The excellent Nature of the divine Commandment infers our Obedience. The
more excellent the Rule of our Conduct is the more it deserves our Regards: for
we ought ever to act as reasonable Creatures, and walk by the best Rules. But
what is there so excellent, for the Rule of our Behavior, as the Divine Law
is? How admirably is it adjusted to the Honor of the Lawgiver, and to
ourselves, our Nature, Capacity, and Interest? It Is the only perfect Rule of
Rectitude, and Purity. The Words of the Lord are pure Words, as Silver tried in
the Furnace, purified seven Times Ps. xii. 6.
. That is, it is wrought up to the highest Degrees of Excellency; so that there
wants nothing to complete it is Perfection, and recommend it to our Acceptance:
and needs must it be so, because it is the Result of infinite Wisdom. Thus it
is a most perfect Rule to us, and we need never to fear our mistaking of our
Way while we closely observe it. Beauty charms the Eye, and Harmony captivates
the Ear, and we are not wont to act so unreasonably as not to give the
Preference to what we know to be most excellent in its Kind. And what is there
that can be more agreeable to the Sentiments of our rational Minds, than to
govern ourselves, in all our Conduct, by that Rule which is best, which is
true, certain, determinate, and safest for us? which can never lead us out of
the Way, and in our Conformity unto which, only, we act wisely, in doing what
is best for us, and safely, in doing what we ought to do, both in our personal,
and relative Capacity, whether in The Family, State, or Church? So that because
the Divine Commandment is most excellent in itself, it ought to be embraced by
us, and observed as the Rule of our Walk; and we cannot, knowingly, act
contrary thereto, without doing Violence to right Reason, and exposing
ourselves to our own just and severe Reproaches, by refusing to practice what,
we are forced to own, is a most excellent Law. But this Argument will appear
more fully under the next Head.

3. The End and Design of the divine Commandment infers Obedience: whether we
consider it, as it respects Society, or our Selves in particular.

For, if we consider the divine Commandment as it respects our Society, and
Relation, to one another, so it is the just Rule, and Measure, of our Conduct,
and Behavior toward our FellowCreatures; it shows us how we may be truly
serviceable in the World, and promote the public Good, and Welfare, by the
Practice of these, and those Virtues, which will render us obliging,
beneficent, and helpful, to all about us; and by carefully avoiding such Vices,
and Irregularities, in our Temper, and Behavior, as would render us hurtful,
and injurious, to one another. Thus it sweetens our Tempers, improves, and
betters, our Manners, and lays it is Restraints upon our unruly Lusts and
Passions, and prevents the dismal Effects of their unbridled Rage, and puts us
upon the Exercise of universal Benevolence, and Goodness, and so makes us
profitable Members of the Body Politic, Ornaments in the Church, and Delights
in the Family. Now, certainly, a Law, so admirably calculated for the general
Service of Mankind, ought to be obeyed. For without something of this, there
would be no quiet, and peaceable, living in the World; but every Man would turn
a Beast of Prey upon his Neighbor, and the World would presently wear the Face
of the wildest Anarchy, and Confusion. It Is the want of a due Regard to the
divine Commandment which renders the World so bad as it is, at present: this
introduces Tyranny, and Oppression, among the higher Orders of Men; Mutiny,
Sedition, and Rebellion, among Inferiors; Injustice, Rapine, Cruelty, Hatred,
Strife, Revenge, and the like, among Equals. And whilst the great Props of the
World, Righteousness, and Truth, so much fail from among the Children of Men,
it is no Wonder to hear Men complain of the Badness of the Times, and the
Difficulty of living; and, believe it, there is nothing, the Wit of Man can
invent, that will ever correct, and mend, the Times, without a more
conscientious Observation of the divine Commandment: the Thought of which
alone, one would be ready to suppose, should have it is due Influence upon us
all, to move us, to take more Heed to our Ways, and govern ourselves according
to the Word of GOD, that excellent Rule of all our Actions.

But then, if we consider the divine Commandment, as it more particularly
relates to Ourselves, we shall see how indispensibly we are obliged to obey it.

For, as ever we would be freed from the domineering Power of those Lusts, and
Passions, of Concupiscence, Covetousness, Pride, Anger, Wrath, Malice, Revenge,
and such like, which fret, and disturb, our Minds, and give us the greatest
Uneasiness; as ever we would have our vicious, and unreasonable Prejudices,
against what is truly good, and profitable to us, removed, and have our
Understandings brightened, our manifold Disorders cured, and would possess
ourselves, with Calmness, and Serenity, certainly we are concerned to be very
careful to keep the Commandments of our GOD; because nothing, without this,
will give us the Mastery over what is prejudicial to us, and afford us inward
Satisfaction. And let but the covetous Worldling, the impure Sensualist, and
the raging Madman, think a little seriously, how much the Prevalency of those
Lusts, and Passions, over him, is truly a Burden to him, and lays the
Foundation of most, if not all, the Sorrows he meets with, what unaccountable
Pains, and Difficulties, he is at to gratify them, what unknown Struggles to
screen, and defend them, what perplexing, and sometimes inextricable, Broils
they entangle him in, and, at the same Time, how much it debases him below the
Dignity of his Nature, hurries him into unmanly Actions, and not seldom brings
very grievous Hurt, and Damage, upon his Person, and worldly Interest; I say,
let him but seriously consider these things, and he will plainly see, that it
is richly worth his while to endeavor to rid himself of such troublesome
Companions, such baneful Inmates, by a close Adherence to the divine
Commandment, which will render him Master of himself, and pleased with his own
Actions.

Nay; as ever we would entertain any well grounded Hope of eternal Happiness,
we are indispensibly obliged to Obedience. For, though our Obedience to the
Divine Commandment is, by no Means, meritorious of future Happiness, yet it is
the sure Way to it; the Way which the unerring Wisdom, and spotless Purity, of
the Divine. Nature have marked out for us; and a Man may as reasonably hope, to
support, his animal Life, without Food, as think to obtain true Happiness,
which is the Life of the Soul, without Obedience; Nay, more: for the Life of
the Body is not so necessarily dependent upon Food, but that GOD can support it
without any; but GOD Himself cannot make a Soul happy, without Holiness;
because this would imply a Contradiction to the Divine Nature, and to our own.
Hither looks all the Grace of the Gospel, as well as all the positive Commands
of the divine Oracles, and JESUS CHRIST is the Author of eternal Salvation unto
them, and them only, that obey Him Heb. v. 9.
. And who, in his Wits, would not think an eternal State of complete Happiness
worth his striving for? That Man, must first divest himself of his very Nature,
who has no Desires after Happiness; and he must cease to think rationally, who
can imagine he may be happy, without being obedient. Thus you see, that, since
the Divine Commandment is exceeding broad, it necessarily infers our Obedience
to it, and you see also how strong our Obligations to Obedience are.

(2). As it infers Obedience, in the general, so does it particularly, with
Respect to each, and every one of the divine Commands: that our Obedience be
universal, and without Exception. For, they are all the same, in the Dignity of
their Original, the Excellency of their Nature, and the same noble End and
Design is pursued by them all. The same Authority that enacted one Command, has
enacted all; they all bear the evident Impress of the supreme Lord of all upon
them; and therefore are all to be obeyed by us. If we urge upon you the
Practice of any Duty, which GOD has not required of you, regard us not.
Examine, with the noble Bereans Act. xvii. 11.
, whether the things we preach to you, for divine Commands, are agreeable to the
Mind and Will of GOD, or no; and if they are not, reject them; but if we
publish to you nothing more than what GOD demands of you, then you ought to pay
a due Regard thereunto, and do accordingly, and that, not because we tell you,
This is your Duty, but, because the Lord your GOD requires it at your Hands.

It is very possible, indeed, that we may not be able to see into the Reason of
all the divine Commands, though we may of many of them; yet this is no
sufficient Objection against our Obedience to them, when we know they are the
Commands of GOD, any more than it is a sufficient Objection in a Servant,
against his complying with the Commands of his Master, that he knows not to
what End and Purpose his Master has given him such a Command. A Master may,
perhaps, command a thing, which yet may be very unworthy of himself, and
unfitting for his Servant to comply with; because he is liable to Mistakes in
his Judgment, or may be influenced by the Strength of his Passions in what he
commands; and then that Servant may very reasonably be allowed modestly to
expostulate the Case with his Master, and finally refuse to obey his Master, in
that thing which is contrary to the Commands of a superior Power, to whom he is
under Obligation to obey. But the infinitely wise, and good GOD cannot possibly
be guilty of any such Error, as to command any thing unworthy of Himself, or
unfitting for us to do, and has sufficient, and good Reasons, for every one of
his Commands, though we are not able to see them: So that it is enough for us
to know that it is the Command of GOD; our Business is to resign our Wills
entirely into the divine Will. For, though we know not why He has commanded
such a thing, yet we know why we ought to obey that Command, namely, because
God has commanded it. Judge. iv. 6.
Has not the Lord GOD of Israel commanded thee? is sufficient to silence all
Cavils, and put us upon the most ready Obedience. Nor is this to make GOD an
arbitrary Being, as some Men count Arbitrariness. Though Arbitrariness is of an
ill Sound, when it is applied unto Men, who are liable to Mistakes, and are
accountable to a superior Power, and therefore have no Right to set up their
Wills as the Rules of their own, much less of others Actions; yet, rightly
understood, when it is applied unto God, it is no other than his acting His own
Pleasure Isa. xlvi. 10.
, and His performing all things according to the Counsel of his own Will, Ephesians.
i. 11.
without being accountable unto us, or any of his Creatures, for the Reason of
his Actions, or Designs: and this the Perfection, and absolute Supremacy of the
divine Nature challenges as his indisputable, and unalienable Right: and thus
GOD is arbitrary, and it is his peculiar Glory that He is so; that is, it is
the Greatness, and Glory, of the divine Being, and what none but GOD can
challenge, that his Will alone, without Dependence on, or Accountableness to,
any other Being, or any Thing out of Himself, gives Law unto all Creatures: His
Will, I say, which, from the Perfection of his Nature, is above all Possibility
of being erroneous, or biassed with Prejudices, and ill Affections, and
therefore cannot possibly be subject to Caprice, and Humor, as the Will of a
finite, and fallible Being may. And sure I am, that it is an Argument of the
greatest Arrogance, and of an Arbitrary Temper, in the worst Sense, for any Man
to assume to himself a Power that does not, in the least, belong to him, and
set up his own Will in Opposition to the divine, and determine with himself, to
obey none of the divine Commands, until GOD is pleased, first, to be
accountable unto him for the Reasonableness of them; or if, forsooth, he is not
able to discern that there is good Reason for the Command, that then he will
have nothing to do with it. For what is this but to set himself up in the
Throne of GOD, and to bring the Almighty to his Bar. My Soul, come not thou
into their Secret, unto their Assembly, mine Honor, be not thou united! The
infinitely Great GOD is the sole Disposer of his own Actions, and has an
absolute, uncontrollable, Sovereignty over all His Creatures, and therefore has
a Right to be obeyed by them, in whatsoever he commands them. For, I suppose,
and, doubtless, it will be readily granted, that GOD, who is infinite in Power,
and Wisdom, and Goodness, has a Right to do whatsoever is consistent with
himself; and that GOD perfectly knows what is consistent with himself, though we
do not; and from hence, I conclude, he never will, or can, do, or order to be
done, any thing, but what is consistent with himself: and from hence, it
follows, that there is no Room for us to hesitate in our Obedience to any
thing, we know to be the Command of GOD, though we should be perfectly ignorant
of the Design, or Reasonableness of the Command, until we can be guilty of the
Vanity, and Blasphemy, to think ourselves wiser than GOD, and that we know,
what is consistent with himself, better than he does himself. So that, whatever
GOD has required of us, it is our Duty to perform without disputing the
Legality, or Reasonableness of it; His Will being the highest Law and Reason of
all our Actions. For, though there may be what is called the Fitness, or
Unfitness, of Things, arising from their Relation, Proportion, and Dependence,
which are of excellent Use in Philosophy, without Revelation; yet to us who
enjoy a divine Revelation, these can be no false Rule for us to go by in our
Conduct, nor be the formal Obligation of our Obedience to the divine Law:
because, as a great Man observes, Dr. S. Clark, Them. of the Being etc. p. 183.
What these eternal and unalterable, Relations, Respects, or Proportions, of
things, with their consequent Agreements, or Disagreements, Fitnesses or
Unfitnesles, absolutely and necessarily are in themselves; That also they
appear to be, to the Understandings of all Intelligent Beings; except those
only, who understand Things to be what they are not, that is, whose
Understandings are either very imperfect, or very much depraved: Where, though
doubtless that learned Person designed to evidence that the Fitness, or
Unfitness, of Things, is the formal Obligation of our Obedience, and Rule of
our Behavior, yet, I humbly conceive, that, by his Exception, he truly evinces
the contrary: For, alas, the Exception, which he makes, is the very Case of all
Mankind, since the Fall, whatever it be of Angels, namely, that their
Understandings are very imperfect, and very much depraved. That the Mind of
Man, since the Fall, is very imperfect is evident, from the little real
Knowledge any attain unto after all their diligent Study and Search, and the
much less Knowledge the Bulk of Mankind can attain to, for want of Leisure, if
not of Capacity; and from the different Sentiments, which different Persons,
(though as far as we can judge, of equally clear Perception, and
Understanding,) have of one and the same thing, in many Instances; and from the
said Author, who asserts, p. 223.
that what is for the good of the whole Creation, in very many Cases, none but
an infinite Understanding can possibly judge; and from the sacred Scripture,
which assures us, that naturally Men have their Understandings darkened Ephesians.
iv. 18.
. So that, from the evident Imperfection of our Understandings, we are not able
clearly to discern, in many Cases at least, the absolute and necessary
Relation, and Fitness or Unfitness of things, in themselves, and therefore can
by no Means, with Safety, make it the Rule of our Conduct. And besides this
Imperfection, there is evidently a very considerable Depravity upon our
Understandings, which is seen in their being biassed and bribed, by Passions,
and Prejudices, swaying the Minds of those that seem to be most free from them;
and the same Author acknowledges, p. 254.
a great and general Corruption and Depravation. Hence though we may be able to
discern the Fitness or Unfitness of Things, in many Instances, yet, since, from
our Imperfection and Depravity, in many other we do not; and in some we cannot,
therefore the Will of GOD, the supreme Lawgiver, which Will is always wise and
good, is the only sure and certain Rule, to us, to regulate our Actions by; and
consequently the Will of GOD, made known to us, is the highest Law and Reason
of our Conduct, and not our own Conception of the Fitness or Unfitness of
Things. And our not being able to discern the Fitness, or Unfitness, of Things,
can be no sufficient Reason why any Man should refuse to observe that Law, or
believe that Truth, which GOD has clearly revealed to us. For since, said that
learned Author, p. 184.
the natural Attributes of GOD, his infinite Knowledge, Wisdom and Power, sets
him infinitely above all Possibility of being deceived by Error, or of being
influenced by wrong Affections; it is manifest his divine Will cannot but always
and necessarily determine itself to choose to do what in the whole is
absolutely Best and Fittest to be done; therefore his divine Will which
necessarily orders what is most fitting for us to do, is, to us, the best Rule
by which to Judge of the Fitness, or Unfitness, of Things, and the strongest
formal Obligation upon us to Obedience; and consequently our Obedience must be
universal and extend to every Command, that has the Authority of GOD stamped
upon it, whether we see the Reason of it, or no.

We may not therefore think to excuse ourselves with a partial Obedience, or in
obeying such Commands only as are suitable to our particular Temper, and
Interest in the World, or which we can see the Reason of; nor may we hope to
enjoy the Benefit of the exceeding broad Commandment, unless our Obedience
extend to every particular Duty required of us: that is, unless we sincerely
endeavor after universal Obedience to every divine Command. The Commandment is
all of a Piece, and therefore called, the Commandment, in the singular Number.
We must sincerely endeavor after an Obedience as extensive as the Commandment
is, or it will be no true Obedience, in the Sight of GOD. Hence is that of the
Apostle James, Jam. ii. 10.
Whosoever shall keep the whole Law, and yet offend in one Point, is guilty of
all. He is guilty of denying the Authority of the supreme Lawgiver, and guilty
of breaking the Unity of the Commandment; and from the same Principle, by which
he allows himself in Disobedience to any Part of the Law, he would also
transgress the whole, under equal Temptations, and Opportunities. It must
therefore be our great Care, as ever we would be esteemed obedient Subjects, to
comply with the just Expectation of GOD, and his earnest Desire, of an
universal Obedience. O that there were such an Heart in them! (says he,) that
they would fear me, and keep all my Commandments, always, that it might go well
with them, and their Children, forever Deuteronomy. v. 29.
.

Thus, we must not content ourselves with being Legalists, by observing only
the moral Duties of the divine Commandment, without taking due Care to obey
evangelical Percepts; for the Young Man, in the Gospel, could say, Luke xviii.
21.
all these have I kept from my Youth up; and yet our Lord said to him, in the
next Verse, One Thing thou lackest.

And it will be but a vain Presumption in us, to think that we are truly
obedient to the Precepts of the Gospel, and call ourselves Christians, while
the Duties of the moral Law are neglected by us. Will thou know, O vain Man,
that Faith, without Works, is Dead Jam. ii. 20.
. Moral, and Positive, Natural, and Evangelical, Precepts, must all, in their
proper Place, be duly regarded by us; these ought ye to have done, and not to
leave the other undone Matthew. xxiii. 23.
: they must go Hand in Hand with us, and our Obedience, in our sincere Aim, and
Endeavors, must universally extend to them all and to every Article included
under them.

I will only add,

3. Lastly; Thus too it infers the Constancy, and Perpetuity, as well as the
Universality of our Obedience: that we persevere in our Obedience as long as we
live. For the divine Authority ever remains good, and GOD is our Sovereign,
in one Part of our Lives as well as in another, yea, as long as we have any
Being; and the Commandment remains the same excellent Commandment, to Day, that
it was Yesterday; and as that is not more holy, just, and good, at one Time,
than at an other, so neither is it less Obligatory upon us at any Time, but
always abides in full Force, and Virtue, and therefore ought always to be
obeyed by us; Every Day we live, and all the Day long, and as long as we live
in the World. So said the devout Psalmist, Psalm. cxix. 112.
I have inclined my Heart to perform thy Statutes, always, even unto the End.
We may not imagine, therefore, that there are any particular Seasons for
Obedience, and others in which we may lawfully interrupt our Obedience; for,
though there may be special Seasons for This, or That, particular Branch of our
Duty, and sometimes Lesser Duties must give place to Greater ones, according to
that of our Savior, Matthew. ix. 13.
I will have Mercy, and not Sacrifice, yet, with Respect unto the whole of the
divine Commandment, there is no Part of Time can be called, a special Season
for Obedience, because there is not, nor can there be, any Season for
Disobedience. GOD allows us no Part of our Lives to Sin in, though he allows
us, at proper Seasons, to call off our Minds, from those Duties which are more
toilsome, and burdensome, to us, unto those that are more easy, and pleasant;
but He demands of us a constant, persevering, Course of Duty, throughout the
whole of our State of Probation, and Trial, in this World; that we serve him in
Righteousness, and Holiness, all the Days of our Life Luke i. 75.
: that we patiently continue in the Way of well doing? Romans ii. 7.
: that we hold fast the Profession of our Faith, without Wavering Heb. x. 23.
: and that we be steadfast, unmovable, always abounding in the Work of the Lord;
forasmu^^ as we know that our Labor shall not be in vain in the Lord 1 Cor.
xv. 58.
. If this were well remembered, it would have a mighty Influence upon us, to
make us more exact, in our Obedience to the Commands of GOD, throughout the
whole Course of our Lives; and we should not so easily be prevailed upon, to
allow such wide Gaps in our Duty, as are often to be found among us.

SERMON VIII.
PSALM CXIX. 96. I have seen an End of all Perfection; but thy Commandment is
exceeding broad.


THE last Opportunity of discoursing upon this Subject, I entered upon the
Improvement of the second Doctrine from the Words, viz. The Commandment of GOD
is exceeding broad; and I inferred from it,

1. The wonderful Goodness, Mercy and Compassion of GOD to a miserable World,
in making a clear Revelation of his Mind and Will, in such important Affairs,
wherein our own Reason would not have been sufficient to have directed us, and
all with the blessed Design of recovering of us to Rectitude, and Happiness;
which special Advantage demands of us our grateful Tribute of Thankfulness, and
Praise.

I have also inferred,

2. The indispensible Obligations we lie under to keep the Commandment of GOD;
that is, to believe all that GOD has told us, and perform all that he requires
of us. It Is the Commandment of the GOD that made us, who is our supreme Ruler,
and to whom we must be accountable; it is a most excellent Commandment in
itself, and respecting Society, and particular Persons; and therefore as ever
we would act reasonably, possess the Peace of our own Minds, and be happy in
the Favor of our GOD, we are indispensibly obliged to obey it, and that every
Part thereof, as the Will of GOD concerning us, and be constant and persevering
in our Obedience to the End, without allowing any Interruptions therein.

And I now shall go on to a Third Inference from this Doctrine; viz.

3. This Doctrine teaches us, That Religion is our truest Wisdom. For what is
Religion, but our keeping the Commandments of GOD? Religion indeed includes in
it, that we believe that there is a GOD, and that we believe the Commandments,
as the Rule of our Duty, is from GOD, and that the Way, in which GOD has
signified to us that he is willing to be reconciled unto us, and admit us to
his Favor, namely, in and by his Son JESUS CHRIST, is the only Way of our
obtaining Mercy with him: but yet all our Faith in GOD, and in his Son JESUS
CHRIST, all our Fear of GOD, and Love to him, all terminates in this, as the
Sum of true Religion, and what includes all the Rest, that we readily obey this
GOD, in whatsoever he commands us; Therefore the Preacher said, Eccl. xii. 13.
Fear GOD, and keep his Commandments; for this is the whole of Man. His whole
Duty is included in this, and his whole Happiness is laid up in it. Since
therefore the Commandment of GOD is so exceeding broad, as to reach to us in
all our Capacities, and Relations, and Designs to better us, as rational
Creatures, to render our Lives comfortable to us here, and to make us
completely happy hereafter, then it must needs be the truest Wisdom in us, thus
to be religious. And, indeed, what Wisdom is there equal to this? Job. xxviii.
28.
Unto Man, he said, Behold, the Fear of the Lord, that is Wisdom, and to depart
from Evil is Understanding. Let a Man be ever so worldly wise, though he should
understand all the Secrets of Nature, and of Art, and be deeply read in the
most refined Politics, yet, without Religion, he has not the Wisdom, and
Understanding, of a Man; and his whole Life will be but an ill concerted
Design, which will come far short of his true End, and all his fine Schemes,
his Labor, and Toil, will be in vain, and to no god Purpose: when a Storm
gathers thick and dark about him, and the Waves of Adversity beat heavy upon
him, he will be destitute of every thing that can afford him any solid Comfort;
and when the gloomy Prospect of Death, and the Grave, appears, with all its
Terrors, before him, he will not be able to look, with Calmness, into the
future World, and comfort his Heart with the refreshing View of a State of
complete, and endless, Happiness reserved for him. For his inquisitive Search,
and clearest Discoveries, his closest Thought, and greatest Labor, have been
about those things which are of the least, and most temporary, Concernment to
him, while he has contented himself to remain a Stranger to that which is his
main Interest, and of everlasting Consequence unto him: the Folly of which is
apparently much greater than that, of him, who should spend all his Thoughts,
and Time, about catching of Butterflies, to the Neglect of the necessary
Provision for the Support of his Body. Whereas, he that is truly religious
takes a prudent Course to secure his main Interest, to enjoy the Favor of his
GOD, and possess everlasting Peace and Joy; and let the World frown upon him,
and all things about him be thrown into Confusion, and his whole Life, here, be
filled up with various Afflictions, and Sorrows, yet, in the midst of all, he
can look within himself with Calmness and Pleasure, at the Thought of his
having done his Duty; and can look forward with a joyful Prospect of an happy
Issue to all his Afflictions, secured to him in the Promise of that GOD, who is
faithful, and will do it: Nay, though he should be forced for the Sake of this
his main Interest, to suffer in lesser, and more trifling Matters; yet, so long
as his greatest Concerns are safe, he has evidently acted the Part of a Wise
Man, in making a lesser Interest stoop, and give Place, to the greater. So,
like the wise Merchant, having found one Pearl of great Price, he readily sells
all that he has, parts with things of lesser Value, and buys it Math. xiii. 45.
.

Besides, the Wisdom of Religion appears in this, that a Man does nothing
herein that he will afterward have any Reason to be ashamed, and repent of;
whereas he that leads an irreligious Life, in Disobedience to the Divine
Commandment, will certainly, as he has just Cause for it, be ashamed, and
heartily sorry for his Folly, sooner, or later: If he ever see his Error, while
he has Opportunity to correct it, his past Folly will cost him many an uneasy
Thought, and make him very restless; and his Repentance, though it be the best
thing he can possibly do, will be attended with inward Shame, and Regret, and
he will bitterly reflect upon himself, and most sadly condemn himself, as a
vile, wretched, loathsome Creature, who by his Rebellions against his
Sovereign, and Ingratitude to his best Friend, has deserved Hell a Thousand
Times over. But if he should go on in his Irreligion, until Death, and
Judgment, overtake him, how severely, then, will he reproach, and condemn
himself? What pointed Stings will pierce deep into his very Soul, at the
Reflection on his past Folly? What inexpressible Horror will take hold upon
him, at the Thought of his former mad Course of Life? How dreadfully will he
become his own Tormentor, and that throughout an endless Eternity? Whereas, he
that lives religiously, in Obedience to the divine Commands, is always doing
what he ought to do, what becomes him as a rational Creature, what greatly
improves and betters him, and therefore what will forever set easy and
comfortably about him, and what will afford him unspeakable Satisfaction in the
Review of it.

Nay; if the religious Man should have deluded himself, with the pleasing
Hopes, of living happily forever, in an other World, after he has acted his
Part in this, and, instead of his partaking of that Joy and Satisfaction he
lived in Expectation of, should, at last, die, and perish, like the Beast, yet
has he acted the wise Part: because he has denied himself of nothing that was
fitting for a wise Man to allow himself in, he has had the Pleasure, and
Satisfaction, as he went along, to carry himself regularly, and behave
decently, and to do nothing but what was worthy of him, as a Man; and all this
he did upon, at least, the probable, Hopes of a happy Eternity, as the full
Reward of all: and, if after all, he should miss of what he hoped for, by
ceasing to have any Being beyond the Grave, yet he will truly have lost
nothing, by his Religion, but what he could very well spare, without any real
Damage to himself, and he will then be in no Capacity to receive any
Uneasiness, at his Disappointment, or to feel any Degree of Misery. But he that
lives irreligiously truly gains nothing, by his Irreligion, but what he had
better be without, namely, an indecent, misbecoming, and unmanly Conduct, which
exposes him to the Censure, and Disesteem, of the thinking Part of Mankind, and
uneasy Reflections within himself, which he cannot, at Times, be without; and
all the Liberty he has taken to gratify the irregular Appetites of Flesh and
Sense, besides it is reducing him upon a Level with the Brute, has been with a
View to some probable Hope, (for no Man is, or can be sure of it,) that he
shall have no Being in an other World; which Hope if he should find himself, at
last, mistaken in, he would be unavoidably miserable, and that forever. So
that, upon Supposition, that the future State is only probable, and that there
were equal Reason to conclude, that it will, or will not, be, the religious Man
is, by far, the wiser of the two; because he has provided for that which
possibly may happen, and that with no real Disadvantage to himself in his
present State, while the irreligious has made no real Gain to himself, by a
Life of Disobedience, and is utterly unprovided for the fatal Chance, which,
for ought he can possibly know, may, at last, happen to him.

But then, whatever profane Men may think of it, there is no such Chance,
whether we shall have a Being in an other World; no, my Brethren, it is an
undoubted Certainty, founded upon solid Principles of Reason, and evidenced by
the clear Light of indisputable Revelation, that we shall exist after we leave
this World, that Death does not make a final and full End of us, but we pass,
from h^^^e, into an other World, where we shall have assigned unto us a Portion
answerable to our Conduct in this: and then who will be found to be the wise
Man? He that has aforehand been thoughtful about that State he is passing into,
and done all he can to render it a comfortable and happy State to him; or, he
that has cast off all Thoughts of Futurity, and has been doing all he can to
render it a State of endless Misery, and insupportable Torment to him? Verily,
when all things are duly considered, it will certainly be found, that Religion
is our truest Wisdom. Well then might Solomon, the wisest of Men, say, Prove.
xxviii. 7.
Whose keeps the Law is a wise Son; and, chapter xix. 8.
He that geteth Wisdom loves his own Soul, and be that keeps Understanding
shall find good.

4. We may from hence infer the very great Evil of wilfully making light of,
and contemning, the divine Commandment. Is the Commandment, a Revelation from
GOD, partaking of the Purity of his Nature, with the Stamp of his royal
Authority upon it? Is it exceeding broad, as it reaches to every one of us, and
every Part of us, includes our whole Duty, and consults our truest Interest, in
this World, and the next? What an high Crime, and misdemeanor, must it then be,
for any to make Light of it, and pour their Contempt upon it, as though it were
mean, and despicable, and not worthy to be treated with Decency, and good
Manners: What is this but to pour Contempt upon GOD himself, who speaks to us
in his Word? Surely the Oracles of the great GOD ought to be forever sacred
with us, and to be thought, and spoken, of, with the greatest Reverence. One
would be ready to think, that the Purity of its Morals, the Sublimity, and
Majesty, of its Sentiments, and the Nobleness, and Gravity, as well as
Familiarity, and Plainness, of its Diction, besides the Remembrance that Life,
or Death, turns upon our Regards to it, should secure it our greatest
Veneration, beyond that of any other Writings whatever; because no other
Writings, whatever, can pretend to come near the Sanctity, and Majesty, of the
sacred Scriptures; nor so nearly concern us, in our best, and lasting Interest.
And yet, as if it were not enough to live, and act, contrary to the Documents
of this sacred Word, are there not a Generation, (O how lofty are they in their
own Eyes!) who add to all their other Crimes the prodigious Guilt, of pleasing
themselves in breaking their scurrilous Jests upon the holy Writings, and
scruple not to turn the divine Oracles into Burlesque? What can be more
contrary to that Reverence and Esteem which is due to a Revelation from GOD,
than for Persons to account themselves witty in their profane Drollery upon it?
And yet, for ought all that the wittiest of them can say, it may possible be a
